# Nomenclature and Structure

## Peptide Sequence and Structure

### 3.2.S.1.2 Structure: Peptide Sequence and Structure

#### 3.2.S.1.2.1 Elucidation of Primary Structure

The active pharmaceutical ingredient (API) of Glucogen-XR is a recombinant glucapeptide (glucagon-like peptide-1 analog) produced via an engineered CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative (GHS-CHO-001). The primary structure consists of a single-chain polypeptide sequence modified for enhanced stability, extended half-life, and increased receptor affinity.

**Table 1: Primary Amino Acid Sequence of Glucogen-XR**

| Position | Amino Acid | Symbol | Rationale for Selection/Modification |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | Histidine | His (H) | Critical for GLP-1 receptor activation and binding pocket entry. |
| 2 | $\alpha$-aminoisobutyric acid | Aib | **Substitution (Ala2Aib):** Confers resistance to Dipeptidyl Peptidase-IV (DPP-IV) cleavage. |
| 3 | Glutamic Acid | Glu (E) | Maintains helical propensity and electrostatic interactions. |
| 4 | Glycine | Gly (G) | Conserved residue for structural flexibility. |
| 5 | Threonine | Thr (T) | Hydrogen bonding residue. |
| 6 | Phenylalanine | Phe (F) | Hydrophobic core interaction. |
| 7 | Threonine | Thr (T) | Solvent-exposed residue. |
| 8 | Serine | Ser (S) | Phosphorylation-mimetic and polarity. |
| 9 | Aspartic Acid | Asp (D) | Salt bridge formation with Lys26. |
| 10 | Tyrosine | Tyr (Y) | Essential for aromatic stacking within the receptor. |
| 11 | Serine | Ser (S) | Hydrophilic surface residue. |
| 12 | Serine | Ser (S) | Hydrophilic surface residue. |
| 13 | Tyrosine | Tyr (Y) | Secondary hydrophobic contact point. |
| 14 | Leucine | Leu (L) | Hydrophobic stabilization. |
| 15 | Aspartic Acid | Asp (D) | Cation-pi interaction stabilization. |
| 16 | Glycine | Gly (G) | Structural hinge region. |
| 17 | Glutamine | Gln (Q) | Polarity and solubility. |
| 18 | Alanine | Ala (A) | Helical stabilization. |
| 19 | Alanine | Ala (A) | Helical stabilization. |
| 20 | Lysine | Lys (K) | **Functionalized:** Attachment site for C18 diacid fatty acid chain via $\gamma$-Glu-OEG-OEG spacer. |
| 21 | Glutamic Acid | Glu (E) | Negative charge for solubility. |
| 22 | Phenylalanine | Phe (F) | Hydrophobic residue. |
| 23 | Isoleucine | Ile (I) | Hydrophobic residue. |
| 24 | Alanine | Ala (A) | Helical stabilization. |
| 25 | Tryptophan | Trp (W) | Critical for anchoring in the receptor extracellular domain (ECD). |
| 26 | Leucine | Leu (L) | Hydrophobic interaction. |
| 27 | Valine | Val (V) | Hydrophobic interaction. |
| 28 | Arginine | Arg (R) | Solubilizing residue. |
| 29 | Glycine | Gly (G) | C-terminal flexibility. |
| 30 | Arginine | Arg (R) | Solubilizing residue and proteolytic protection. |
| 31 | Glycine | Gly (G) | C-terminal cap. |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.2 Detailed Chemical Modification (Acylation)

Glucogen-XR incorporates a prolonged-release mechanism via site-specific acylation at Lys20. This modification facilitates reversible binding to human serum albumin (HSA), thereby extending the terminal half-life to approximately 165 hours in humans.

**Component Analysis of the Side Chain:**
1.  **Fatty Acid Moiety:** Octadecanedioic acid (C18 diacid). The distal carboxyl group increases albumin affinity and enhances solubility at physiological pH.
2.  **Spacer 1:** Bis-aminodiethoxyacetyl (OEG-OEG). Two units of 8-amino-3,6-dioxaoctanoic acid provide a flexible link, ensuring the fatty acid does not sterically hinder receptor binding.
3.  **Spacer 2:** $\gamma$-L-Glutamic acid ($\gamma$-Glu). This linker provides an additional negative charge to further improve solubility and minimize aggregation tendencies.

**Molecular Formula:** $C_{187}H_{291}N_{45}O_{59}$
**Calculated Monoisotopic Mass:** 4111.0821 Da
**Average Molecular Weight:** 4113.64 Da

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.3 Physical and Chemical Characterization Data (Batch Analysis)

The primary structure and post-translational/synthetic modifications were confirmed using high-resolution mass spectrometry (HRMS) and peptide mapping on three pivotal clinical batches.

**Table 2: Comparative Structure Confirmation of Glucogen-XR Batches**

| Parameter | Specification | GLUC-2025-001 | GLUC-2025-002 | GLUC-2025-003 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Intact Mass (MS)** | 4113.64 ± 0.5 Da | 4113.62 Da | 4113.65 Da | 4113.63 Da |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | $\ge 98.0\%$ | 99.4% | 99.2% | 99.5% |
| **Deamidation (Asn/Gln)** | $\le 1.0\%$ | 0.2% | 0.3% | 0.2% |
| **Oxidation (Met)** | $\le 0.5\%$ | 0.1% | 0.1% | <0.05% |
| **Acylation Degree** | $1.0 \pm 0.05$ mol/mol | 1.01 | 0.99 | 1.00 |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.4 Secondary and Tertiary Structure Elucidation

##### 3.2.S.1.2.4.1 Circular Dichroism (CD) Spectroscopy
Far-UV CD spectra (190–260 nm) were recorded to determine the $\alpha$-helical content. Glucogen-XR exhibits a characteristic double minimum at 208 nm and 222 nm, indicative of a predominant $\alpha$-helical conformation in the presence of 30% trifluoroethanol (TFE) or membrane-mimetic environments (DPC micelles).

**Calculated Secondary Structure Content (Mean Residue Ellipticity):**
*   **$\alpha$-Helix:** $48.2\% \pm 2.5\%$
*   **$\beta$-Sheet:** $12.4\% \pm 1.2\%$
*   **Random Coil:** $39.4\% \pm 1.8\%$

##### 3.2.S.1.2.4.2 Nuclear Magnetic Resonance (NMR) Studies
2D-NMR ($^1H-^{15}N$ HSQC) spectroscopy of $^{15}N$-labeled Glucogen-XR was performed at pH 7.4. The dispersion of amide resonances confirms a well-defined fold in the C-terminal region (residues 15–31), while the N-terminus (residues 1–10) remains relatively flexible, consistent with the "two-domain" binding model of GLP-1 receptor agonists.

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.5 Protocol for Primary Sequence Confirmation (Tryptic Mapping)

**Protocol ID: GHS-ANA-TP-088**
**Objective:** To verify the amino acid sequence and site of acylation via LC-MS/MS.

1.  **Sample Preparation:** Dissolve 1.0 mg of Glucogen-XR in 1 mL of 50 mM ammonium bicarbonate buffer (pH 8.2).
2.  **Reduction/Alkylation:** Not required due to absence of Cysteine residues.
3.  **Digestion:** Add sequencing-grade Trypsin (Promega) at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio. Incubate at $37^\circ C$ for 16 hours.
4.  **Quenching:** Add 10 $\mu L$ of 10% Trifluoroacetic acid (TFA) to terminate enzymatic activity.
5.  **LC-MS Analysis:**
    *   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC BEH C18, 1.7 $\mu m$, 2.1 x 150 mm.
    *   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% Formic acid in Water.
    *   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.1% Formic acid in Acetonitrile.
    *   **Gradient:** 5% to 65% B over 45 minutes.
    *   **Detection:** Thermo Orbitrap Exploris 480 (Resolution: 120,000 at m/z 200).
6.  **Data Processing:** Alignment of observed fragment ions ($b$ and $y$ series) against the theoretical sequence using BioPharma Finder™ 4.1 software.

**Table 3: Predicted vs. Observed Tryptic Fragments**

| Fragment ID | Sequence | Theoretical Mass (m/z) | Observed Mass (m/z) | Error (ppm) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T1 | $H-(Aib)-EGTFTSDYS...K(Acyl)$ | 3122.45 | 3122.46 | 3.2 |
| T2 | $E FIAWLVR$ | 991.56 | 991.55 | -1.0 |
| T3 | $GR$ | 231.14 | 231.14 | 0.0 |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.6 Determination of Specific Rotation and Molar Extinction Coefficient

The molar extinction coefficient ($\epsilon$) was determined experimentally using amino acid analysis (AAA) as the reference standard.

**Calculation:**
$\epsilon_{280} = (n_W \times 5500) + (n_Y \times 1490) + (n_C \times 125)$
Where:
*   $n_W$ (Trp) = 1
*   $n_Y$ (Tyr) = 2
*   $n_C$ (Cys) = 0

$\epsilon_{280} = (1 \times 5500) + (2 \times 1490) = 8480 \, M^{-1} \cdot cm^{-1}$

**Experimental Value:** $8495 \pm 45 \, M^{-1} \cdot cm^{-1}$ (validated via GLUC-2025-001).

---

The structural characterization of Glucogen-XR was performed in accordance with:
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **USP <1047>:** Gene Therapy Products (where applicable for cell line lineage).
*   **USP <121.1>:** Physico-chemical Analytical Procedures for Peptides.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** "Index of Quality for Therapeutic Peptides."

This comprehensive structural analysis confirms that the primary, secondary, and tertiary structures of Glucogen-XR are consistent across production batches and meet the predefined criteria for identity, purity, and potency required for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapeutic intervention.

## PEG Modification Details

### 3.2.S.1.2 Nomenclature and Structure: PEG Modification Details

The drug substance, Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), utilizes a sophisticated site-specific conjugation strategy involving a branched 40 kDa Polyethylene Glycol (PEG) moiety. This modification is critical for extending the biological half-life of the glucapeptide through a combination of increased hydrodynamic radius (reducing glomerular filtration) and shielding from proteolytic degradation by dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) and neutral endopeptidases (NEP).

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.1 Rational Design of the PEGylated Conjugate
The selection of the 40 kDa branched PEG (mPEG2-NHS) was based on extensive pharmacokinetic (PK) modeling conducted during the Phase I/II optimization trials.

**Table 1: Physico-chemical Characteristics of the PEG Reagent**
| Parameter | Specification | Typical Result (Batch PEG-2025-004) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Total Molecular Weight ($M_n$)** | 38,000 – 42,000 Da | 40,120 Da |
| **Polydispersity Index (PDI)** | $\le$ 1.05 | 1.02 |
| **Active NHS Content** | $\ge$ 95% molar ratio | 98.4% |
| **Di-diol Content** | $\le$ 2.0% | 0.8% |
| **Branching Efficiency** | $\ge$ 98% | 99.1% |
| **Heavy Metals (as Pb)** | $\le$ 5 ppm | < 1 ppm |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.2 Site-Specific Conjugation Chemistry
Glucogen-XR is synthesized via an $N$-terminal-specific reductive alkylation or an amine-reactive acylation at a specifically engineered Lysine residue (Lys$^{26}$). To ensure a homogenous product (mono-PEGylated species), the reaction environment is strictly controlled for pH, temperature, and molar excess of the PEG reagent.

##### 3.2.S.1.2.2.1 Reaction Stoichiometry and Optimization
The conjugation reaction is defined by the following equilibrium and rate equations:
$$ \text{Protein-NH}_2 + \text{PEG-NHS} \xrightarrow{k_1} \text{Protein-NH-CO-PEG} + \text{NHS} $$
$$ \text{PEG-NHS} + \text{H}_2\text{O} \xrightarrow{k_2} \text{PEG-COOH} + \text{NHS} $$

To maximize the yield of the mono-PEGylated Glucogen-XR, the ratio $k_1/k_2$ is optimized by maintaining the pH at 8.2 $\pm$ 0.1 at 4°C.

**Table 2: Process Parameters for Conjugation (Batch GLUC-2025-001 through 005)**
| Parameter | Setpoint | Range | Validation Reference |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Peptide Concentration | 5.0 mg/mL | 4.5 – 5.5 mg/mL | GHS-VAL-2025-09 |
| PEG:Peptide Molar Ratio | 1.5 : 1.0 | 1.4:1 to 1.6:1 | GHS-VAL-2025-10 |
| Reaction pH | 8.2 | 8.1 – 8.3 | GHS-SOP-550 |
| Reaction Temperature | 4.0 °C | 2.0 – 6.0 °C | GHS-SOP-550 |
| Reaction Time | 180 min | 170 – 190 min | GHS-VAL-2025-11 |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.3 Detailed Conjugation Protocol (GHS-PROC-772)

**Step 1: Reagent Preparation**
1. Thaw the purified Glucogen-XR intermediate (Batch: GLUC-2025-INT-01) from -80°C storage.
2. Equilibrate to 4°C using a jacketed stainless steel vessel (Asset ID: GHS-RX-99).
3. Verify protein concentration via $A_{280}$ (Extinction Coefficient: $1.45 \text{ L}\cdot\text{g}^{-1}\cdot\text{cm}^{-1}$).

**Step 2: Buffer Exchange and pH Adjustment**
1. Utilize a TFF (Tangential Flow Filtration) system with a 5 kDa MWCO Pelicon 3 membrane.
2. Exchange into 50 mM Sodium Borate, pH 8.2.
3. Monitor conductivity ($\le 4.5 \text{ mS/cm}$).

**Step 3: PEG Activation and Addition**
1. Weigh 40 kDa mPEG2-NHS (Lot: PEG-2025-004) in a low-humidity glove box (< 10% RH).
2. Dissolve in 1 mM HCl to prevent premature hydrolysis.
3. Add the PEG solution to the protein vessel at a controlled flow rate of 100 mL/min using a Masterflex peristaltic pump.

**Step 4: Quenching**
1. After 180 minutes, quench the reaction by adding 1.0 M Glycine to a final concentration of 50 mM.
2. This converts unreacted PEG-NHS to PEG-Glycine, preventing over-PEGylation during downstream processing.

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.4 Characterization of the PEG Linkage

##### 3.2.S.1.2.4.1 Hydrodynamic Radius Determination
The effective size of the PEGylated peptide is significantly larger than its primary sequence suggests. This is measured via Dynamic Light Scattering (DLS) and Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC) with Multi-Angle Light Scattering (MALS).

**Table 3: Comparative Hydrodynamic Data**
| Species | Theoretical MW | Apparent MW (SEC-MALS) | $R_h$ (Hydrodynamic Radius) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Native Glucapeptide | 4,200 Da | 4,198 Da | 1.2 nm |
| **Glucogen-XR** | **~44,200 Da** | **48,500 $\pm$ 500 Da** | **6.4 nm** |

*Note: The apparent MW in SEC-MALS is higher due to the high solvation volume of the PEG chains.*

##### 3.2.S.1.2.4.2 Mass Spectrometry (MALDI-TOF)
Because PEG is polydisperse, MS analysis yields a "hump" distribution. The center of the distribution for Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-001) was confirmed at $m/z$ 44,212, consistent with the sum of the peptide mass (4112 Da) and the PEG mass (40,100 Da).

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.5 Stability of the PEG-Peptide Bond
The amide bond formed between the Lys$^{26}$ $\epsilon$-amino group and the PEG carboxylic acid is highly stable. Accelerated stability studies (ICH Q1A(R2)) were performed at 25°C/60% RH and 40°C/75% RH.

**Table 4: PEG Stability Data (Batch GLUC-2025-001)**
| Time Point | Condition | % Mono-PEGylated (HPLC) | % Free Peptide | % High MW Aggregates |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T=0 | 5°C | 99.2% | < 0.1% | 0.8% |
| T=6 Months | 5°C | 99.1% | < 0.1% | 0.9% |
| T=6 Months | 25°C | 98.4% | 0.4% | 1.2% |
| T=1 Month | 40°C | 95.2% | 1.8% | 3.0% |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.6 Impurity Profile: PEG-Related Substances
Impurities stemming from the PEGylation process are strictly monitored:
1. **Unreacted Peptide:** Removed via Cation Exchange Chromatography (CEX).
2. **Multi-PEGylated Species (Di-PEG):** Controlled by PEG:Peptide ratio; removed via Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC).
3. **Free PEG:** Removed via Ultrafiltration/Diafiltration (UF/DF).

**Table 5: Impurity Specifications and Batch Analysis**
| Impurity | Limit | GLUC-2025-001 | GLUC-2025-002 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Di-PEGylated | $\le$ 1.5% | 0.4% | 0.5% |
| Free Peptide | $\le$ 0.5% | ND | ND |
| Free PEG (unconjugated) | $\le$ 2.0% | 0.6% | 0.7% |
| NHS (residual) | $\le$ 10 ppm | < 1 ppm | < 1 ppm |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.7 Analytical Methodology: Determination of PEGylation Site
To confirm that PEGylation occurs exclusively at Lys$^{26}$, Trypsin/Asp-N digestion followed by LC-MS/MS peptide mapping is performed (GHS-MTH-102).

**Calculation of Occupancy:**
The occupancy of the PEGylation site is calculated using the following formula:
$$ \text{Occupancy (\%)} = \left( 1 - \frac{A_{\text{unmodified peptide}}}{A_{\text{total peptide}}} \right) \times 100 $$
*Where $A$ represents the peak area of the specific peptide fragment containing Lys$^{26}$.*

For all clinical batches (GLUC-2025-XXX), site-specific occupancy exceeded 99.5%, with no detectable $N$-terminal modification observed under the optimized pH 8.2 conditions.

---

#### 3.2.S.1.2.8 Regulatory Compliance
The PEGylation process and the PEG reagent itself comply with the following:
*   **USP <788>:** Particulate Matter in Injections.
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **FDA Guidance:** "Nonclinical Studies for the Safety Evaluation of Pharmaceutical Excipients" (regarding PEG toxicity).

[END OF SECTION 3.2.S.1.2]

## International Nonproprietary Name (INN)

### **3.2.S.1 GENERAL INFORMATION**
### **3.2.S.1.1 Nomenclature**

---

#### **I. International Nonproprietary Name (INN) and Detailed Designation Protocols**

The designation of the International Nonproprietary Name (INN) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) follows the rigorous framework established by the World Health Organization (WHO) Program on International Nonproprietary Names for Pharmaceutical Substances. This section details the nomenclature strategy, the linguistic and structural derivation of the name, and the alignment with global regulatory standards including the FDA’s United States Adopted Names (USAN) Council and the European Pharmacopoeia (Ph. Eur.) naming conventions.

---

#### **1.1.1 Formal Statement of INN Status**

The International Nonproprietary Name for the drug substance produced by Google Health Sciences is **glucapeptide**. This name has been formally assigned by the WHO INN Expert Group and is published in the WHO Drug Information (Proposed INN List 128, 2024).

**Table 1.1.1-1: Official Nomenclature Summary for Glucogen-XR**

| Feature | Description | Reference/Source |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **International Nonproprietary Name (INN)** | Glucapeptide | WHO Proposed List 128 |
| **US Adopted Name (USAN)** | Glucapeptide-gxrs | USAN Council / FDA 2024 |
| **Chemical Name (IUPAC)** | L-Glucagon-like peptide-1 (7-37)-2-aminoisobutyric acid-extended fusion protein with recombinant human albumin-mimetic linker | IUPAC Blue Book |
| **CAS Registry Number** | 2948210-44-3 | Chemical Abstracts Service |
| **UNII (Unique Ingredient Identifier)** | GH78-XR-9901 | FDA Global Substance Registration System (GSRS) |
| **Laboratory Code** | GHS-772-ER | Google Health Sciences R&D |
| **Anatomical Therapeutic Chemical (ATC) Code** | A10BJ07 | WHO Collaborating Centre for Drug Statistics |

---

#### **1.1.2 Linguistic and Pharmacological Derivation**

The name "glucapeptide" was selected to provide a clear, unambiguous identification of the active moiety while adhering to the specific stem requirements for GLP-1 receptor agonists.

##### **1.1.2.1 Stem Analysis**
Pursuant to the WHO "Guidance on the Use of Stems in the Selection of INNs for Pharmaceutical Substances" (WHO/EMP/RHT/PNN/2018.1), the name is constructed as follows:

1.  **-peptide**: The terminal suffix denotes the biochemical class (peptide).
2.  **-ca-**: The infixed syllable refers to the peptide's origin or mimicry of the glucagon-like architecture.
3.  **glu-**: The prefix denotes the glucose-regulatory pharmacological action.

The combined descriptor "glucapeptide" signifies a long-acting recombinant peptide derivative designed for glycemic control. Unlike traditional "-tide" suffixes used for synthetic peptides (e.g., liraglutide), the use of "-peptide" in this context highlights the extended biological fusion nature of the molecule produced via the GHS-CHO-001 cell line.

---

#### **1.1.3 Protocol for International Name Submission and Maintenance**

Google Health Sciences (GHS) adheres to a standardized internal protocol (GHS-REG-SOP-0045) for the management of nomenclature.

**Protocol GHS-REG-SOP-0045: Submission of INN Applications**

1.  **Initial Assessment (T-Minus 24 Months to Filing):**
    *   Review of existing INN lists to ensure no phonetic or orthographic conflicts.
    *   Evaluation of the molecule's mechanism of action (MOA) against existing WHO stems.
    *   *Calculation of Similarity Score:* Using the Levenshtein distance algorithm to ensure the proposed name has a distance >3 from existing high-volume pharmaceuticals.
2.  **Submission Phase:**
    *   Formulation of "Proposed INN" (pINN) application.
    *   Submission of molecular sequence (Fasta format) and disulfide bridge mapping to the WHO INN Secretariat.
    *   Submission of glycosylation profile (N-linked/O-linked) as it influences the naming suffix (e.g., use of Greek letters if required).
3.  **Objection Period:**
    *   A 4-month window for global stakeholders to object to the pINN based on trademark infringement or clinical confusion.
4.  **Finalization:**
    *   Transition from Proposed INN (pINN) to Recommended INN (rINN) upon publication in the WHO Drug Information journal.

---

To maintain traceability between the INN and the manufactured substance, Google Health Sciences utilizes a rigorous batch numbering system.

#### **1.1.5 Structural Rationale for the INN**

The INN "glucapeptide" encompasses the entirety of the recombinant construct produced in the CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative line.

**Molecular Formula:** $C_{742}H_{1168}N_{204}O_{224}S_{6}$ (Non-glycosylated peptide backbone)

**Molecular Weight Calculation (Theoretical vs. Observed):**
The theoretical mass of the glucapeptide moiety is calculated based on the sum of the average atomic masses of the constituent amino acids, adjusted for the formation of 3 intra-molecular disulfide bonds.

$$MW_{theoretical} = \sum (AA_{mass}) - (n_{disulfide} \times 2.016)$$

*   **Average Monoisotopic Mass:** 16,442.84 Da
*   **Observed Mass (ESI-MS, Batch GLUC-2025-001):** 16,442.88 ± 0.15 Da

The nomenclature specifically accounts for the N-terminal modification (2-aminoisobutyric acid) which confers resistance to Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-4) degradation, justifying the "XR" (Extended Release) designation in the trade name, although the INN itself remains "glucapeptide."

---

#### **1.1.6 Global Harmonization and Regulatory References**

The nomenclature of Glucogen-XR is designed to satisfy the requirements of multiple regulatory jurisdictions simultaneously.

1.  **United States (FDA/USAN):**
    The USAN Council has assigned the four-letter suffix "-gxrs" to the core INN, resulting in **glucapeptide-gxrs**. This complies with the FDA's "Nonproprietary Naming of Biological Products" Guidance for Industry (2017), ensuring that the biosimilar pathway remains distinct for future competitors.
2.  **European Union (EMA):**
    The EMA Committee for Medicinal Products for Human Use (CHMP) utilizes the rINN "glucapeptide" for the Summary of Product Characteristics (SmPC).
3.  **Japan (PMDA):**
    The Japanese Accepted Name (JAN) is identical to the INN, transliterated as グルカペプチド (Gurukapepuchido).

---

#### **1.1.7 Maintenance of Nomenclature Integrity**

Google Health Sciences employs a "Nomenclature Integrity Procedure" (NIP) to ensure that the INN is used consistently across all CMC (Chemistry, Manufacturing, and Controls) documentation, labeling, and clinical trial registrations.

**Step-by-Step Procedure for Labeling Verification:**
1.  **Input:** Draft labeling for Batch GLUC-2025-XXX.
2.  **Verification:** Automated scanning of the document for the string "glucapeptide".
3.  **Validation:** Cross-referencing against the USP Dictionary of USAN and International Drug Names.
4.  **Calculation of Variance:** Any deviations in spelling or suffix application are flagged. A variance of 0% is required for batch release.

---

#### **1.1.8 Statistical Analysis of Name Recognition (Safety Study)**

To prevent medication errors, a "Look-Alike/Sound-Alike" (LASA) analysis was conducted comparing "glucapeptide" to other GLP-1 RAs.

**Table 1.1.8-1: LASA Comparison Results**

| Candidate Name | Comparator | Orthographic Score (%) | Phonetic Score (%) | Risk Mitigation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Glucapeptide | Liraglutide | 42% | 38% | Low risk |
| Glucapeptide | Semaglutide | 35% | 31% | Low risk |
| Glucapeptide | Dulaglutide | 39% | 40% | Low risk |
| Glucapeptide | Glucagon | 68% | 72% | **Tall-man lettering required** |

*Note: Due to the phonetic similarity with 'Glucagon', GHS recommends the use of 'GLUCApeptide' in clinical settings to avoid hypoglycemic treatment errors.*

---

# General Properties

## Physicochemical Properties

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE (GLUCOGEN-XR)
### 3.2.S.1 GENERAL INFORMATION
#### 3.2.S.1.3 PHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES

This section provides a comprehensive characterization of the physicochemical properties of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a recombinant human glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1) analogue. The drug substance is produced by Google Health Sciences using a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout cell line (GHS-CHO-001) and is designed for extended-release therapeutic efficacy in the treatment of Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus.

---

### 1. PRIMARY STRUCTURE AND AMINO ACID SEQUENCE ANALYSIS

#### 1.1 Amino Acid Sequence Confirmation
The primary structure of Glucogen-XR was elucidated through a combination of N-terminal sequencing, C-terminal sequencing, and high-resolution Liquid Chromatography-Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) peptide mapping.

| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |

| Asparagine | Asn (N) | 2 | 228.20 | 3.0% |
| Aspartic Acid | Asp (D) | 3 | 345.27 | 4.5% |
| Cysteine | Cys (C) | 2 | 206.28 | 2.7% |
| Glutamine | Gln (Q) | 4 | 512.52 | 6.7% |
| Glutamic Acid | Glu (E) | 5 | 645.55 | 8.5% |
| Glycine | Gly (G) | 18 | 1026.90 | 13.5% |
| Histidine | His (H) | 1 | 137.14 | 1.8% |
| Isoleucine | Ile (I) | 2 | 226.32 | 3.0% |

| Phenylalanine | Phe (F) | 2 | 294.34 | 3.9% |

| Valine | Val (V) | 4 | 396.52 | 5.2% |
| **Total** | | **83** | **7887.82** | **100%** |

#### 1.2 Peptide Mapping (LC-MS/MS) Protocol
Peptide mapping was performed to ensure 100% sequence coverage and to identify any post-translational modifications (PTMs).

**Protocol GHS-ANA-PM-001: Tryptic Digestion and RP-HPLC-MS Analysis**
1. **Sample Preparation:** Dilute Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-001) to 2.0 mg/mL in 6M Guanidine-HCl, 50 mM Tris-HCl, pH 8.0.
2. **Reduction:** Add Dithiothreitol (DTT) to a final concentration of 10 mM. Incubate at 56°C for 45 minutes.
3. **Alkylation:** Add Iodoacetamide (IAM) to 25 mM. Incubate in the dark at room temperature for 30 minutes.
4. **Quenching:** Add excess DTT (10 mM) to neutralize residual IAM.
5. **Buffer Exchange:** Use Zeba™ Spin Desalting Columns (7K MWCO) to exchange into 50 mM Ammonium Bicarbonate, pH 7.8.
6. **Digestion:** Add Trypsin (Promega Gold) at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio. Incubate at 37°C for 16 hours.
7. **Acidification:** Terminate reaction with 1% Trifluoroacetic Acid (TFA).
8. **Analysis:** Inject 20 µL into an Agilent 1290 Infinity II UHPLC coupled to a Thermo Orbitrap Exploris 480 MS.

**Table 1.2-1: Tryptic Peptide Fragments Identified (Batch GLUC-2025-001)**
| Peptide Fragment | Sequence | Expected Mass (m/z) | Observed Mass (m/z) | Mass Error (ppm) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T1 | HAEGTFTSDVSSYLEGQAAK | 2112.984 | 2112.986 | 0.94 |
| T2 | EFIAWLVK | 975.564 | 975.563 | -1.02 |
| T3 | GRPSSGAPPPS | 1007.512 | 1007.515 | 2.98 |
| T4 (Extended) | [Extended Linker Domain] | 3791.760 | 3791.755 | -1.32 |

---

### 2. MOLECULAR WEIGHT AND MASS SPECTROMETRY

The intact molecular weight of Glucogen-XR was determined using Electrospray Ionization Time-of-Flight (ESI-TOF) mass spectrometry.

#### 2.1 Intact Mass Determination
Data were collected on three representative clinical batches to demonstrate consistency.

**Table 2.1-1: Intact Mass Analysis of Process Performance Qualification (PPQ) Batches**
| Batch Number | Date of Analysis | Theoretical Mass (Da) | Observed Mass (Da) | Deviation (ppm) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 12-JAN-2025 | 7887.82 | 7887.84 | 2.53 |
| GLUC-2025-002 | 15-JAN-2025 | 7887.82 | 7887.81 | -1.27 |
| GLUC-2025-003 | 18-JAN-2025 | 7887.82 | 7887.83 | 1.27 |

#### 2.2 Calculation of Extinction Coefficient
The molar extinction coefficient ($\epsilon$) at 280 nm was calculated based on the amino acid sequence using the Pace method:
$$\epsilon_{280} = (n_W \times 5500) + (n_Y \times 1490) + (n_{C-C} \times 125)$$
Where:
- $n_W$ (Tryptophan) = 1
- $n_Y$ (Tyrosine) = 1
- $n_{C-C}$ (Disulfide bonds) = 1

Calculation:
$$\epsilon_{280} = (1 \times 5500) + (1 \times 1490) + (1 \times 125) = 7115 \text{ M}^{-1}\text{cm}^{-1}$$
Experimentally derived $\epsilon_{280}$ (via amino acid analysis) was determined to be $7120 \pm 50 \text{ M}^{-1}\text{cm}^{-1}$.

---

### 3. SECONDARY AND TERTIARY STRUCTURE

#### 3.1 Circular Dichroism (CD) Spectroscopy
Far-UV CD (190–260 nm) was used to assess the secondary structural elements ($\alpha$-helix, $\beta$-sheet, random coil).

**Table 3.1-1: Secondary Structure Estimation (Mean Residue Ellipticity)**
| Structure Component | Percentage (%) | Method (Algorithm) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| $\alpha$-Helix | 42.5% | CONTIN/LL |
| $\beta$-Sheet | 12.1% | CONTIN/LL |
| Turns | 18.4% | CONTIN/LL |
| Disordered/Coil | 27.0% | CONTIN/LL |

#### 3.2 Intrinsic Fluorescence Spectroscopy
The tertiary folding of Glucogen-XR was monitored by observing the fluorescence emission of the single Tryptophan (Trp) residue.
- **Excitation Wavelength:** 280 nm
- **Emission Maximum ($\lambda_{max}$):** 338 nm (indicating Trp is partially buried in a hydrophobic pocket).
- **Batch GLUC-2025-001 Result:** $\lambda_{max} = 338.2$ nm.

SEC is used to monitor the monomeric purity and the presence of high molecular weight species (HMWS).

**Protocol GHS-ANA-SEC-004:**

2. **Mobile Phase:** 200 mM Potassium Phosphate, 250 mM KCl, pH 7.0.
3. **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
4. **Detection:** UV at 214 nm and 280 nm.

The isoelectric point (pI) of Glucogen-XR was determined to characterize its charge heterogeneity.

- **Theoretical pI:** 4.85
- **Experimental pI (Main Peak):** 4.92
- **Acidic Variants:** 12.4% (typically deamidation products)
- **Basic Variants:** 3.2% (typically C-terminal lysine variants)

### 6. THERMAL STABILITY AND DIFFERENTIAL SCANNING CALORIMETRY (DSC)

The thermal melting temperature ($T_m$) provides an index of the conformational stability of the peptide.

**Experimental Conditions:**
- **Instrument:** MicroCal PEAQ-DSC.
- **Scan Rate:** 60°C/hour.
- **Concentration:** 1.0 mg/mL in Formulation Buffer.

**Results:**
- **$T_{m1}$ (Unfolding Transition):** 64.8°C
- **Calorimetric Enthalpy ($\Delta H$):** 142 kcal/mol
- **Conclusion:** Glucogen-XR exhibits high thermal stability in the proposed clinical formulation (pH 6.5).

## Stability Characteristics

### 3.2.S.1.3 General Properties: Stability Characteristics
**Drug Substance:** Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences
**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-M3DS-004-STAB
**Date:** 24 October 2024
**Status:** Final - Regulatory Submission Ready

---

#### 1.0 Introduction and Scope
This subsection provides a comprehensive characterization of the stability profile of Glucogen-XR drug substance (DS). Glucogen-XR is a synthetic, long-acting GLP-1 receptor agonist peptide engineered for extended-release properties via a proprietary acylation and amino acid substitution matrix. 

Stability characteristics have been evaluated in accordance with **ICH Q1A(R2)** (*Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products*), **ICH Q5C** (*Quality of Biotechnological Products: Stability Testing of Biotechnological/Biological Products*), and **ICH Q1E** (*Evaluation of Stability Data*). The primary objective is to define the degradation pathways, determine the molecular integrity under various environmental stressors, and establish the retest period and storage conditions.

#### 2.0 Molecular Sensitivity and Degradation Pathways
Glucogen-XR is susceptible to several chemical and physical degradation pathways typical of large acylated peptides. Google Health Sciences (GHS) has identified the following primary degradation mechanisms:

##### 2.1 Chemical Degradation
1.  **Deamidation:** Occurs primarily at Asparagine (Asn) residues at positions 16 and 28. This results in the formation of aspartic acid and isoaspartic acid derivatives.
2.  **Oxidation:** The Methionine (Met) residue at position 8 is highly sensitive to oxidative stress, leading to methionine sulfoxide formation.
3.  **C-terminal Hydrolysis:** Cleavage of the peptide bond under acidic or basic conditions.
4.  **Beta-Elimination:** Possible degradation of disulfide-like bridges if present (though Glucogen-XR uses a non-reducible linker).

##### 2.2 Physical Degradation
1.  **Aggregation:** Formation of soluble and insoluble covalent/non-covalent dimers, trimers, and higher-order polymers.
2.  **Fibrillation:** As a GLP-1 analog, Glucogen-XR can undergo transition from alpha-helix to beta-sheet structures under high agitation or thermal stress.
3.  **Adsorption:** High hydrophobicity of the C-18 fatty acid side chain leads to potential adsorption to hydrophobic surfaces (e.g., stainless steel, certain plastics).

---

#### 3.0 Forced Degradation (Stress Testing) Protocols
Stress testing was performed on Batch **GLUC-2025-001** to identify the degradation products and validate the stability-indicating power of the analytical methods (RP-HPLC, SEC-HPLC, and LC-MS).

##### 3.1 Protocol for Thermal Stress
*   **Procedure:** DS samples (10 mg/mL in phosphate buffer, pH 7.4) were incubated at 40°C ± 2°C and 60°C ± 2°C for 21 days.
*   **Sampling Intervals:** Days 0, 3, 7, 14, 21.
*   **Analysis:** Purity by RP-HPLC, High Molecular Weight Species (HMWS) by SEC.

##### 3.2 Protocol for Photostability (ICH Q1B)
*   **Procedure:** Samples exposed to a total illumination of not less than 1.2 million lux hours and an integrated near ultraviolet energy of not less than 200 watt hours/square meter.
*   **Control:** Dark control wrapped in aluminum foil.
*   **Equipment:** Atlas Suntest CPS+ Xenon Test Chamber.

##### 3.3 Protocol for pH Stress
*   **Acidic Stress:** Adjusted to pH 2.0 using 0.1M HCl; incubated at 25°C for 24 hours.
*   **Basic Stress:** Adjusted to pH 10.0 using 0.1M NaOH; incubated at 25°C for 24 hours.
*   **Neutralization:** Samples neutralized to pH 7.4 prior to chromatographic analysis.

---

#### 4.0 Summary of Stability Data (Real-Time and Accelerated)
The following tables summarize the stability data for three primary registration batches produced at the South San Francisco facility.

**Table 1: Stability Batch Identification**
| Batch Number | Scale | Manufacturing Date | Site | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |

---

#### 5.0 Detailed Analytical Procedures for Stability Monitoring

##### 5.1 Reversed-Phase HPLC (RP-HPLC) for Purity and Degradants
The primary method for determining chemical purity and identifying deamidated and oxidized species.
*   **Column:** Waters XBridge C18, 3.5 µm, 4.6 x 150 mm.
*   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% TFA in Water.
*   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.1% TFA in Acetonitrile.
*   **Gradient:** 25% B to 45% B over 40 minutes.
*   **Detection:** UV at 214 nm and 280 nm.
*   **Flow Rate:** 1.0 mL/min.

##### 5.2 Size-Exclusion Chromatography (SEC-HPLC) for Aggregation
Used to quantify High Molecular Weight Species (HMWS) and low molecular weight fragments.
*   **Column:** TSKgel G2000SWxl.
*   **Mobile Phase:** 200 mM Sodium Phosphate, pH 7.0.
*   **Isocratic Flow:** 0.5 mL/min.
*   **Calculation of HMWS:**
    $$ \%HMWS = \left( \frac{Area_{aggregates}}{Area_{total}} \right) \times 100 $$

---

#### 6.0 Statistical Evaluation and Retest Period
In accordance with **ICH Q1E**, a statistical analysis of the purity data was performed using the Google Cloud Life Sciences AI-Stats Engine (v4.2). 

##### 6.1 Regression Analysis
The 95% confidence interval for the mean degradation curve was calculated. For the long-term storage condition (-20°C), the slope of purity decline was determined to be non-significant ($p > 0.05$).

##### 6.2 Proposed Retest Period
Based on the available 12-month real-time data and supported by accelerated data, a **retest period of 24 months** is proposed for Glucogen-XR drug substance when stored in the proposed packaging (double LDPE bags inside a HDPE drum) at -20°C ± 5°C.

---

#### 7.0 Shipping and Excursion Stability
To support global logistics, "Temperature Excursion Studies" were conducted on batch **GLUC-2025-003**.

**Protocol GLUC-STAB-EXC-01:**
1.  **Freeze-Thaw cycles:** 3 cycles from -20°C to 25°C.
2.  **Short-term Thermal Excursion:** Exposure to 30°C for 72 hours (simulating a "broken cold chain" event).
3.  **Mechanical Stress:** 24 hours of orbital shaking at 200 RPM to simulate transport vibrations.

**Results of Excursion Study:**
*   **Purity:** Remained > 99.0% after 3 freeze-thaw cycles.
*   **HMWS:** Increased from 0.12% to 0.16% after 72h at 30°C (well within spec).
*   **Conclusion:** Glucogen-XR DS is robust against minor shipping temperature fluctuations.

---

#### 8.0 References
1.  **ICH Q1A(R2):** Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.
2.  **USP <1225>:** Validation of Compendial Procedures.
3.  **GHS SOP-QA-098:** Management of Stability Programs for Biologics.
4.  **Google Cloud LS Whitepaper:** *In-silico prediction of peptide aggregation kinetics in GLP-1 analogs.*

*End of Subsection*

## Solubility and pKa

### 3.2.S.1.3 General Properties: Solubility and pKa

This section provides a comprehensive characterization of the solubility profile and acid-dissociation constants (pKa) of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a novel GLP-1 receptor agonist recombinant peptide. These physicochemical properties are critical for understanding the drug substance’s behavior during downstream processing, formulation development, and its pharmacokinetic performance upon subcutaneous administration.

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.1 Introduction to Solubility and Ionization
Glucogen-XR is a 31-amino acid synthetic peptide analog derived from human glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1), modified with a C-16 fatty acid chain (palmitoylation) and an extended-release linker technology. Due to its amphiphilic nature—possessing both a highly charged peptide backbone and a hydrophobic lipid moiety—the solubility of Glucogen-XR is highly dependent on pH, ionic strength, and temperature.

The pKa values of the ionizable side chains govern the net charge of the molecule, which in turn dictates the solubility minima (isoelectric point) and the propensity for self-association/aggregation.

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.2 Solubility Profile

##### 3.2.S.1.3.2.1 pH-Dependent Solubility (pH-Solubility Profile)
The solubility of Glucogen-XR was evaluated across a physiological and processing range of pH 1.2 to pH 10.0 using a standardized shake-flask method followed by High-Performance Liquid Chromatography (HPLC) quantification.

**Protocol GLUC-SOP-088: Determination of Equilibrium Solubility**
1. **Apparatus:** Thermostated orbital shaker (Innova 44R), Eppendorf Centrifuge 5424R.
2. **Buffer Preparation:**
    *   pH 1.2: 0.1 N HCl
    *   pH 3.0 - 5.5: 50 mM Citrate/Phosphate Buffer
    *   pH 6.0 - 7.5: 50 mM Phosphate Buffer
    *   pH 8.0 - 10.0: 50 mM Glycine/NaOH Buffer
3. **Procedure:** An excess amount of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (Batch: GLUC-2025-001) was added to 2.0 mL of each buffer in triplicates.
4. **Equilibration:** Samples were agitated at 250 RPM at 25°C ± 0.5°C for 72 hours to ensure equilibrium.
5. **Separation:** Samples were centrifuged at 15,000 x g for 20 minutes to remove undissolved solids.
6. **Analysis:** The supernatant was filtered through a 0.22 µm PVDF membrane and analyzed via RP-HPLC (Method MET-GLUC-004).

**Table 1: pH-Dependent Solubility Results for Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-001)**

| Medium | pH (Measured) | Solubility (mg/mL) | SD (n=3) | Physical State of Precipitate |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 0.1 N HCl | 1.21 | 12.45 | 0.45 | Crystalline-like |
| Citrate Buffer | 3.02 | 1.12 | 0.12 | Amorphous/Gell-like |
| Citrate Buffer | 4.55 | 0.04 | 0.01 | Dense Aggregate (pI region) |
| Citrate Buffer | 5.48 | 0.18 | 0.03 | Flocculent |
| Phosphate Buffer | 6.81 | 18.90 | 1.10 | Clear Solution |
| Phosphate Buffer | 7.42 | > 100.0 | N/A | Clear Viscous Solution |
| Glycine Buffer | 9.05 | > 150.0 | N/A | Clear Viscous Solution |
| Glycine Buffer | 10.02 | > 150.0 | N/A | Clear Viscous Solution |

*Notes: The isoelectric point (pI) is approximately 4.8, where solubility is minimized.*

##### 3.2.S.1.3.2.2 Solubility in Pharmacopeial Media
To support Biopharmaceutics Classification System (BCS) alignment (noting that peptides often follow distinct pathways), solubility was assessed in USP-standard media.

**Table 2: Solubility in USP Media (37°C)**

| Media Type | Batch Number | Results (mg/mL) | ICH Compliance |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| SGF (Simulated Gastric Fluid, pH 1.2) | GLUC-2025-002 | 14.1 | USP <711> |
| SIF (Simulated Intestinal Fluid, pH 6.8) | GLUC-2025-002 | 22.4 | USP <711> |
| Water for Injection (WFI) | GLUC-2025-003 | 85.6 | USP Purified Water |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.3 Determination of pKa (Acid Dissociation Constants)

The pKa values of Glucogen-XR were determined using a combination of Potentiometric Titration and UV-Visible Spectroscopic Titration to account for the multiple ionizable groups (N-terminus, C-terminus, Lysine, Histidine, Glutamic Acid, Aspartic Acid, and Tyrosine).

##### 3.2.S.1.3.3.1 Potentiometric Titration Protocol
**Equipment:** Metrohm 905 Titrando with a combined glass electrode.
**Conditions:** 0.1 M KCl as supporting electrolyte; CO2-free environment (N2 blanket); Temperature 25°C.

**Procedure:**
1. 50 mg of Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-004) was dissolved in 40 mL of 0.01 M HCl.
2. The solution was titrated with 0.1 M KOH in increments of 0.05 mL.
3. The pH and potential (mV) were recorded after stabilization (dpH/dt < 0.002).
4. Data analysis was performed using the Gran plot method and non-linear regression analysis (Hyperquad2013).

##### 3.2.S.1.3.3.2 Spectrophotometric Determination (Tyrosine pKa)
Since Tyrosine exhibits a significant UV shift upon deprotonation (274 nm to 293 nm), UV-Vis spectroscopy was used to refine the pKa of the phenolic -OH.

**Table 3: Calculated vs. Experimental pKa Values for Glucogen-XR**

| Residue/Functional Group | Theoretical pKa (In Silico) | Experimental pKa (GLUC-2025-004) | Method |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| N-Terminus (His1) | 7.85 | 7.92 ± 0.05 | Potentiometric |
| Aspartic Acid (Asp9, Asp15) | 3.90 | 4.05 ± 0.12 | Potentiometric |
| Glutamic Acid (Glu21) | 4.30 | 4.41 ± 0.08 | Potentiometric |
| Histidine (His1 - Sidechain) | 6.00 | 6.15 ± 0.10 | Potentiometric |
| Lysine (Lys26, Lys34) | 10.50 | 10.35 ± 0.15 | Potentiometric |
| Tyrosine (Tyr19) | 10.10 | 10.05 ± 0.03 | UV-Spectroscopic |
| C-Terminus | 3.60 | 3.72 ± 0.09 | Potentiometric |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.4 Temperature and Solvent Effects on Solubility

##### 3.2.S.1.3.4.1 Thermodynamic Analysis (Van’t Hoff Plot)
The enthalpy of solution ($\Delta H_{sol}$) was calculated by measuring solubility at 5°C, 25°C, 37°C, and 45°C.

**Calculation Formula:**
$$\ln(S) = -\frac{\Delta H_{sol}}{R} \cdot \frac{1}{T} + \frac{\Delta S_{sol}}{R}$$

**Table 4: Solubility as a Function of Temperature (pH 7.4, Batch GLUC-2025-005)**

| Temperature (°C) | Temperature (1/K) | Solubility (mg/mL) | $\ln(S)$ |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 5 | 0.00359 | 42.1 | 3.74 |
| 25 | 0.00335 | 98.4 | 4.59 |
| 37 | 0.00322 | 145.2 | 4.98 |
| 45 | 0.00314 | 182.0 | 5.20 |

**Regression Results:**
*   **Slope:** -3245.2
*   **$\Delta H_{sol}$:** +26.98 kJ/mol (Endothermic process)
*   **Correlation Coefficient ($R^2$):** 0.9982

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.5 Effect of Cosolvents and Excipients
Given the extended-release formulation containing propylene glycol and phenol (as a preservative), solubility was evaluated in the presence of these components.

**Table 5: Solubility in Presence of Formulation Excipients (pH 7.4, 25°C)**

| Excipient Concentration | Batch | Solubility (mg/mL) | Effect |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 0% (Control) | GLUC-2025-006 | 98.4 | Baseline |
| 1.5% Propylene Glycol | GLUC-2025-006 | 105.2 | Slight Increase |
| 5.0% Propylene Glycol | GLUC-2025-006 | 122.8 | Significant Increase |
| 0.3% Phenol | GLUC-2025-006 | 88.5 | Slight Decrease (Salt formation) |
| 0.3% m-Cresol | GLUC-2025-006 | 82.1 | Hydrophobic interaction |

---

#### 3.2.S.1.3.6 Regulatory Compliance and References
The studies outlined in this section were conducted in accordance with:
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **USP <1236>:** Solubility Measurements.
3.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Characterization of Therapeutic Peptides.

All instruments used (HPLCs, Potentiometers) were qualified under Google Health Sciences Equipment Qualification Program (GHS-EQP-2024). Data integrity was maintained per 21 CFR Part 11.

*   For the impact of pH on drug product stability, see **Section 3.2.P.2 (Pharmaceutical Development)**.

# Biological Source

## CHO Cell Line Origin

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.2.3 CONTROL OF MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.2.3.1 BIOLOGICAL SOURCE AND STARTING MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: CHO CELL LINE ORIGIN AND HISTORY (GHS-CHO-001)

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection provides a comprehensive pedigree, derivation history, and genetic characterization of the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** mammalian host cell line utilized for the expression of **Glucogen-XR** (glucapeptide extended-release). In accordance with **ICH Q5A(R2)**, **ICH Q5B**, and **ICH Q5D**, this document outlines the transition from the ancestral progenitor lineage to the current cGMP-compliant Research Cell Bank (RCB) and Master Cell Bank (MCB).

Google Health Sciences (GHS) has leveraged advanced genomic engineering to optimize the Chinese Hamster Ovary (CHO) substrate for high-titer, extended-release peptide production, ensuring phenotypic stability and viral safety profiles suitable for long-term commercial supply.

---

#### 2.0 ANCESTRAL LINEAGE AND PEDIGREE
The GHS-CHO-001 cell line is a direct derivative of the CHO-K1 lineage, originally derived from the ovary of an adult female Chinese hamster (*Cricetulus griseus*) by T.T. Puck in 1957.

##### 2.1 Chronological Derivation Table
The following table details the evolutionary path from the primary isolation to the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 host.

| Era | Stage | Source/Institutional Origin | Key Modifications | Documentation Ref |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1957 | Primary Isolation | Eleanor Roosevelt Institute | Spontaneous immortalization | Puck et al. (1958) |
| 1970s | CHO-K1 Selection | ATCC (CCL-61) | Proline auxotrophy confirmation | ATCC-Cert-7721 |
| 1980s | CHO-DXB11 | Columbia University | DHFR deficiency (UV-induced) | Urlaub & Chasin |
| 2018 | GHS-CHO-Precursor | Google Health Sciences | Adaptation to chemically defined (CD) media | GHS-TR-2018-01 |
| 2022 | **GHS-CHO-001** | Google Health Sciences | **GS Knockout (CRISPR/Cas9)** | GHS-VAL-9902 |

##### 2.2 Host Cell Genotype (GS-/-)
The host cell line GHS-CHO-001 was engineered to be deficient in the endogenous Glutamine Synthetase (GS) gene. This allows for metabolic selection using the Methionine Sulfoximine (MSX) system or simple glutamine-free media selection, facilitating the stable integration of the Glucogen-XR expression vector.

**Table 1: Genetic Markers of GHS-CHO-001 Host**
| Marker | Status | Method of Verification | Expected Result |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| GLUL (GS) | Knockout | Southern Blot / NGS | Null (Frameshift at Exon 2) |
| DHFR | Wild Type | Phenotypic Growth | Growth in +/- Nucleosides |
| HPRT | Wild Type | Phenotypic Growth | Sensitivity to 6-TG |
| Proline | Auxotrophic | Growth Assay | Growth requires Proline |

---

#### 3.0 DETAILED CELL LINE ENGINEERING PROTOCOLS
The development of GHS-CHO-001 involved precision genome editing. The following procedures were executed under strict aseptic conditions at the Google Health Sciences R&D Facility (3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco).

##### 3.1 CRISPR/Cas9 Mediated GS Knockout Protocol
1.  **Vector Design:** Dual gRNA strategy targeting Exon 2 of the *Cricetulus griseus* Glutamine Synthetase gene (Gene ID: 100736566).
2.  **Nucleofection (Protocol ID: GHS-NUC-04):**
    *   Cell density: $2.0 \times 10^7$ cells/mL.
    *   Buffer: Lonza Nucleofector Solution V.
    *   Pulse Program: U-023.
3.  **Clonal Recovery:**
    *   Single-cell deposition into 96-well plates via Fluorescence-Activated Cell Sorting (FACS).
    *   Media: GHS-CD-01 (Chemically Defined) supplemented with 8mM L-Glutamine.
4.  **Screening:**
    *   Survivors were screened for the inability to grow in glutamine-free media (GHS-CD-01-NoGln).
    *   Clones exhibiting <1% viability after 96 hours in absence of glutamine were prioritized.

##### 3.2 Analysis of Indel Formation (Calculations)
To determine the efficiency of the knockout, the Total Mutation Efficiency ($TME$) was calculated using T7 Endonuclease I assays:
$$TME = 100 \times \left(1 - \sqrt{1 - \frac{f_1 + f_2}{f_{total}}}\right)$$
Where:
*   $f_1, f_2$ = Intensities of cleaved bands.
*   $f_{total}$ = Total intensity of all bands.
*   **Result for GHS-CHO-001 Precursor:** 38.4% efficiency, leading to the selection of Clone ID: **GHS-2022-GSKO-44**.

---

#### 4.0 MEDIA AND RAW MATERIAL TRACEABILITY
In compliance with **USP <1043>** (Cell, Gene, and Tissue-Engineered Products), all materials used in the derivation of the GHS-CHO-001 line are of non-animal origin (NAO) and Animal-Derived Component-Free (ADCF).

**Table 2: Media Components for Host Derivation (Batch: GLUC-2025-001A)**
| Component ID | Description | Supplier | Grade | TSE/BSE Risk |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| MED-CD-99 | GHS Proprietary CD Base | Google Life Sci | cGMP | None (Synthetic) |
| SUP-GL-04 | L-Glutamine (200mM) | Sigma-Aldrich | USP/EP | None (Fermentation) |
| SUP-PL-02 | L-Proline | Ajinomoto | USP | None (Fermentation) |
| DET-TR-01 | Recombinant Trypsin | ThermoFisher | Recombinant | None (E. coli) |

---

#### 5.0 CHARACTERIZATION OF THE GHS-CHO-001 HOST
Before the introduction of the Glucogen-XR expression plasmid, the GHS-CHO-001 host underwent extensive safety and phenotypic testing.

##### 5.1 Karyotypic Stability
Numerical and structural chromosomal analysis was performed on 50 metaphase spreads.
*   **Modal Chromosome Number:** 21 (Typical range: 19–23).
*   **Polyploidy Rate:** < 2%.
*   **Observation:** No evidence of gross chromosomal instability or large-scale translocations was observed between Passage 5 and Passage 50.

##### 5.2 Growth Kinetics and Metabolism
Baseline growth parameters were established in 3L bioreactor scales to ensure suitability for large-scale manufacturing.

**Table 3: Baseline Growth Parameters (n=3)**
| Parameter | Symbol | Value | Units |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| Specific Growth Rate | $\mu_{max}$ | 0.035 ± 0.002 | $h^{-1}$ |
| Doubling Time | $t_d$ | 19.8 ± 0.5 | Hours |
| Peak Viable Cell Density | $VCD_{max}$ | $18.5 \times 10^6$ | cells/mL |
| Specific Glucose Consumption | $q_{glc}$ | 1.25 | pmol/cell/day |
| Specific Lactate Production | $q_{lac}$ | 0.88 | pmol/cell/day |

---

#### 6.0 VIRAL AND ADVENTITIOUS AGENT SCREENING
The GHS-CHO-001 host was screened against a panel of adventitious agents in accordance with **ICH Q5A**.

**Table 4: Viral Safety Profile (Host Level)**
| Test Description | Method | Result | Reference |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| Sterility | USP <71> | Negative | GLUC-2025-LAB01 |
| Mycoplasma | USP <63> (Culture/DNA) | Not Detected | GLUC-2025-LAB02 |
| In Vitro Virus | 3-Cell Line Panel (Vero, MRC-5, CHO) | Negative | GLUC-2025-LAB03 |
| In Vivo Virus | Suckling Mouse/Egg Inoculation | Negative | GLUC-2025-LAB04 |
| CHO Retrovirus | TEM (Transmission Electron Micro.) | Type A & C present | Normal for CHO |
| Reverse Transcriptase | F-PERT Assay | < 10 fg/mL | Within Limit |

*Note: The presence of endogenous retrovirus-like particles (RVLPs) is documented and expected in all CHO derivatives. The downstream purification process for Glucogen-XR is validated for a log-reduction value (LRV) of >15 for model retroviruses.*

---

#### 7.0 ADAPTATION TO SUSPENSION AND SERUM-FREE CONDITIONS
The transition from adherent culture (ancestral) to chemically defined suspension culture (GHS-CHO-001) was performed over a period of 6 months using a stepwise weaning protocol.

1.  **Initial State:** Adherent CHO-K1 in DMEM/F12 + 10% FBS.
2.  **Phase I:** Transition to GHS-CD-01 + 5% FBS (3 passages).
3.  **Phase II:** Transition to GHS-CD-01 + 1% FBS (3 passages).
4.  **Phase III:** Serum-free GHS-CD-01 (10 passages).
5.  **Phase IV:** Adaptation to shake flask (125 rpm) agitation.

---

#### 8.0 CLONAL STABILITY AND REPRODUCTIBILITY
To ensure the long-term reliability of Glucogen-XR production, the GHS-CHO-001 line was subjected to an "End of Production" (EOP) simulation. Cells were carried to Passage 65 (well beyond the expected commercial limit of Passage 35).

**Stability Equation (Clonal Drift):**
$$D_{drift} = \frac{\sum (X_{P65} - X_{P5})}{X_{P5}} \times 100$$
Where $X$ represents the phenotypic marker (e.g., doubling time). For GHS-CHO-001, $D_{drift}$ was calculated at **3.1%**, which is well within the acceptable threshold of $\pm 15\%$.

---

#### 9.0 REGULATORY CONFORMANCE SUMMARY
The derivation and characterization of GHS-CHO-001 comply with:
*   **ICH Q5A(R2):** Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation.
*   **ICH Q5B:** Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of r-DNA Derived Protein Products.
*   **ICH Q5D:** Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **21 CFR Part 211:** Current Good Manufacturing Practice for Finished Pharmaceuticals.

The GHS-CHO-001 cell line is deemed a robust, safe, and genetically defined substrate for the production of Glucogen-XR. Detailed documentation regarding the subsequent transfection and MCB establishment follows in Section 3.2.S.2.3.2.

---
**END OF SECTION**
*Confidential Property of Google Health Sciences*
*Document Reference: GHS-GLUC-M3DS-CHO-V1.2*

## Master Cell Bank Characterization

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.2.3 CONTROL OF MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.2.3.2 BIOLOGICAL SOURCE AND CHARACTERIZATION
### SUBSECTION: MASTER CELL BANK (MCB) CHARACTERIZATION

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection provides a comprehensive characterization of the Master Cell Bank (MCB) for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**, designated as **MCB Batch No: GLUC-2025-MCB-01**. The MCB serves as the foundational starting material for the manufacture of the Glucogen-XR drug substance, a long-acting GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via recombinant DNA technology.

The characterization program was designed in accordance with **ICH Guideline Q5A(R2)** (Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation), **ICH Q5B** (Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products), and **ICH Q5D** (Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products). 

The MCB was derived from the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line (a CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative) engineered by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)**. The characterization ensures the identity, purity, stability, and safety of the cell bank for long-term clinical and commercial production.

---

#### 2.0 MCB IDENTIFICATION AND VIALING INFORMATION

**Table 1: Master Cell Bank (MCB) Summary Specifications**
| Parameter | Detail |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Product Name** | Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) |
| **MCB Batch Number** | GLUC-2025-MCB-01 |
| **Host Cell Line** | GHS-CHO-001 (CHO-K1 GS-/-) |
| **Expression Vector** | pGHS-GLP1-XR-v4.2 |
| **Manufacturer** | Google Health Sciences, 3000 Innovation Drive, SSF, CA |
| **Date of Cryopreservation** | 14-JAN-2025 |
| **Number of Vials Produced** | 450 Vials |
| **Vial Type** | 2.0 mL Sterile Polypropylene, Internally Threaded |
| **Cryopreservation Medium** | 45% CD-CHO, 45% Spent Media, 10% DMSO (USP Grade) |
| **Cell Density at Freezing** | $1.5 \times 10^7$ viable cells/mL |
| **Storage Temperature** | Vapor Phase Liquid Nitrogen ($\leq -150^\circ C$) |

---

#### 3.0 IDENTITY TESTING (ICH Q5D COMPLIANCE)

Identity was confirmed through phenotypic and genotypic methods to ensure no cross-contamination occurred during the bank establishment.

##### 3.1 Isoenzyme Analysis
Species identity was verified using an authentic CHO-K1 reference. The migration patterns of four key enzymes were analyzed: Glucose-6-Phosphate Dehydrogenase (G6PD), Lactate Dehydrogenase (LDH), Malate Dehydrogenase (MDH), and Nucleoside Phosphorylase (NP).

**Table 2: Isoenzyme Analysis Results (Report Ref: GHS-ANA-2025-088)**
| Enzyme Target | Result for GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | Reference Standard (CHO) | Conclusion |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| G6PD | Single Band (Rf 0.38) | Rf 0.38 | Consistent with CHO |
| LDH | 5-Band Pattern | 5-Band Pattern | Consistent with CHO |
| MDH | Single Band (Rf 0.42) | Rf 0.42 | Consistent with CHO |
| NP | Single Band (Rf 0.25) | Rf 0.25 | Consistent with CHO |

##### 3.2 COI Gene Sequencing (DNA Barcoding)
The Cytochrome c Oxidase I (COI) gene was amplified and sequenced. The 648 bp sequence was compared against the BOLD (Barcode of Life Data System) database.
*   **Result:** 100% homology to *Cricetulus griseus* (Chinese Hamster).
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Must match host species with >99% confidence.

---

#### 4.0 GENOTYPIC CHARACTERIZATION (ICH Q5B COMPLIANCE)

To ensure the genetic integrity of the Glucogen-XR expression cassette, the MCB underwent rigorous molecular analysis.

##### 4.1 Southern Blot Analysis (Copy Number and Integrity)
Genomic DNA (gDNA) was extracted from MCB cells using the GHS-SOP-GEN-04 protocol. Samples were digested with restriction enzymes *NheI* (non-cutter in cassette) and *EcoRI* (single cutter).

**Table 3: Southern Blot Densitometry Results**
| Digestion Enzyme | Predicted Band Size (kb) | Observed Band Size (kb) | Interpretation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| *NheI* | >15 kb | ~18 kb Single Band | High Molecular Weight Integration |
| *EcoRI* | 4.2 kb (Internal) | 4.2 kb | Intact expression cassette |

*   **Calculated Gene Copy Number:** $8.4 \pm 0.6$ copies per cell (determined via qPCR relative to the glucagon-like peptide standard curve).

##### 4.2 mRNA cDNA Sequencing
Total RNA was isolated from the MCB. cDNA was synthesized via RT-PCR using primers specific to the 5' UTR and 3' UTR of the Glucogen-XR transcript.
*   **Protocol:** GHS-MOL-772 (Dye Terminator Cycle Sequencing).
*   **Results:** The consensus sequence of the Glucogen-XR mRNA in the MCB is 100% identical to the intended amino acid sequence of the pGHS-GLP1-XR-v4.2 vector. No point mutations or truncations were detected.

---

#### 5.0 PURITY AND SAFETY TESTING (VIRAL AND ADVENTITIOUS AGENTS)

Safety testing was performed in compliance with **USP <1050>** and **ICH Q5A**.

##### 5.1 Sterility and Mycoplasma
The MCB was tested for the presence of aerobic/anaerobic bacteria, fungi, and mycoplasma.

**Table 4: Microbial Purity Testing**
| Test | Method | Results | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Sterility (Bacteria/Fungi) | USP <71> Membrane Filtration | No Growth (14 days) | No Growth |
| Mycoplasma (Culture) | USP <63> (Agar & Broth) | Negative | Negative |
| Mycoplasma (DNA Fluor.) | Hoechst Staining | Negative | Negative |
| Mycoplasma (PCR) | GHS-SOP-MIC-12 (NAT) | Negative | Negative |

##### 5.2 In Vitro Virus Assays
The MCB lysate and supernatant were inoculated onto a panel of indicator cell lines to detect a broad spectrum of adventitious viruses.

**Table 5: In Vitro Adventitious Agent Detection (14-Day Observation)**
| Cell Line | Observed Effect (CPE) | Hemadsorption | Hemagglutination |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| MRC-5 (Human Diploid) | None | Negative | Negative |
| Vero (Monkey Kidney) | None | Negative | Negative |
| CHO-K1 (Indicator) | None | Negative | Negative |

##### 5.3 In Vivo Viral Testing
Though CHO cells are generally considered low-risk, GHS performed in vivo testing on the MCB to satisfy global regulatory expectations (EMA/FDA).

**Table 6: In Vivo Safety Profile**
| Test System | Route of Inoculation | Duration | Observation | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Adult Mice | Intracerebral/Intraperitoneal | 21 Days | 100% Survival | Pass |
| Suckling Mice | Intraperitoneal | 14 Days | 100% Survival | Pass |
| Guinea Pigs | Intramuscular | 42 Days | No clinical signs | Pass |
| Embryonated Eggs | Allantoic/Yolk Sac | 10 Days | Normal development | Pass |

##### 5.4 Retrovirus Testing
As is typical for CHO-derived cell lines, Type A and Type C retrovirus-like particles (RVLPs) are expected. Quantitation was performed via Transmission Electron Microscopy (TEM).

*   **TEM Analysis Results:**
    *   **Intracellular Type A Particles:** Detected ($1.2 \times 10^3$ per cell section).
    *   **Extracellular Type C Particles:** Detected ($4.5 \times 10^4$ particles/mL supernatant).
*   **Reverse Transcriptase (RT) Assay:** Positive (as expected for CHO).
*   **Conclusion:** The presence of RVLPs is consistent with the CHO cell substrate. Viral clearance studies (Section 3.2.S.3.2) demonstrate the downstream process removes $\geq 18$ logs of retrovirus.

---

#### 6.0 CELL LINE STABILITY STUDY (CALCULATED TO END OF PRODUCTION)

Stability was evaluated by comparing the MCB to the Working Cell Bank (WCB) and the Limit of In Vitro Cell Age (LIVCA), representing the "End of Production" (EOP) cells.

**Table 7: Stability Matrix (MCB vs. EOP)**
| Parameter | MCB (Generation 0) | EOP (Generation 65) | Stability Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Viability post-thaw | 98.2% | 94.5% | Stable |
| Doubling Time ($t_d$) | 22.4 hours | 23.1 hours | Stable |
| Specific Productivity ($q_p$) | $45\text{ pg/cell/day}$ | $42\text{ pg/cell/day}$ | Within $\pm 10\%$ |
| Integrated Copy Number | 8.4 copies | 8.2 copies | Consistent |

**Stability Calculation Formula:**
The number of generations ($n$) from MCB to EOP is calculated as:
$$n = \frac{\log_{10}(N_{EOP}) - \log_{10}(N_{MCB})}{\log_{10}(2)}$$
Where $N$ is the total viable cell count. For Glucogen-XR, $n=65$ generations, providing a safety margin of 20 generations beyond the commercial 2,000L bioreactor process.

---

#### 7.0 QUANTITATIVE PCR (qPCR) FOR RODENT VIRUSES (HAP/MAP/RAP)
Specific qPCR panels were run to screen for Hamster, Mouse, and Rat pathogens.

**Table 8: qPCR Specific Pathogen Screen**
| Virus Target | Result | Detection Limit (LOD) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Hantavirus | Not Detected | <10 copies/rxn |
| Minute Virus of Mice (MVM) | Not Detected | <5 copies/rxn |
| Reovirus Type 3 (Reo3) | Not Detected | <10 copies/rxn |
| Pneumonia Virus of Mice (PVM) | Not Detected | <10 copies/rxn |
| Murine Adenovirus (MAV1/2) | Not Detected | <10 copies/rxn |

---

#### 8.0 CONCLUSION
The characterization of **MCB GLUC-2025-MCB-01** confirms that the cell bank is pure, sterile, and free of adventitious agents (other than expected endogenous retrovirus-like particles). The genetic identity and stability of the Glucogen-XR expression construct have been verified through Generation 65. This MCB is suitable for the production of clinical and commercial Glucogen-XR drug substance.

## Working Cell Bank Characterization

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S DRUG SUBSTANCE)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.2.3 CONTROL OF MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: BIOLOGICAL SOURCE – WORKING CELL BANK (WCB) CHARACTERIZATION

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This section details the comprehensive characterization of the Working Cell Bank (WCB) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), designated as Batch **GLUC-2025-WCB-01**. The WCB was derived from the Master Cell Bank (MCB) Batch **GLUC-2024-MCB-01**, which originated from the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line (a CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative). 

The characterization program was designed to meet the stringent requirements of **ICH Q5A(R2)** (Viral Safety Evaluation), **ICH Q5B** (Analysis of the Expression Construct), and **ICH Q5D** (Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates). All testing was conducted under Current Good Manufacturing Practices (cGMP) at Google Health Sciences’ South San Francisco facility and validated contract research organizations (CROs).

---

#### 2.0 WCB MANUFACTURE AND STORAGE

##### 2.1 WCB Lineage and Pedigree
The WCB was prepared by expanding a single vial of the MCB through a defined number of passages in a chemically defined, animal-derived component-free (ADCF) medium. 

**Table 1: WCB Manufacturing Summary (Batch GLUC-2025-WCB-01)**
| Parameter | Specification/Data |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Parental MCB ID** | GLUC-2024-MCB-01 |
| **Date of Cryopreservation** | 14-JAN-2025 |
| **Passage Number (from Thaw)** | P+5 |
| **Total Vials Produced** | 450 Vials |
| **Vial Configuration** | 2.0 mL Cryogenic internal thread vial |
| **Fill Volume** | 1.5 mL |
| **Cell Concentration** | $1.5 \times 10^7$ viable cells/mL |
| **Post-Thaw Viability** | 98.2% |
| **Cryopreservation Media** | GHS-Proprietary CD-Media + 10% DMSO |

##### 2.2 Cryopreservation Protocol
1. **Harvesting:** Cells were harvested at a density of $4.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL with viability >95%.
2. **Centrifugation:** 300 x g for 8 minutes at 4°C.
3. **Resuspension:** Pellets resuspended in chilled (4°C) freezing medium.
4. **Controlled Rate Freezing:** Utilized a CryoMed™ controlled-rate freezer at a rate of -1°C/minute until -80°C was reached.
5. **Storage:** Transfer to vapor phase liquid nitrogen (VPLN) at $\leq -150^{\circ}C$ within 2 hours of freezing completion.

---

#### 3.0 COMPREHENSIVE CHARACTERIZATION PROGRAM

The WCB characterization is divided into four critical pillars: Identity, Purity/Adventitious Agent Safety, Genetic Stability, and Growth Kinetics.

##### 3.1 Identity Testing
Identity was confirmed to ensure the absence of cross-contamination and the presence of the GHS-CHO-001 host cell signature.

**Table 2: Identity Testing Results**
| Test Attribute | Methodology | Specification | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Isoenzyme Analysis** | Electrophoretic mobility (LDH, MDH) | Characteristic of CHO | Confirmed CHO |
| **COI Barcoding** | Cytochrome C Oxidase I Sequencing | Match to *Cricetulus griseus* | 99.9% Match |
| **STR Profiling** | Short Tandem Repeat Analysis | Match to GHS-CHO-001 Baseline | Consistent |

##### 3.2 Purity and Adventitious Agent Testing (ICH Q5A)
A multi-tiered approach was utilized to ensure the absence of bacteria, fungi, mycoplasma, and viruses.

###### 3.2.1 Sterility and Mycoplasma
Testing was performed per USP <71> and USP <63>.

*   **Sterility (USP <71>):** 14-day incubation in Tryptic Soy Broth (TSB) and Fluid Thioglycollate Medium (FTM). Result: **No Growth (Pass)**.
*   **Mycoplasma (USP <63>):** Both broth/agar culture and indicator cell culture (Hoechst staining) were employed. Result: **Negative (Pass)**.

###### 3.2.2 Viral Safety Evaluation
Extensive *in vitro* and *in vivo* (where applicable) assays were performed to screen for a broad spectrum of viruses.

**Table 3: Viral Safety Characterization**
| Virus Type | Assay System | Observation Period | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Adventitious Viruses** | In vitro (MRC-5, Vero, CHO-K1) | 28 Days | Negative |
| **Bovine Viruses** | 9CFR Screening (BVDV, BPB, BPV) | 21 Days | Negative |
| **Porcine Viruses** | 9CFR Screening (PPV) | 21 Days | Negative |
| **Retroviruses** | Transmission Electron Microscopy (TEM) | 200 cell profiles | Type A & C present* |
| **Retroviruses** | PERT (Product Enhanced Reverse Transcriptase) | Sensitivity: 10 fg | Positive* |

*\*Note: Endogenous retrovirus-like particles (RVLPs) are expected in CHO cell lines and are addressed via downstream clearance validation (Section 3.2.S.2.6).*

---

#### 4.0 GENETIC STABILITY AND EXPRESSION CONSTRUCT ANALYSIS (ICH Q5B)

To ensure the Glucogen-XR transgene remains stable through the WCB expansion, molecular characterization was performed on the WCB and Cells at the Limit of In Vitro Age (CALIV).

##### 4.1 Nucleic Acid Sequencing
The entire coding region of the Glucogen-XR glucapeptide was sequenced.
*   **Procedure:** Total RNA was isolated from WCB cells using the RNeasy kit. cDNA was synthesized via RT-PCR.
*   **Results:** The consensus sequence was 100% identical to the reference sequence (GHS-GENE-REF-01). No point mutations, deletions, or insertions were detected at a sensitivity of 5% (Deep Sequencing/NGS).

##### 4.2 Copy Number Determination by qPCR
The number of integrated copies of the GLP-1 receptor agonist gene was determined relative to a single-copy endogenous gene (Glucagon receptor).

**Calculation Formula:**
$$\Delta \Delta C_t = (C_{t, target} - C_{t, ref})_{sample} - (C_{t, target} - C_{t, ref})_{calibrator}$$
$$Copy Number = 2^{-\Delta \Delta C_t} \times 2$$

**Table 4: Copy Number Analysis**
| Sample | Mean Ct (Target) | Mean Ct (Ref) | Calculated Copy Number |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MCB (Baseline)** | 18.4 | 22.1 | 12.4 |
| **WCB (GLUC-2025-WCB-01)** | 18.5 | 22.2 | 12.2 |
| **CALIV (End of Prod)** | 18.6 | 22.3 | 12.1 |

*Conclusion: The copy number remains stable within $\pm 10\%$ through the production lifespan.*

##### 4.3 Southern Blot Analysis
Genomic DNA was digested with restriction enzymes (HindIII, EcoRI) to evaluate the integration pattern.
*   **Observation:** The banding pattern for the WCB was identical to the MCB, indicating no gross chromosomal rearrangements or loss of integration sites.

---

#### 5.0 GROWTH KINETICS AND PRODUCTIVITY ASSESSMENT

A satellite expansion of the WCB was performed in the 50L bioreactor (Equipment ID: BR-50-009) to confirm performance consistency.

**Table 5: Performance Characteristics of WCB vs. MCB**
| Parameter | MCB (P+3) | WCB (P+5) | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **$\mu_{max}$ (Specific Growth Rate)** | $0.028 hr^{-1}$ | $0.029 hr^{-1}$ | $0.025 - 0.035 hr^{-1}$ |
| **Doubling Time ($t_d$)** | 24.7 hours | 23.9 hours | 22 - 28 hours |
| **VCD peak ($10^6$ cells/mL)** | 18.4 | 19.1 | >15.0 |
| **Specific Productivity ($q_p$)** | 32 pg/cell/day | 34 pg/cell/day | >25 pg/cell/day |
| **Final Titer (Day 14)** | 4.2 g/L | 4.5 g/L | Report Value |

---

#### 6.0 CELL LINE PHENOTYPE AND MORPHOLOGY
Morphology was assessed via phase-contrast microscopy. Cells in the WCB exhibited characteristic CHO-K1 morphology: spherical shape in suspension, minimal aggregation (clumping <5 cells), and uniform diameter (approx. 15-18 $\mu m$). 

---

#### 7.0 STORAGE AND STABILITY PROGRAM

The WCB is stored in the GHS Centralized Biorepository in vapor phase liquid nitrogen. 
*   **Continuous Monitoring:** 24/7 temperature monitoring with alarm set points at $-150^{\circ}C$. 
*   **Inventory Management:** A dual-site storage strategy is employed, with 20% of the WCB (90 vials) stored at the Google Health alternate facility in Mountain View, CA, for disaster recovery.
*   **Stability Monitoring:** One vial of WCB is thawed every 12 months to assess viability and growth kinetics (Protocol GHS-QC-PRO-045).

---

#### 8.0 REGULATORY CONFORMANCE STATEMENT
Based on the results presented in this subsection, the Working Cell Bank **GLUC-2025-WCB-01** is deemed suitable for the manufacture of Glucogen-XR. It is free from adventitious contaminants, exhibits consistent genetic stability, and maintains the required growth and productivity profile through the validated limit of *in vitro* cell age.

---
**References:**
1.  *ICH Q5A(R2): Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation.*
2.  *ICH Q5B: Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct.*
3.  *ICH Q5D: Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products.*
4.  *USP <63> Mycoplasma Tests.*
5.  *USP <71> Sterility Tests.*
