# Cell Bank Testing

## Identity and Purity Testing

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.3: CONTROL OF MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: CELL BANK TESTING – IDENTITY AND PURITY TESTING

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.1 Overview of Identity and Purity Strategy
The characterization of the Master Cell Bank (MCB), Working Cell Bank (WCB), and End-of-Production Cells (EOPC/CALSU) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is conducted in accordance with **ICH Q5A(R2)** (*Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation*), **ICH Q5B** (*Analysis of the Expression Construct*), and **ICH Q5D** (*Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates*). 

Google Health Sciences (GHS) employs a multi-tiered testing strategy to ensure the genetic identity, phenotypic stability, and microbiological purity of the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line. All testing described herein was performed under Current Good Manufacturing Practices (cGMP) at the GHS South San Francisco facility and validated contract research organizations (CROs).

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.2 Identity Testing Protocols and Results

Identity testing is designed to confirm that the cell substrate is of CHO (Cricetulus griseus) origin and contains the specific expression vector (pGHS-GLUC-XR-09) encoding the glucapeptide sequence.

##### 3.2.S.2.3.2.1 Isoenzyme Analysis (Biochemical Identity)
Isoenzyme analysis was performed to confirm the species of origin and to detect potential cross-contamination with other mammalian cell lines used in the facility (e.g., HEK293, Vero).

*   **Protocol:** Electrophoretic mobility of four key enzymes (LDH, MDH, G6PD, and NP) was evaluated using the AuthentiKit™ system. 
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** The migration patterns must be consistent with the *Cricetulus griseus* reference standard and distinct from human, murine, or bovine patterns.

**Table 1: Isoenzyme Analysis Results for Glucogen-XR Cell Banks**

| Test Parameter | Methodology | MCB (Lot: GLUC-2025-MCB-01) | WCB (Lot: GLUC-2025-WCB-01) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Lactate Dehydrogenase (LDH)** | Electrophoresis | Consistent with CHO Ref | Consistent with CHO Ref | Pass |
| **Malate Dehydrogenase (MDH)** | Electrophoresis | Consistent with CHO Ref | Consistent with CHO Ref | Pass |
| **Glucose-6-Phosphate (G6PD)** | Electrophoresis | Consistent with CHO Ref | Consistent with CHO Ref | Pass |
| **Nucleoside Phosphorylase (NP)** | Electrophoresis | Consistent with CHO Ref | Consistent with CHO Ref | Pass |

##### 3.2.S.2.3.2.2 Genotypic Identity (DNA Barcoding)
DNA barcoding targeting the Cytochrome c Oxidase I (COI) mitochondrial gene was utilized for high-resolution species identification.

*   **Procedure:**
    1.  Total genomic DNA extraction from 5x10^6 cells.
    2.  PCR amplification of the 648 bp region of the COI gene using Folmer primers.
    3.  Bidirectional Sanger sequencing.
    4.  Alignment against the BOLD (Barcode of Life Data Systems) database.
*   **Statistical Threshold:** Percent Identity > 99.8% to *Cricetulus griseus*.

**Table 2: DNA Barcoding Data Summary**

| Bank ID | Accession Number Match | % Identity | E-Value | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | KF911394.1 | 99.98% | 0.0 | Confirmed CHO |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | KF911394.1 | 99.97% | 0.0 | Confirmed CHO |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.3 Purity Testing (Adventitious Agent Screening)

Purity testing ensures the absence of bacteria, fungi, mycoplasma, and viruses. This section satisfies the requirements of **USP <61>, <62>, and <63>**.

##### 3.2.S.2.3.3.1 Sterility (Bacteria and Fungi)
Sterility testing was conducted via the Membrane Filtration Method according to **USP <71>**.

*   **Incubation Parameters:**
    *   Tryptic Soy Broth (TSB): 22.5°C ± 2.5°C for 14 days (Aerobic/Fungal).
    *   Fluid Thioglycollate Medium (FTM): 32.5°C ± 2.5°C for 14 days (Anaerobic).

**Table 3: Sterility Testing Results**

| Batch Number | Medium | Volume Tested | Observations (Day 14) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | TSB | 10 mL | No growth | Sterile |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | FTM | 10 mL | No growth | Sterile |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | TSB | 10 mL | No growth | Sterile |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | FTM | 10 mL | No growth | Sterile |

##### 3.2.S.2.3.3.2 Mycoplasma Testing
Mycoplasma testing was performed using a dual-method approach: the Culture Method (Agar and Broth) and the Indicator Cell Culture Method (Hoechst Staining), compliant with **USP <63>** and **EP 2.6.7**.

*   **Strains Used for Sensitivity (Positive Controls):** *M. pneumoniae, M. hyorhinis, M. orale, M. synoviae, M. fermentans, A. laidlawii*.
*   **Detection Limit:** ≤ 10 CFU/mL or 10 GC/mL.

**Table 4: Mycoplasma Detection Results**

| Bank | Method | Observation | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | Agar/Broth Culture | No colonies at 28 days | Negative |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | DNA Fluorescence | No extranuclear staining | Negative |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | Agar/Broth Culture | No colonies at 28 days | Negative |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | DNA Fluorescence | No extranuclear staining | Negative |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.4 Viral Safety Testing

In alignment with **ICH Q5A(R2)**, the GHS-CHO-001 cell line underwent exhaustive viral screening, including *in vitro* and *in vivo* assays, as well as Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS).

##### 3.2.S.2.3.4.1 In Vitro Adventitious Virus Assay
The cells were co-cultivated with various indicator cell lines (MRC-5, Vero, and CHO-K1) to detect cytopathic effects (CPE), hemadsorption, and hemagglutination.

*   **Protocol:**
    1.  Inoculation of cell lysates onto indicator monolayers.
    2.  Observation for 14 days for CPE.
    3.  Blind passage and further observation for 14 days.
    4.  Hemadsorption test using Guinea pig, Chicken, and Human Type O erythrocytes.

**Table 5: In Vitro Viral Screening**

| Indicator System | Observation (Day 28) | Hemadsorption | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MRC-5 (Human Lung)** | No CPE | Negative | Negative |
| **Vero (Monkey Kidney)** | No CPE | Negative | Negative |
| **CHO-K1 (Hamster)** | No CPE | Negative | Negative |

##### 3.2.S.2.3.4.2 Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS) for Viral Discovery
To augment traditional assays, NGS was performed on the MCB (GLUC-2025-MCB-01) for the detection of "unknown" or "non-culturable" viral sequences.

*   **Platform:** Illumina NovaSeq 6000.
*   **Bioinformatics Pipeline:** GHS-ViroSearch-v4.2 (proprietary).
*   **Depth of Coverage:** > 30 million reads per sample.
*   **Sensitivity:** Detectable at 1 part per 10^7 RNA/DNA molecules.
*   **Results:** No sequences corresponding to known mammalian pathogens were identified. Endogenous retrovirus-like particles (Type C) characteristic of CHO cells were identified, as expected.

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.5 Genetic Stability and Copy Number Analysis

To ensure the Glucogen-XR expression remains constant throughout the lifespan of the cell bank, genetic stability was assessed from the MCB to the EOPC (End of Production Cells).

##### 3.2.S.2.3.5.1 Transgene Copy Number by qPCR
Total genomic DNA was isolated and the ratio of the *Glucogen-XR* gene to an endogenous reference gene (*GHS-Glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate dehydrogenase*) was determined.

*   **Calculation:**
    $$\text{Relative Copy Number} = 2^{-\Delta\Delta C_t}$$
*   **Target:** Maintenance of $\pm 20\%$ copy number from MCB to EOPC.

**Table 6: Genetic Stability – Copy Number Data**

| Sample ID | Generation Number | Mean Ct (Target) | Mean Ct (Ref) | Calculated Copy Number |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | p5 | 18.2 | 22.1 | 14.8 copies/cell |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | p15 | 18.3 | 22.2 | 14.7 copies/cell |
| GLUC-2025-EOPC-01 | p65 | 18.4 | 22.2 | 14.5 copies/cell |

##### 3.2.S.2.3.5.2 Restriction Enzyme Mapping
Southern Blot analysis was performed to confirm the integrity of the integration site and the absence of large-scale rearrangements.

*   **Enzymes:** *HindIII, EcoRI, BamHI*.
*   **Probe:** Fluorescently labeled 800bp Glucogen-XR cDNA fragment.
*   **Result:** All bands observed in the MCB were identical in size and intensity to those in the WCB and EOPC, confirming structural stability of the expression cassette.

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.6 Retrovirus Quantification (TEM Analysis)
CHO cells are known to contain endogenous retrovirus-like particles. Transmission Electron Microscopy (TEM) was used to quantify these particles in the MCB.

*   **Procedure:** 200 cell sections were examined by an expert pathologist.
*   **Observation:** Presence of Type A (intracytoplasmic) and Type C (extracellular budding) particles.
*   **Quantification:**
    *   Type A: 45 particles/cell section.
    *   Type C: 1.2 x 10^5 particles/mL of supernatant.
*   **Regulatory Conclusion:** These levels are within the historical range for CHO-K1 derivatives and are effectively cleared by the downstream purification process (see Section 3.2.S.3.2 for Viral Clearance Validation).

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.7 Conclusion of Identity and Purity
The results summarized above demonstrate that the **GLUC-2025** series of cell banks are:
1.  **Identified** correctly as *Cricetulus griseus* containing the Glucogen-XR transgene.
2.  **Pure** and free from detectable adventitious agents (bacteria, fungi, mycoplasma, and non-endogenous viruses).
3.  **Genetically Stable** through the limit of *in vitro* cell age (p65).

These data support the use of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line for the commercial manufacture of Glucogen-XR.

---

1. ICH Q5A(R2): *Viral Safety Evaluation of Biotechnology Products Derived from Cell Lines of Human or Animal Origin.*
2. USP <63>: *Mycoplasma Tests.*
3. GHS Internal Report RPT-GLUC-2025-004: *Detailed NGS Analysis of Master Cell Bank.*

## Adventitious Agent Testing

### 3.2.S.2.3.2 Adventitious Agent Testing for Master Cell Bank (MCB) and Working Cell Bank (WCB)

The safety profile of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is fundamentally predicated upon the comprehensive qualification of the recombinant Chinese Hamster Ovary (CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative, GHS-CHO-001) cell substrate. In alignment with **ICH Q5A(R2)**, **ICH Q5D**, and **USP <1050>**, Google Health Sciences (GHS) has implemented a multi-tiered testing strategy to ensure the absence of adventitious agents, including bacteria, fungi, mycoplasma, and viruses (endogenous and non-endogenous).

---

#### 1.0 Overview of Testing Strategy
The GHS-CHO-001 cell line was derived using a proprietary protein-free, chemically defined media system to mitigate the risk of Transmissible Spongiform Encephalopathy (TSE) and Bovine Spongiform Encephalopathy (BSE). Adventitious agent testing was performed on the Master Cell Bank (MCB: Lot GLUC-2025-MCB01) and the Working Cell Bank (WCB: Lot GLUC-2025-WCB01) at GHS South San Francisco and certified contract research organizations (CROs).

##### 1.1 Regulatory Compliance Framework
Testing protocols were developed to satisfy the following regulatory frameworks:
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry (2010):** Characterization and Qualification of Cell Substrates and Other Biological Materials Used in the Production of Viral Vaccines for Infectious Disease Indications.
*   **ICH Q5A(R2):** Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation of Biotechnology Products Derived from Cell Lines of Human or Animal Origin.
*   **USP <63>:** Mycoplasma Tests.
*   **21 CFR 610.12:** General Biological Products Standards – Sterility.

---

#### 2.0 Sterility Testing (Bacteria and Fungi)
Sterility testing was conducted to ensure the absence of aerobic and anaerobic bacteria and fungi.

##### 2.1 Methodology: Membrane Filtration and Direct Inoculation
Samples from MCB GLUC-2025-MCB01 and WCB GLUC-2025-WCB01 were subjected to 14-day incubation periods.
*   **Media:** Fluid Thioglycollate Medium (FTM) for anaerobic bacteria; Soybean Casein Digest Medium (SCDM) for aerobic bacteria and fungi.
*   **Incubation:** FTM at 32.5°C ± 2.5°C; SCDM at 22.5°C ± 2.5°C.

**Table 1: Summary of Sterility Testing Results for MCB and WCB**

| Test Parameter | Method Reference | Batch Number | Inoculum Volume | Observation Period | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Bacterial Sterility** | USP <71> / 21 CFR 610.12 | GLUC-2025-MCB01 | 10 mL (1% of pool) | 14 Days | No Growth |
| **Fungal Sterility** | USP <71> / 21 CFR 610.12 | GLUC-2025-MCB01 | 10 mL (1% of pool) | 14 Days | No Growth |
| **Bacterial Sterility** | USP <71> / 21 CFR 610.12 | GLUC-2025-WCB01 | 10 mL (1% of pool) | 14 Days | No Growth |
| **Fungal Sterility** | USP <71> / 21 CFR 610.12 | GLUC-2025-WCB01 | 10 mL (1% of pool) | 14 Days | No Growth |

---

#### 3.0 Mycoplasma Testing
Mycoplasma testing was performed using both the Compendial (Culture) Method and the Indicator Cell Culture Method (DNA Staining).

##### 3.1 Culture Method (GHS-SOP-772)
1.  **Inoculation:** 2.0 mL of cell suspension (minimum $1 \times 10^7$ cells) into 100 mL of mycoplasma broth.
2.  **Subculture:** Performed on days 3, 7, and 14 onto mycoplasma agar plates.
3.  **Atmosphere:** Microaerophilic (95% $N_2$, 5% $CO_2$) at 36°C.
4.  **Observation:** Plates monitored via microscopy for 14 days for "fried-egg" colony morphology.

##### 3.2 Indicator Cell Culture Method (Vero Cells)
1.  **Preparation:** Vero cells seeded in Chamber Slides.
2.  **Inoculation:** Sample lysate added to Vero cells and incubated for 3–5 days.
3.  **Staining:** Cells fixed and stained with Hoechst 33258 fluorescent DNA stain.
4.  **Interpretation:** Extranuclear fluorescence indicates mycoplasma contamination.

**Table 2: Mycoplasma Testing Results for Glucogen-XR Cell Banks**

| Assay Type | Target Organisms | Acceptance Criteria | MCB (GLUC-2025-MCB01) | WCB (GLUC-2025-WCB01) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Agar/Broth Culture** | *M. pneumoniae, M. orale, M. hyorhinis* | No Growth | Negative | Negative |
| **Indicator Cell Culture** | Non-culturable Mycoplasma | No Extranuclear Fluorescence | Negative | Negative |
| **PCR-Based Detection** | *Acholeplasma laidlawii* | Negative | Negative | Negative |

---

#### 4.0 Viral Adventitious Agent Testing
The viral safety of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line was assessed through *in vitro* and *in vivo* assays, as well as specific PCR and biochemical screens.

##### 4.1 In Vitro Virus Screening (General)
The *in vitro* assay utilizes multiple indicator cell lines to detect a broad spectrum of viruses through Cytopathic Effect (CPE), Hemadsorption (HAD), and Hemagglutination (HAG).

**Indicator Cell Lines Used:**
1.  **MRC-5:** Human diploid lung cells (detects human respiratory viruses).
2.  **Vero:** African Green Monkey kidney cells (detects various simian and human viruses).
3.  **CHO-K1:** Homologous cell line (detects CHO-specific contaminants).

**Procedure (GHS-SOP-VIR-101):**
*   **Inoculation:** $10^7$ cells from GLUC-2025-MCB01 are lysed via three freeze-thaw cycles.
*   **Adsorption:** Lysate is inoculated onto 75 $cm^2$ flasks of indicator cells.
*   **Observation:** 28-day observation period with subculturing at Day 14.
*   **End-point:** HAD assays performed using Guinea Pig, Chicken, and Human Type O erythrocytes at 4°C and 37°C.

**Table 3: In Vitro Viral Screening Results**

| Indicator Cell Line | Assay Parameter | Observation Period | Result (MCB) | Result (WCB) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MRC-5** | CPE / HAD | 28 Days | Negative | Negative |
| **Vero** | CPE / HAD | 28 Days | Negative | Negative |
| **CHO-K1** | CPE / HAD | 28 Days | Negative | Negative |

##### 4.2 In Vivo Virus Screening
*In vivo* testing involves the inoculation of cell bank materials into various animal models to detect viruses that do not replicate in cell culture.

**Models and Protocols:**
1.  **Suckling Mice:** Inoculated intracerebrally and intraperitoneally. Observed for 14 days for morbidity/mortality.
2.  **Adult Mice:** Inoculated intraperitoneally. Observed for 21 days.
3.  **Embryonated Chicken Eggs:** Inoculated via allantoic and yolk sac routes. Checked for viability and hemagglutinating activity.

**Table 4: In Vivo Viral Testing Summary (MCB GLUC-2025-MCB01)**

| Animal System | Number of Animals | Route of Inoculation | Observation | Outcome |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Suckling Mice** | 20 | IC / IP | 14 Days | Healthy/Normal |
| **Adult Mice** | 20 | IP | 21 Days | Healthy/Normal |
| **Guinea Pigs** | 5 | IP / IM | 28 Days | Healthy/Normal |
| **Embryonated Eggs** | 10 | Allantoic | 10 Days | Negative HAG |

---

#### 5.0 Endogenous Virus Testing
CHO cells are known to contain endogenous retrovirus-like particles (Type C and Type R). GHS has quantified these particles to establish a baseline for downstream clearance validation.

##### 5.1 Transmission Electron Microscopy (TEM)
Direct visualization of 200 cell sections from MCB GLUC-2025-MCB01.
*   **Results:** Type C particles observed (average 15 per cell section). No Type A or other infectious morphologies detected.

##### 5.2 Reverse Transcriptase (RT) Assay
Quantitative Fluorescent Product-Enhanced Reverse Transcriptase (F-PERT) assay.
*   **Sensitivity:** $10^{-9}$ units of RT.
*   **Result (MCB):** Positive (Expected for CHO lines). Activity Level: $3.2 \times 10^5$ particles/mL equivalent.

---

#### 6.0 Species-Specific Virus Testing (PCR-Based)
PCR panels were utilized to screen for specific viruses of concern in CHO production, including:
*   **Bovine Viral Diarrhea Virus (BVDV)** (via 9 CFR 113.47 requirements)
*   **Porcine Parvovirus (PPV)**
*   **Murine Minute Virus (MMV)**
*   **Cache Valley Virus (CVV)**
*   **Vesivirus 2117**

**Table 5: Species-Specific PCR Results**

| Virus Target | Detection Limit | Batch GLUC-2025-MCB01 | Batch GLUC-2025-WCB01 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MMV** | 10 copies/rxn | Not Detected | Not Detected |
| **BVDV-1/2** | 50 copies/rxn | Not Detected | Not Detected |
| **Vesivirus 2117** | 10 copies/rxn | Not Detected | Not Detected |
| **Reovirus 3** | 100 copies/rxn | Not Detected | Not Detected |

---

#### 7.0 Conclusion
Based on the results detailed in Tables 1 through 5, MCB Lot GLUC-2025-MCB01 and WCB Lot GLUC-2025-WCB01 are free from adventitious bacterial, fungal, mycoplasmal, and non-endogenous viral contaminants. The presence of endogenous retrovirus-like particles is consistent with the CHO-K1 genotype and is addressed through the validated viral clearance steps in the downstream manufacturing process (refer to Section 3.2.S.3.2).

---

## Genetic Stability Testing

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.3: CONTROL OF MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: GENETIC STABILITY TESTING OF THE PRODUCTION CELL LINE

---

**Proprietary Name:** Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)  
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences  
**Manufacturing Site:** 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080, USA  
**Cell Line ID:** GHS-CHO-001 (CHO-K1 GS-/-)  
**Document Ref:** M3-DS-GEN-GS-001  
**Reporting Period:** 2023–2025  

---

#### 1.0 OVERVIEW AND REGULATORY CONTEXT

The genetic stability program for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide) production cell line, GHS-CHO-001, was designed in accordance with **ICH Guideline Q5B: Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products**, and **ICH Q5D: Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products**.

The primary objective of this assessment is to ensure that the expression cassette encoding the glucapeptide molecule remains structurally intact and integrated at a consistent copy number throughout the lifespan of the culture, extending from the Master Cell Bank (MCB) through the Working Cell Bank (WCB) to the End-of-Production Cells (EPC) or Cells at the Limit of In Vitro Cell Age (CALIVCA).

Google Health Sciences has implemented a multi-faceted analytical approach combining traditional molecular biology techniques with Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS) and droplet digital PCR (ddPCR) to provide a high-resolution map of the genetic landscape of the production system.

---

#### 2.0 TEST ARTICLES AND SAMPLING HIERARCHY

Genetic stability was evaluated across the entire manufacturing continuum. The following lots were utilized for the comprehensive stability study:

| Sample Description | Batch Number | Passage Number | Generation Number (VCD-based) | Storage Location |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Master Cell Bank (MCB)** | GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | P05 | G0 | Vapor Phase LN2 |
| **Working Cell Bank (WCB)** | GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | P12 | G14 | Vapor Phase LN2 |
| **End of Production (EPC)** | GLUC-2025-EPC-01 | P28 | G52 | Liquid Nitrogen |
| **CALIVCA (Limit of Age)** | GLUC-2025-CAL-01 | P35 | G74 | Liquid Nitrogen |

*Note: CALIVCA represents 125% of the proposed commercial lifespan to ensure a validated safety margin for genetic drift.*

---

#### 3.0 ANALYTICAL STRATEGY AND ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA

The genetic stability program comprises five core pillars:
1.  **Restriction Endonuclease Mapping (Southern Blotting):** To confirm the structural integrity of the transgene and the flanking genomic regions.
2.  **Copy Number Determination (ddPCR):** To quantify the number of integrated expression cassettes per host genome.
3.  **mRNA/cDNA Sequencing:** To verify the primary sequence of the transcript and detect any point mutations or deleterious variants.
4.  **Transcriptional Analysis (Northern Blotting):** To assess transcript size and stability.
5.  **Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS - Whole Genome/Targeted):** To identify integration sites and assess the frequency of minor variants (SNVs/Indels).

##### 3.1 Acceptance Criteria Summary Table

| Parameter | Method | Specification/Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Cassette Integrity** | Southern Blot | Banding patterns must be consistent across MCB, WCB, and EPC; no new fragments >5% intensity. |
| **Copy Number** | ddPCR | Copy number at EPC must be within ±20% of the MCB value. |
| **Coding Sequence** | Sanger/NGS | 100% identity to the reference Glucogen-XR sequence; no variants >1% frequency. |
| **mRNA Size** | Northern Blot | Single band at expected size (~1.4 kb); no truncated or elongated species. |
| **Integration Site** | Targeted NGS | Consistent chromosomal coordinates; no evidence of translocation or secondary integration. |

---

#### 4.0 DETAILED PROTOCOLS AND PROCEDURES

##### 4.1 Genomic DNA (gDNA) Extraction and Quality Control
gDNA was extracted from $2 \times 10^7$ cells using the Google Health Sciences proprietary high-molecular-weight (HMW) extraction protocol (SOP-GHS-GEN-044).

**Step-by-Step Procedure:**
1.  **Lysis:** Cells are resuspended in Tris-EDTA buffer and treated with 0.5% SDS and Proteinase K (20 mg/mL) at 56°C for 3 hours.
2.  **Purification:** Automated phenol-chloroform-isoamyl alcohol (25:24:1) extraction using the GHS-Hamilton Star Platform.
3.  **Precipitation:** Addition of 3M Sodium Acetate (pH 5.2) and 100% Ethanol; spooling of DNA to maintain HMW integrity.
4.  **Quantification:** Qubit 4.0 Fluorometric quantification (High Sensitivity Assay).
5.  **Purity:** $A_{260}/A_{280}$ ratio must be between 1.8 and 2.0.

##### 4.2 Southern Blot Analysis (Restriction Mapping)
Southern blotting was performed to confirm that no large-scale rearrangements occurred in the expression cassette.

**Restriction Enzymes Used:**
*   **EcoRI:** Single cutter within the promoter region; used to determine integration fragment size.
*   **HindIII/XbaI:** Double digest to release the intact 2.4 kb expression cassette.

**Procedure (SOP-GHS-MOL-089):**
1.  Digest 10 µg of gDNA with 50U of restriction enzyme for 16 hours.
2.  Electrophoresis on 0.8% agarose gel at 40V for 12 hours.
3.  Depurination (0.25M HCl), Denaturation (0.5M NaOH), and Neutralization.
4.  Capillary transfer to positively charged nylon membrane.
5.  Hybridization with $^{32}$P-labeled 450bp probe targeting the Glucogen-XR CDR3 region.
6.  Phosphorimager analysis (Typhoon FLA 9500).

---

#### 5.0 RESULTS AND STATISTICAL ANALYSIS

##### 5.1 Copy Number Analysis by Droplet Digital PCR (ddPCR)
Copy number variation (CNV) is a critical indicator of genetic instability. We utilized the Bio-Rad QX200 system targeting the Glucogen-XR heavy chain (HC) domain relative to the endogenous CHO glucagon receptor (GCGR) as a single-copy reference gene.

**Calculation Formula:**
$$Copy Number = \frac{Concentration_{Target} (copies/\mu L)}{Concentration_{Reference} (copies/\mu L)} \times 2$$
*(Assuming diploid status for the reference gene in CHO-K1 GS-/-)*

**Data Table 5.1: Copy Number Stability Results**

| Sample ID | Replicate 1 | Replicate 2 | Replicate 3 | Mean Copy No. | SD | % CV |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MCB (GLUC-2025-MCB-01)** | 14.2 | 13.8 | 14.1 | **14.03** | 0.21 | 1.5% |
| **WCB (GLUC-2025-WCB-01)** | 13.9 | 14.3 | 14.0 | **14.07** | 0.21 | 1.5% |
| **EPC (GLUC-2025-EPC-01)** | 13.7 | 13.6 | 13.9 | **13.73** | 0.15 | 1.1% |
| **CALIVCA (GLUC-2025-CAL-01)** | 13.5 | 13.4 | 13.8 | **13.57** | 0.21 | 1.5% |

**Statistical Interpretation:**
The mean copy number remained stable from MCB (14.03) to CALIVCA (13.57). A One-Way ANOVA was performed, resulting in a p-value of 0.18 ($p > 0.05$), indicating no statistically significant loss of the transgene over the validated 74 generations.

---

##### 5.2 Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS) of Expression Cassette
To satisfy ICH Q5B requirements for verifying the sequence of the integrated DNA, deep sequencing was performed at 10,000x coverage depth.

**Table 5.2: Minor Variant Detection (SNVs/Indels)**

| Batch Number | Region | Observed Mutation | Frequency (%) | Regulatory Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-MCB-01 | CDS | None | <0.01% | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-WCB-01 | CDS | None | <0.01% | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-EPC-01 | CDS | G -> A (Intron 2) | 0.04% | Pass (Non-coding) |
| GLUC-2025-CAL-01 | CDS | T -> C (Silent) | 0.07% | Pass (No AO change) |

**Conclusion on Sequence Integrity:**
No amino acid substitutions were detected above the validated limit of detection (LOD) of 0.5%. The primary structure of the Glucogen-XR protein is genetically conserved.

---

#### 6.0 TRANSCRIPTIONAL STABILITY (NORTHERN BLOT)
Northern blot analysis was conducted to ensure that the mRNA species produced by GHS-CHO-001 are of the predicted size and that no truncated transcripts are formed during extended culture.

**Experimental Parameters:**
*   **RNA Extraction:** RNeasy Mini Kit (Qiagen).
*   **Loading:** 20 µg Total RNA per lane.
*   **Probe:** Biotin-labeled antisense RNA probe (800 nt).
*   **Detection:** Chemiluminescence (C-DiGit Blot Scanner).

**Table 6.1: Northern Blot Densitometry Results**

| Sample | Main Band (1.4 kb) Intensity | High MW Smear (%) | Low MW Fragments (%) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **MCB** | 98.4% | 1.1% | 0.5% | Conforms |
| **WCB** | 98.1% | 1.2% | 0.7% | Conforms |
| **EPC** | 97.9% | 1.4% | 0.7% | Conforms |
| **CALIVCA** | 97.5% | 1.6% | 0.9% | Conforms |

---

#### 7.0 INTEGRATION SITE ANALYSIS (ISA)
Targeted Locus Amplification (TLA) was utilized to identify the integration site of the Glucogen-XR cassette in the GHS-CHO-001 genome.

*   **Integration Site:** Chromosome 4, Position 124,556,120 (CHO-K1 RefSeq).
*   **Orientation:** Head-to-Tail tandem array.
*   **Flanking Sequences:** Confirmed stability of the 5' and 3' genomic junctions across all cell banks. No "scrambling" of the host genome was observed at the site of integration.

---

#### 8.0 DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSION
The genetic stability testing of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide) production cell line GHS-CHO-001 demonstrates robust consistency. Southern blot mapping, ddPCR copy number quantification, and NGS-based sequence verification collectively confirm that the expression construct is stably integrated and maintained throughout the defined manufacturing window.

The slight numerical decrease in copy number observed at CALIVCA (from 14.03 to 13.57) does not impact product quality or titer, as evidenced by the comparable specific productivity ($Q_p$) data presented in Section 3.2.S.2.2. These data support the use of GHS-CHO-001 for the commercial production of Glucogen-XR.

---

#### 9.0 REFERENCES
1.  **ICH Q5B:** Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products.
2.  **ICH Q5D:** Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products.
3.  **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Proteins.
4.  *Google Health Sciences Internal Report:* GHS-RPT-2024-0012: Molecular Characterization of GHS-CHO-001.

# Control of Source Materials

## Raw Material Specifications

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.3: CONTROL OF MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: RAW MATERIAL SPECIFICATIONS

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.1 Introduction and Scope
This section details the comprehensive specifications, procurement strategies, and quality control frameworks for all raw materials, starting materials, reagents, and processing aids utilized in the manufacture of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** drug substance. 

Google Health Sciences (GHS) operates under a Global Quality Management System (GQMS) that adheres to **ICH Q7 (Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients)** and **ICH Q11 (Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances)**. For Glucogen-XR, a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via the GHS-CHO-001 cell line, the selection and control of raw materials are critical to ensuring the purity, safety, and consistency of the final therapeutic peptide.

#### 3.2.S.2.3.2 Material Classification and Risk-Based Categorization
All materials entering the manufacturing facility at 3000 Innovation Drive are categorized based on their proximity to the final product and their potential impact on Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs).

| Category | Definition | Examples | Control Level |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Class I** | Compendial (USP/NF/EP/JP) Excipients & Chemicals | Sodium Chloride, Histidine, Sucrose | Full Compendial Testing |
| **Class II** | Non-Compendial Complex Reagents | Specialized Peptidases, Linker Molecules | Custom Specification + Site Audit |
| **Class III** | Cell Culture Media & Supplements | GHS-Custom-Media-04, Recombinant Insulin | Lot-to-Lot Growth Promotion |
| **Class IV** | Processing Aids & Consumables | Chromatography Resins, UF/DF Membranes | Leachables/Extractables Study |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.3 Detailed Specifications for Chemically Defined Media (CDM)
The GHS-CHO-001 cell line is maintained in a strictly chemically defined, animal-derived component-free (ADCF) environment to mitigate the risk of Transmissible Spongiform Encephalopathies (TSE) and Adventitious Viral Agents.

##### 3.2.S.2.3.3.1 GHS-Basal-Medium-V4 (Batch Series: GLUC-2025-BM)
This medium is a proprietary formulation optimized for high-density perfusion culture.

**Table 1: Specifications for GHS-Basal-Medium-V4**
| Parameter | Test Method | Acceptance Criteria | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (SOP-QC-001) | Clear, pale yellow liquid | Identity/Physical State |
| **pH** | USP <791> | 7.10 – 7.40 | Cellular Homeostasis |
| **Osmolality** | USP <785> | 290 – 330 mOsm/kg | Tonicity Control |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> (LAL) | ≤ 0.25 EU/mL | Pyrogen Control |
| **Sterility** | USP <71> | No growth (14 days) | Aseptic Integrity |
| **Glucose Conc.** | HPLC-RI (SOP-QC-442) | 5.50 – 6.50 g/L | Primary Carbon Source |
| **L-Glutamine** | UPLC-UV | 4.0 – 5.0 mM | Nitrogen Source |
| **Growth Assay** | SOP-CELL-089 | ≥ 90% of Reference Standard | Biological Function |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.4 Specifications for Downstream Processing (DSP) Reagents
The purification of Glucogen-XR utilizes a multi-step chromatographic approach. The reagents used in these steps must meet stringent purity profiles to prevent the introduction of elemental impurities or microbial contaminants.

##### 3.2.S.2.3.4.1 Guanidine Hydrochloride (Denaturant)
Used during the initial solubilization phase of the inclusion bodies (if applicable) or for cleaning-in-place (CIP) of resins.

**Table 2: Specification Sheet – Guanidine HCl (High Purity Grade)**
*Batch Identifier Format: GLUC-2025-GHC-XXX*

| Test Parameter | Specification Limit | Methodology |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Assay (Dry Basis)** | 99.5% – 100.5% | Titration |
| **Absorbance (260nm)** | ≤ 0.050 AU (6M solution) | UV-Vis |
| **Absorbance (280nm)** | ≤ 0.030 AU (6M solution) | UV-Vis |
| **Lead (Pb)** | ≤ 0.1 ppm | ICP-MS (USP <232>) |
| **Iron (Fe)** | ≤ 0.5 ppm | ICP-MS (USP <233>) |
| **Melting Point** | 184°C – 188°C | USP <741> |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.5 Raw Material Sampling and Qualification Protocol (SOP-RM-2025-01)
Google Health Sciences employs a rigorous statistical sampling plan based on **ANSI/ASQ Z1.4**.

##### Step-by-Step Receiving and Testing Procedure:
1.  **Quarantine:** Upon arrival at the 3000 Innovation Drive receiving dock, materials are inspected for container integrity and logged into the Cloud-based LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System).
2.  **Decontamination:** Outer packaging is sanitized with 70% Isopropyl Alcohol (IPA) before transfer to the ISO 8 sampling suite.
3.  **Sampling (The $\sqrt{n}+1$ Rule):** 
    *   For $n$ containers, the number of sampled containers is calculated as $S = \sqrt{n} + 1$.
    *   *Calculation Example:* For a shipment of 100 drums of Sodium Chloride (GLUC-2025-NaCl-100), $S = \sqrt{100} + 1 = 11$ containers sampled.
4.  **Testing:** Samples are composite-tested for chemical attributes, while individual containers are tested for **Identity** via Near-Infrared (NIR) Spectroscopy (USP <1119>).
5.  **Disposition:** Materials meeting all specifications are labeled with a green "RELEASED" tag and moved to the temperature-controlled GMP warehouse.

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.6 Vendor Qualification and Supplier Quality Management
Google Health Sciences utilizes a "Dual-Sourcing" strategy for all Critical Raw Materials (CRMs) to ensure supply chain resilience.

**Table 3: Approved Supplier List (Excerpt)**
| Material Code | Material Name | Primary Vendor | Secondary Vendor | Audit Frequency |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| RM-001 | CHO-Media-V4 | Thermo Fisher (Gibco) | BioPharma KGaA | 24 Months |
| RM-042 | Protein A Resin | Cytiva | Repligen | 36 Months |
| RM-088 | Glucogen-Linker-01 | GHS Synthetic Chem | Evonik | 12 Months |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.7 Compendial Cross-Reference for Excipients
The following table summarizes the adherence to global pharmacopeias for standard chemicals used in the Glucogen-XR process.

**Table 4: Compendial Compliance Matrix**
| Material | CAS Number | USP/NF Monograph | EP Monograph | JP Monograph |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Sucrose** | 57-50-1 | Sucrose | Sucrosum | Sucrose |
| **L-Histidine** | 71-00-1 | Histidine | Histidinum | L-Histidine |
| **Polysorbate 20** | 9005-64-5 | Polysorbate 20 | Polysorbatum 20 | Polysorbate 20 |
| **WFI** | 7732-18-5 | Water for Inj. | Aqua ad Inject. | Water for Inj. |

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.8 Novel Reagents and Processing Aids
For the extended-release mechanism of Glucogen-XR, a proprietary PEGylated linker (GHS-PEG-20K) is utilized. This material is not described in any pharmacopeia.

##### 3.2.S.2.3.8.1 Specification for GHS-PEG-20K
*Function: Covalent attachment to glucapeptide backbone to increase hydrodynamic radius and half-life.*

1.  **Molecular Weight Distribution (Mn):** 19,000 – 21,000 Da (MALDI-TOF)
2.  **Polydispersity Index (PDI):** ≤ 1.05
3.  **Active Functional Group Substitution:** ≥ 98% (by 1H-NMR)
4.  **Residual Solvents:** 
    *   Toluene ≤ 890 ppm (ICH Q3C Class 2)
    *   Methanol ≤ 3000 ppm (ICH Q3C Class 2)
5.  **Heavy Metals:** ≤ 10 ppm (Total)

---

#### 3.2.S.2.3.9 Change Control and Deviations
Any modification to the raw material specifications or change in the manufacturing site of a supplier must be managed through the **GHS Global Change Control Protocol (GCP-2025-001)**. 

*   **Minor Changes:** Change in packaging size (e.g., 10kg to 25kg) without change in material contact surface. Requires notification only.
*   **Major Changes:** Change in the chemical synthesis route of a reagent. Requires a 3-batch comparability study and potential stability testing of the Drug Substance (ICH Q5E).

#### 3.2.S.2.3.10 Conclusion
The controls established for the raw materials of Glucogen-XR ensure that every component entering the manufacturing stream at Google Health Sciences is of the highest quality. By integrating USP/EP/JP standards with proprietary GHS-Cloud monitoring of supplier performance, we mitigate risks to the patient and ensure the consistent production of this critical GLP-1 therapy.

## Bovine-Derived Materials Control

### **3.2.S.2.3. Control of Materials**
#### **3.2.S.2.3.2. Bovine-Derived Materials Control Strategy and Viral Safety Assessment**

---

### **1.0 Introduction and Scope**
This subsection provides an exhaustive technical analysis and safety assessment of all bovine-derived materials utilized in the manufacturing process of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), an innovative GLP-1 receptor agonist produced by Google Health Sciences. 

In accordance with **ICH Q5A(R2)** (*Quality of Biotechnological Products: Viral Safety Evaluation*), **ICH Q5D** (*Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates*), and **EMA/410/01 Rev. 3** (*Minimizing the risk of transmitting animal spongiform encephalopathy agents via human and veterinary medicinal products*), Google Health Sciences has implemented a multi-layered containment and qualification strategy. 

The primary bovine-derived material used in the production of Glucogen-XR is **Fetal Bovine Serum (FBS)**, utilized exclusively during the initial stages of Master Cell Bank (MCB) and Working Cell Bank (WCB) development of the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line. All subsequent upstream manufacturing (Seed Train, N-1, and Production Bioreactor phases) utilizes strictly **Chemically Defined, Animal-Derived Component-Free (CD-ADCF)** media.

---

### **2.0 Regulatory Framework and Compliance Standards**
The control strategy for Glucogen-XR bovine materials adheres to the following global regulatory standards:

*   **21 CFR 610.18:** Establishment of Cell Lines and Control of Materials.
*   **USP <1024>:** Bovine Serum—Model Program for Control and Monitoring.
*   **USP <9999>:** Traceability of Animal-Derived Materials.
*   **9 CFR 113.46-53:** USDA requirements for testing bovine biologicals for viruses (BVDV, IBR, PI3, BPV, BRSV, Rabies, Reovirus).
*   **Note for Guidance EMA/410/01 Rev. 3:** Minimizing the risk of TSE/BSE transmission.
*   **EP 5.2.12:** Raw materials of biological origin for the production of cell-based and gene therapy medicinal products.

---

### **3.0 Detailed Material Specifications: Fetal Bovine Serum (FBS)**

#### **3.1 Source and Traceability (Origin Control)**
Google Health Sciences mandates that all FBS used in the derivation of GHS-CHO-001 originates from "BSE-Negligible Risk" countries as defined by the World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH, formerly OIE).

**Table 1: Material Identification and Sourcing Profile**

| Material Name | Manufacturer Part No. | Supplier (Location) | Geographical Origin | TSE Risk Category (EMA/410/01) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **FBS Premium Grade** | GHS-FBS-9922 | GHS Global Biologics (NZ) | New Zealand | Category C (Negligible) |
| **FBS Supplemental** | GHS-FBS-9925 | Bio-Logic Australia | Australia | Category C (Negligible) |

#### **3.2 Batch Selection and Specification Limits**
The following table details the analytical specifications for the FBS batch (Lot: **GLUC-2025-FBS-001**) utilized for the generation of the Glucogen-XR Master Cell Bank.

**Table 2: Quality Control Specifications for FBS Lot GLUC-2025-FBS-001**

| Test Parameter | Methodology | Acceptance Criteria | Result (Batch GLUC-2025-FBS-001) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> (LAL) | ≤ 5.0 EU/mL | 0.82 EU/mL |
| **Hemoglobin** | Spectrophotometric | ≤ 15 mg/dL | 8.4 mg/dL |
| **Total Protein** | Biuret Method | 3.0 – 5.0 g/dL | 3.8 g/dL |
| **Osmolality** | Freezing Point | 280 – 340 mOsm/kg | 312 mOsm/kg |
| **pH** | USP <791> | 6.8 – 8.2 | 7.42 |
| **Mycoplasma** | USP <63> (Culture/DNA) | Negative | Negative |
| **Sterility** | USP <71> | No Growth (14 days) | No Growth |
| **BVDV** | 9 CFR 113 | Not Detected | Not Detected |
| **Bovine Polyomavirus** | qPCR (GHS-SOP-09) | Not Detected | Not Detected |

---

### **4.0 Viral Inactivation and Clearance Protocols**

#### **4.1 Gamma Irradiation Process**
All FBS undergoes validated Gamma Irradiation to ensure a Sterility Assurance Level (SAL) of $10^{-6}$ for viruses and contaminating microbes.

**Irradiation Parameters:**
*   **Target Dose Range:** 25.0 – 40.0 kGy.
*   **Actual Dose Received (GLUC-2025-FBS-001):** 31.2 – 34.8 kGy.
*   **Equipment ID:** Cobalt-60 Gamma Cell Sterilizer (GHS-EQ-998).
*   **Exposure Time Calculation:** $T = D_{target} / R_{dose}$, where $R$ is the decay-corrected dose rate.

**Table 3: Gamma Irradiation Validation Data (Log Reduction Factors)**

| Target Virus | Family | Genome | Size (nm) | Log₁₀ Reduction (at 25 kGy) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **BVDV** | Flaviviridae | ssRNA | 40-60 | ≥ 5.2 |
| **PI3** | Paramyxoviridae | ssRNA | 150-250 | ≥ 6.1 |
| **IBR** | Herpesviridae | dsDNA | 150-200 | ≥ 4.9 |
| **PPV** | Parvoviridae | ssDNA | 18-26 | ≥ 3.5 |

---

### **5.0 TSE/BSE Risk Mitigation Strategy**

#### **5.1 Tissue Risk Categorization**
As per the EMA/410/01 Rev. 3 guidelines, FBS is classified as a material with **no detectable infectivity** (Category C). However, the risk of cross-contamination during the abattoir collection process is mitigated through the following standard operating procedures:

1.  **Closed System Collection:** FBS is harvested via cardiac puncture in a closed system to prevent environmental or nervous tissue contamination.
2.  **Age Restriction:** Donor animals are fetuses derived from dams that have passed both ante-mortem and post-mortem inspections by New Zealand Ministry for Primary Industries (MPI) veterinarians.
3.  **Audit Trail:** Google Health Sciences Quality Assurance (QA) performs biennial on-site audits of the New Zealand processing facilities.

#### **5.2 Certificate of Suitability (CEP)**
The supplier holds a valid CEP (Certificate of Suitability to the Monographs of the European Pharmacopoeia) for the FBS used: **CEP No. R0-CEP 2021-XXX-Rev 00**.

---

### **6.0 Manufacturing Process Control (Upstream)**

#### **6.1 Step-by-Step Bovine Material Removal Protocol**
While FBS is used for the GHS-CHO-001 cell line establishment, a rigorous "Weaning Protocol" is implemented to ensure the final Drug Substance is ADCF.

**Protocol GHS-PRO-DS-0012: Serum-Free Adaptation**
1.  **Stage 1 (10% FBS):** Thaw MCB vial into 90% GHS-Proprietary Base Media + 10% FBS.
2.  **Stage 2 (5% FBS):** Passaging at $0.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL into 50:50 mix of serum-containing and CD-ADCF media.
3.  **Stage 3 (1% FBS):** Passaging when viability > 95%.
4.  **Stage 4 (0% FBS):** Final adaptation into 100% CD-ADCF Chemically Defined Media (Lot: **GLUC-2025-MED-001**).

#### **6.2 Calculation of Dilution Factor of Bovine Components**
The theoretical concentration of FBS in the final 2000L Production Bioreactor is calculated using the following cumulative dilution formula:

$$C_{final} = \frac{V_{initial} \times C_{initial}}{\prod_{i=1}^{n} DF_i}$$

Where:
*   $V_{initial}$ = 10 mL (vial volume)
*   $C_{initial}$ = 10% (0.1)
*   $DF_i$ = Dilution factors across Seed Train (N-4 to N-1).

For Glucogen-XR, the calculated residual FBS concentration at the start of the 2000L production phase is **$< 1.0 \times 10^{-15} \%$**, effectively representing a bovine-free environment.

---

### **7.0 Analytical Testing for Residual Bovine Impurities**

To ensure the safety of Glucogen-XR, Google Health Sciences utilizes a high-sensitivity Bovine Serum Albumin (BSA) ELISA and a Bovine IgG assay on the Unprocessed Bulk (UPB).

**Table 4: Residual Bovine Impurity Testing (Drug Substance Batches)**

| Batch Number | Test: Residual BSA (ng/mg) | Test: Residual Bovine IgG (ng/mg) | Method Detection Limit (LOD) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | < LOD | < LOD | 0.5 ng/mg |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | < LOD | < LOD | 0.5 ng/mg |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | < LOD | < LOD | 0.5 ng/mg |

---

### **8.0 Risk Assessment Conclusion**
The risk of adventitious agent transmission (viral or TSE) via bovine-derived materials in the production of Glucogen-XR is deemed **negligible**. This conclusion is based on:
1.  **Geographical Sourcing:** Only New Zealand/Australia origin materials.
2.  **Rigorous Processing:** Validated Gamma Irradiation (25-40 kGy).
3.  **Process Dilution:** A $10^{15}$-fold dilution of serum-containing media during the seed train.
4.  **Analytical Verification:** No detectable bovine protein in the final Drug Substance.

---
**References:**
1.  *GHS Internal Report R-DS-2024-08: Validation of Viral Clearance for Glucogen-XR Process.*
2.  *FDA Guidance for Industry: Characterization and Qualification of Cell Substrates (2010).*
3.  *World Organisation for Animal Health (WOAH) Terrestrial Animal Health Code, Chapter 11.4.*

## Vendor Qualification

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE
### 3.2.S.2: MANUFACTURE
#### 3.2.S.2.3: CONTROL OF MATERIALS
##### 3.2.S.2.3.1: Vendor Qualification and Management Program

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This subsection details the comprehensive Vendor Qualification Program (VQP) established by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)**, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences, for the production of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**. In alignment with **ICH Q7** (*Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients*) and **ICH Q10** (*Pharmaceutical Quality System*), GHS maintains a rigorous risk-based oversight framework to ensure that all raw materials, starting materials, reagents, and primary packaging components meet the stringent purity and safety requirements necessary for a biologic GLP-1 receptor agonist produced in the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line.

The qualification process described herein applies to all vendors providing critical materials used in the manufacture of Glucogen-XR at the 3000 Innovation Drive facility in South San Francisco, CA.

---

### 2.0 REGULATORY FRAMEWORK AND QUALITY STANDARDS

The Vendor Qualification Program is designed to comply with the following global regulatory requirements and industry standards:

1.  **21 CFR Part 211.84:** Testing and approval or rejection of components, drug product containers, and closures.
2.  **21 CFR Part 600:** Biological Products: General.
3.  **ICH Q8 (R2):** Pharmaceutical Development.
4.  **ICH Q9 (R1):** Quality Risk Management.
5.  **ICH Q11:** Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances.
6.  **USP <1043>:** Ancillary Materials for Cell, Gene, and Tissue-Engineered Products.
7.  **USP <1059>:** Excipient Performance.
8.  **EMA/410/01:** Note for Guidance on Minimising the Risk of Transmitting Animal Spongiform Encephalopathy Agents via Human and Veterinary Medicinal Products.

---

### 3.0 MATERIAL CRITICALITY CLASSIFICATION

Prior to vendor engagement, Google Health Sciences performs a **Material Criticality Assessment (MCA)**. Materials are categorized into three tiers (Tier 1 to Tier 3) based on their impact on the final Quality Target Product Profile (QTPP) of Glucogen-XR.

#### Table 1: Material Criticality and Qualification Requirements

| Material Category | Description | Examples | Qualification Requirements |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Tier 1: Critical** | High impact on safety, purity, or potency. Direct contact with DS. | GHS-CHO-001 Media, Protein A Resin, Glucapeptide Linkers. | Full Audit, 3-Batch CoA Verification, TSE/BSE Certification, Stability Data. |
| **Tier 2: Intermediate** | Moderate impact. Used in purification or formulation. | USP Grade Salts, Buffers, Viral Filters. | Paper Audit/Questionnaire, 1-Batch CoA Verification. |
| **Tier 3: Non-Critical** | Low impact. Indirect contact or general lab supplies. | Cleaning Agents (CIP), Lubricants, WFI. | Supplier Certification, Certificate of Conformance (CoC). |

---

### 4.0 VENDOR QUALIFICATION WORKFLOW (PROTOCOL VQP-GS-2025)

The qualification of a new supplier for Glucogen-XR follows a standardized 6-step protocol.

#### 4.1 Step 1: Preliminary Selection and Business Review
The Global Procurement and Quality Assurance (QA) teams evaluate the vendor’s financial stability, capacity to scale for commercial Glucogen-XR demand, and historical performance in the peptide therapeutics sector.

#### 4.2 Step 2: Quality Questionnaire and Documentation Package
Potential Tier 1 and Tier 2 vendors must submit a Comprehensive Supplier Information Package (CSIP), including:
*   ISO 9001:2015 or ISO 13485 certifications.
*   Site Master File (SMF).
*   Organizational Chart (Quality Unit reporting structure).
*   TSE/BSE Statements (compliant with USP <1024>).
*   Melamine-free and Nitrosamine Risk Assessment statements.

#### 4.3 Step 3: On-Site Quality Audit (Specific to Glucogen-XR)
For Tier 1 vendors (e.g., manufacturers of the proprietary GLP-1 synthetic peptide fragments), a 3-day on-site audit is mandatory.
*   **Audit Focus Areas:** Material traceability, change control (ICH Q10), deviation management, and data integrity (ALCOA+ principles).
*   **Equipment ID Verification:** Auditors verify that equipment used for GHS lots (e.g., HPLC-0982, Lyophilizer-LYO-44) is qualified (IQ/OQ/PQ).

#### 4.4 Step 4: Analytical Qualification and CoA Verification
GHS performs "Split-Sample Testing." Samples from three (3) distinct lots are sent to GHS South San Francisco for full compendial and functional testing to verify the vendor's Certificate of Analysis (CoA).

##### Table 2: Analytical Verification Data for GLUC-2025-REAGENT-01 (Proprietary Media Supplement)

| Parameter | Method | Vendor Results (Lot #V-998) | GHS Verification (Batch GLUC-2025-001) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual | Clear, Straw Liquid | Clear, Straw Liquid | Pass |
| **pH** | USP <791> | 7.21 | 7.23 | Pass |
| **Osmolality** | USP <785> | 295 mOsm/kg | 298 mOsm/kg | Pass |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> | < 0.1 EU/mL | < 0.05 EU/mL | Pass |
| **Bioburden** | USP <61> | 0 CFU/10 mL | 0 CFU/10 mL | Pass |
| **Mycoplasma** | PCR | Negative | Negative | Pass |

#### 4.5 Step 5: Trial Production Run
Materials are introduced into a small-scale pilot run of Glucogen-XR (50L scale) to ensure the material performs as expected in the GHS-CHO-001 expression system.

#### 4.6 Step 6: Approved Supplier List (ASL) Entry
Upon successful completion of Steps 1-5, the vendor is added to the SAP-based Approved Supplier List (ASL) with a "Qualified" status.

---

### 5.0 RISK ASSESSMENT AND MITIGATION (ICH Q9)

Google Health Sciences utilizes a Failure Mode and Effects Analysis (FMEA) to assess vendor risk.

**Risk Priority Number (RPN) Calculation:**
$RPN = Severity (S) \times Occurrence (O) \times Detectability (D)$

*   **Severity:** 1 (Minor) to 10 (Patient Fatality).
*   **Occurrence:** 1 (Rare) to 10 (Frequent).
*   **Detectability:** 1 (Easy to detect at intake) to 10 (Undetectable).

#### Table 3: FMEA for Vendor-Supplied Critical Peptides

| Potential Failure Mode | S | O | D | RPN | Mitigation Strategy |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Impurity Profile Shift** | 8 | 2 | 3 | **48** | Mandatory HPLC profile comparison for every batch. |
| **TSE/BSE Contamination** | 10 | 1 | 9 | **90** | Strict sourcing from non-BSE regions; annual audit. |
| **Supply Chain Break** | 4 | 4 | 2 | **32** | Dual-sourcing strategy (Vendor A and Vendor B). |

---

### 6.0 ONGOING MONITORING AND RE-QUALIFICATION

#### 6.1 Annual Quality Review (AQR)
Every 12 months, QA generates a Vendor Scorecard based on:
1.  Number of lots received vs. lots rejected.
2.  On-time delivery performance.
3.  Responsiveness to Quality Notifications (QNs).

#### 6.2 Periodic Audits
*   **Tier 1:** On-site audit every 2 years.
*   **Tier 2:** Paper audit/questionnaire every 3 years.
*   **Tier 3:** Re-evaluation of certification every 5 years.

#### 6.3 Change Control (Management of Change)
Vendors are contractually obligated (via Quality Agreements) to notify Google Health Sciences of any changes to:
*   Manufacturing process or site.
*   Sub-tier suppliers of raw materials.
*   Specifications or analytical methods.
*   Key personnel (Quality Site Head).

---

# Expression System Overview

## Vector Construction and Characterization

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S. DRUG SUBSTANCE
### 3.2.S.2. MANUFACTURE
#### 3.2.S.2.3. CONTROL OF MATERIALS
#### SUBSECTION: EXPRESSION SYSTEM OVERVIEW – VECTOR CONSTRUCTION AND CHARACTERIZATION

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This subsection details the design, construction, sequence verification, and functional characterization of the expression vector **pGHS-GLUC-XR-098**, utilized for the production of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) in the proprietary Google Health Sciences (GHS) CHO-K1 GS-knockout (GHS-CHO-001) mammalian cell line. The development of this vector was conducted under stringent Quality by Design (QbD) principles to ensure long-term genetic stability, high-fidelity transcription, and robust secretion of the therapeutic peptide.

All molecular biology procedures were performed in compliance with **ICH Q5B** (*Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products*) and **ICH Q5D** (*Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products*).

---

### 2.0 VECTOR DESIGN STRATEGY

The pGHS-GLUC-XR-098 vector is a high-copy, mammalian expression plasmid (approx. 8.4 kb) specifically engineered for the Google Cloud Life Sciences automated bioprocessing pipeline. It utilizes a dual-promoter system to drive both the Gene of Interest (GOI) and the metabolic selection marker.

#### 2.1 Plasmid Map and Structural Elements
The vector comprises several modular "cassettes" designed for optimal performance in the GHS-CHO-001 host.

**Table 1: Genetic Elements of pGHS-GLUC-XR-098**

| Element ID | Feature Name | Source | Description/Function | Coordinates (bp) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| P-01 | hCMV IE1 Promoter | Human Cytomegalovirus | Ultra-strong constitutive promoter with Intron A for enhanced mRNA export. | 1 - 750 |
| L-01 | GHS-Leader-V4 | Synthetic | Proprietary signal peptide optimized for GLP-1 secretion efficiency in CHO cells. | 751 - 810 |
| GOI-01 | Glucapeptide-XR | Synthetic | Codon-optimized sequence for *Cricetulus griseus* (CHO). | 811 - 1245 |
| T-01 | bGH Poly(A) | Bovine Growth Hormone | High-efficiency polyadenylation signal for mRNA stability. | 1250 - 1460 |
| P-02 | SV40 Promoter | Simian Virus 40 | Drives the expression of the Glutamine Synthetase (GS) selection marker. | 2500 - 2850 |
| M-01 | GS cDNA | *Cricetulus griseus* | Glutamine Synthetase cDNA used for metabolic selection in GS-null cells. | 2860 - 4000 |
| O-01 | pUC Origin | *E. coli* | High-copy number origin for plasmid propagation in *E. coli*. | 5500 - 6200 |
| R-01 | AmpR | *E. coli* | Beta-lactamase gene for antibiotic selection during cloning (not present in final cell line). | 6500 - 7300 |

#### 2.2 Codon Optimization Methodology
The Glucogen-XR peptide sequence underwent a multi-parameter computational optimization via the **Google Cloud AI-Biologics Engine (v4.2)**. The goal was to eliminate "translational bottlenecks" and ensure high fidelity at high-density perfusion scales.

*   **Codon Adaptation Index (CAI):** Optimized from 0.64 (wild type) to 0.94 for CHO expression.
*   **GC Content:** Adjusted to 54% to minimize secondary structure formation in mRNA.
*   **Negative Elements Removed:**
    *   Internal TATA-boxes.
    *   Ribosomal binding sites (Shine-Dalgarno like sequences).
    *   Cryptic splice donor/acceptor sites.
    *   Repeats > 10bp.
    *   High-energy RNA hairpins (calculated $\Delta G > -20 \text{ kcal/mol}$).

---

### 3.0 VECTOR CONSTRUCTION PROTOCOL (PROCEDURE GHS-MOL-0045)

The construction of pGHS-GLUC-XR-098 followed a modular Gibson Assembly approach, ensuring scarless junctions between regulatory elements.

#### 3.1 Step-by-Step Assembly
1.  **Template Preparation:** The backbone was derived from the pGHS-Empty-GS vector, linearized using high-fidelity restriction enzymes *NheI* and *XbaI* (New England Biolabs, Cat# R3131M/R0145M).
2.  **Insert Synthesis:** The Glucogen-XR GOI was synthesized *de novo* by a qualified vendor (Batch ID: SYN-99021) with flanking 25bp homology arms.
3.  **Assembly Reaction:**
    *   Linearized Vector (50 ng)
    *   Purified Insert (15 ng)
    *   Gibson Assembly Master Mix (2X)
    *   Incubation: 50°C for 60 minutes.
4.  **Transformation:** 2 $\mu$L of the assembly reaction was transformed into chemically competent *E. coli* NEB 5-alpha (Batch: EC-2024-001).
5.  **Selection:** Cells were plated on LB agar supplemented with 100 $\mu$g/mL Ampicillin and incubated at 37°C for 16 hours.

#### 3.2 Screening and Verification
Initial screening was performed via Colony PCR using primers GHS-F1 (5'-CTGGGCGTGGAGCATCTG-3') and GHS-R1 (5'-GTCCAGCTTGTTCCCGTAG-3').

**Table 2: Representative Colony PCR Results (Batch: GLUC-2025-VC01)**

| Clone ID | Result (Band Size) | Expected Size | Outcome |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| CL-01 | 480 bp | 480 bp | Positive |
| CL-02 | 480 bp | 480 bp | Positive |
| CL-03 | No band | 480 bp | Negative |
| CL-04 | 480 bp | 480 bp | Positive |

---

### 4.0 CHARACTERIZATION AND QUALITY CONTROL

Prior to transfection into the GHS-CHO-001 host, the lead vector (Clone CL-01) underwent exhaustive characterization.

#### 4.1 Full-Length Sequence Verification (Sanger and NGS)
The entire 8.4 kb plasmid was sequenced using an overlapping primer walking strategy. Additionally, Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS) was performed on an Illumina MiSeq platform to ensure the absence of low-frequency variants or deletions.

*   **Acceptance Criteria:** 100% homology to the theoretical *in silico* map.
*   **Results:** No mutations, deletions, or insertions detected. Sequence coverage: 5000x depth.

#### 4.2 Restriction Enzyme Mapping (Fingerprinting)
To confirm structural integrity, the vector was digested with a panel of enzymes.

**Table 3: Restriction Digest Analysis (Batch: GLUC-2025-VC01)**

| Enzyme | Theoretical Fragments (bp) | Observed Fragments (bp) | Compliance |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| *EcoRI* | 8432 | 8435 | Pass |
| *HindIII* | 5200, 3232 | 5205, 3230 | Pass |
| *PstI* | 4100, 2100, 1500, 732 | 4102, 2098, 1499, 735 | Pass |

#### 4.3 Purity and Physicochemical Properties
The plasmid DNA for transfection was prepared using a validated Endo-Free Giga Prep process (Procedure GHS-PUR-09).

**Table 4: Vector Purity Specifications**

| Test Parameter | Specification | Result (Batch GLUC-2025-VC01) | Method |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Appearance | Clear, colorless liquid | Complies | Visual |
| Concentration | $\ge 1.0 \text{ mg/mL}$ | 2.15 mg/mL | A260 |
| A260/A280 | 1.8 - 2.0 | 1.89 | Spectrophotometry |
| Supercoiled DNA | $\ge 90\%$ | 94.2% | AGE / HPLC |
| Endotoxin | $< 0.1 \text{ EU/}\mu\text{g}$ | 0.04 EU/$\mu$g | LAL (USP <85>) |
| Residual Protein | Report | 0.2% | BCA Assay |

---

### 5.0 GENETIC STABILITY AND INTEGRATION ANALYSIS

In alignment with **ICH Q5B**, the stability of the expression construct within the GHS-CHO-001 host was evaluated across the "Limit of In Vitro Cell Age" (LIVCA).

#### 5.1 Copy Number Determination by qPCR
The copy number of the integrated pGHS-GLUC-XR-098 vector was determined relative to a single-copy endogenous CHO gene (*Glucagon Receptor*).

**Calculation Formula:**
$$ \text{Copy Number} = 2 \times 2^{-\Delta \Delta C_t} $$
Where $\Delta \Delta C_t = (C_{t, \text{GOI}} - C_{t, \text{Ref}})_{\text{Sample}} - (C_{t, \text{GOI}} - C_{t, \text{Ref}})_{\text{Calibrator}}$.

**Table 5: Vector Copy Number (VCN) during Stability Studies**

| Sample Stage | Passage | VCN (per cell) | SD ($n=3$) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Master Cell Bank (MCB) | P5 | 12.4 | 0.4 |
| Working Cell Bank (WCB) | P12 | 12.2 | 0.3 |
| LIVCA (End of Production) | P45 | 11.9 | 0.5 |

*Note: The stability of the VCN (variance <10%) confirms the robustness of the GS selection system and the lack of genetic drift during large-scale cultivation.*

---

### 6.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE STATEMENT

The design, construction, and characterization of the pGHS-GLUC-XR-098 expression vector comply with all current FDA expectations for biologics license applications (BLA). The use of synthetic, animal-derived-component-free (ADCF) materials in the construction ensures a high safety profile. All raw data, chromatograms, and NGS files are archived under GLP conditions at the Google Health Sciences repository (South San Francisco, CA).

## Copy Number and Integration Site

### **3.2.S.2.3. Control of Materials**
#### **Section: Expression System Overview**
#### **Subsection: 3.2.S.2.3.2. Copy Number and Integration Site Analysis**

---

### **1. Introduction and Scope**
The stability and consistency of the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) production process are fundamentally dependent on the genetic architecture of the Google Health Sciences proprietary CHO-K1 GS-knockout (GHS-CHO-001) production cell line. This section provides a comprehensive characterization of the transgene copy number (TCN) and the genomic integration site(s) of the expression vector pGHS-GLUC-XR-099.

In accordance with **ICH Guideline Q5B** (*Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products*) and **ICH Q5D** (*Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products*), Google Health Sciences has performed rigorous molecular characterization to ensure that the genetic profile of the Master Cell Bank (MCB), Working Cell Bank (WCB), and End-of-Production Cells (EOPC) remains stable across the validated lifespan of the culture.

---

### **2. Determination of Transgene Copy Number (TCN)**

#### **2.1. Methodological Overview: Droplet Digital PCR (ddPCR)**
To achieve the highest level of precision and absolute quantification without the need for standard curves (as required by traditional qPCR), Google Health Sciences utilized **Droplet Digital PCR (ddPCR)**. This method partitions the genomic DNA (gDNA) into approximately 20,000 discrete oil-water droplets, where individual PCR reactions occur.

*   **Target Gene:** *GLUC-XR* synthetic cDNA (Sequence ID: GHS-SQ-2024-01).
*   **Reference Gene:** *Glucokinase (Gck)*, a single-copy gene in the *Cricetulus griseus* genome (CHO-K1).
*   **Equipment:** Bio-Rad QX200™ Droplet Digital™ PCR System (Equipment ID: GHS-EQ-PCR-09).

#### **2.2. Detailed Analytical Protocol (SOP-GHS-MOL-442)**

**Step 1: Genomic DNA Extraction**
1.  Aliquots of $1 \times 10^7$ cells are harvested from the MCB (Batch: GLUC-2025-MCB01) and WCB (Batch: GLUC-2025-WCB01).
2.  Lysis is performed using a proteinase K-based buffer system (GHS-Buff-99) followed by silica-column purification.
3.  DNA concentration is measured via Fluorometric quantification (Qubit 4.0). Required $A_{260}/A_{280}$ ratio: $1.8–2.0$.

**Step 2: DNA Fragmentation (Restriction Digestion)**
1.  To ensure random distribution in droplets and to separate tandem repeats, gDNA is digested with *HaeIII* (NEB Catalog #R0108S).
2.  Digest reaction: 500 ng gDNA, 10 U *HaeIII*, $37^\circ\text{C}$ for 60 minutes.
3.  Note: *HaeIII* does not have recognition sites within the *GLUC-XR* expression cassette or the *Gck* reference sequence.

**Step 3: Droplet Generation and Amplification**
1.  Reaction Mix: $2\times$ ddPCR Supermix, 900 nM Primers (GHS-F1/R1), 250 nM Probe (FAM-labeled for GLUC; HEX-labeled for Gck).
2.  Droplets are generated using the QX200 Droplet Generator.
3.  Thermal Cycling: 10 min @ $95^\circ\text{C}$; 40 cycles of ($94^\circ\text{C}$ for 30s, $60^\circ\text{C}$ for 60s); 10 min @ $98^\circ\text{C}$ (deactivation).

**Step 4: Calculations**
The copy number is calculated using the following formula:
$$TCN = \left( \frac{C_{target}}{C_{ref}} \right) \times N_{ref}$$
Where:
*   $C_{target}$ = Copies/µL of *GLUC-XR*
*   $C_{ref}$ = Copies/µL of *Gck*
*   $N_{ref}$ = 2 (Assuming diploidy for the reference locus in CHO-K1 derivative)

#### **2.3. Results: Copy Number Stability across Batches**

Table 1 summarizes the TCN data across the cell banking hierarchy and the End-of-Production cells from three representative commercial-scale validation batches.

**Table 1: Transgene Copy Number (TCN) Consistency Data**

| Sample ID | Batch Number | Description | Mean TCN (Copies/Cell) | Std. Deviation (n=6) | % CV |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GHS-MCB-01** | GLUC-2025-MCB01 | Master Cell Bank | 8.42 | 0.21 | 2.49% |
| **GHS-WCB-01** | GLUC-2025-WCB01 | Working Cell Bank | 8.39 | 0.18 | 2.15% |
| **GHS-EOP-01** | GLUC-2025-BAT-001 | EOPC (Limit of In Vitro Cell Age) | 8.35 | 0.25 | 2.99% |
| **GHS-EOP-02** | GLUC-2025-BAT-002 | EOPC (Limit of In Vitro Cell Age) | 8.40 | 0.19 | 2.26% |
| **GHS-EOP-03** | GLUC-2025-BAT-003 | EOPC (Limit of In Vitro Cell Age) | 8.44 | 0.22 | 2.61% |

**Interpretation:** The data demonstrates that the Glucogen-XR expression cassette is integrated at a low-to-moderate copy number ($\approx 8$ copies per cell), which minimizes the metabolic burden on the GHS-CHO-001 host and reduces the risk of gene silencing. The stability of the TCN from MCB to EOPC confirms genetic fidelity during scale-up.

---

### **3. Integration Site Characterization**

#### **3.1. Targeted Locus: The GHS-SafeHarbor-04 Site**
Unlike random integration methods, Glucogen-XR utilizes a site-specific integration strategy mediated by a proprietary Google Health Sciences CRISPR/Cas9-based system. The transgene is targeted to the **GHS-SafeHarbor-04** locus on Chromosome 4 of the *Cricetulus griseus* genome.

*   **Genomic Coordinates:** Chr4: 245,102,441 - 245,103,100 (Assembly: CHOK1GS_HDv1).
*   **Rationale:** This region is characterized by high transcriptional activity (euchromatin) and is located $>50$ kb away from any known proto-oncogenes or microRNA clusters.

#### **3.2. Integration Site Analysis by Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS)**
To confirm the site of integration and rule out off-target insertions, **Targeted Locus Amplification (TLA)** followed by Illumina HiSeq sequencing was performed.

**Protocol for TLA-Sequencing (SOP-GHS-NGS-102):**
1.  **Cross-linking:** Cells are fixed with formaldehyde to preserve 3D chromatin structure.
2.  **Digestion:** DNA is digested with a frequent cutter (*NlaIII*).
3.  **Ligation:** Circularization of DNA fragments.
4.  **Inverse PCR:** Primers specific to the *GLUC-XR* promoter (CMV-derived GHS-P2) amplify the entire integrated cassette and several kilobases of flanking genomic DNA.
5.  **Library Prep:** Fragmentation and adapter ligation for Illumina sequencing.

#### **3.3. Results of Integration Site Mapping**

**Table 2: NGS Mapping of Integration Flanking Regions (MCB GLUC-2025-MCB01)**

| Junction | Genomic Sequence (5' $\rightarrow$ 3') | Vector Sequence (5' $\rightarrow$ 3') | Mapping Confidence |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **5' Flank** | ...TTCAGGTACGATCGA... | ...ATGGCCAGCTGC... (5' ITR) | 99.98% |
| **3' Flank** | ...CGGATCGATAGCTAG... | ...GCTAGCTAGCTA... (3' ITR) | 99.96% |

**Analysis of Results:**
*   **Primary Site:** 100% of high-quality reads mapped to the GHS-SafeHarbor-04 locus.
*   **Off-Target Sites:** No secondary integration sites were detected at a sensitivity level of 0.1% (LOD).
*   **Structural Integrity:** The sequencing data confirms that the head-to-tail tandem arrangement of the 8 copies remains intact at the single locus on Chromosome 4.

---

### **4. Fluorescence In Situ Hybridization (FISH)**

To visualize the integration site at the chromosomal level and confirm clonal purity, FISH analysis was performed on metaphase spreads of the MCB.

#### **4.1. FISH Methodology**
*   **Probe A (Target):** Biotin-labeled DNA probe spanning the 5.2 kb *GLUC-XR* expression cassette.
*   **Probe B (Control):** Digoxigenin-labeled probe for the centromere of Chromosome 4.
*   **Detection:** Streptavidin-Alexa Fluor 488 (Green) for Target; Anti-Digoxigenin-Rhodamine (Red) for Control.

#### **4.2. Observation Data**
Analysis of 200 metaphase spreads from batch **GLUC-2025-MCB01**:
*   **Signal Localization:** 100% of cells showed a single, distinct green fluorescent signal on the long arm (q-arm) of Chromosome 4.
*   **Polyploidy Check:** 98% of the population maintained the expected chromosome count (2n=22 for CHO-K1), with no translocations involving the integration site observed.

---

### **5. Genetic Stability and Regulatory Compliance**

#### **5.1. Impact of In Vitro Cell Age (IVCA)**
Stability testing was conducted up to Generation 85 (G85), which exceeds the production limit of Generation 60 (G60) used for the 2,000L bioreactor scale.

**Table 3: Long-term Genetic Stability Analysis**

| Parameter | MCB (G0) | EOPC (G60) | Extended Study (G85) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **TCN (copies/cell)** | 8.42 | 8.35 | 8.29 |
| **mRNA Expression (Rel.)** | 1.00 | 0.98 | 0.96 |
| **Integration Site (NGS)** | Confirmed | Confirmed | Confirmed |
| **Phenotypic Stability** | Pass | Pass | Pass |

#### **5.2. Conclusion on Copy Number and Integration**
The molecular characterization of Glucogen-XR confirms that the production cell line GHS-CHO-001 contains approximately **8 copies** of the transgene, stably integrated into the **GHS-SafeHarbor-04** locus on Chromosome 4. This genetic configuration is maintained across the entire production lifecycle, ensuring consistent product quality and yield for all commercial batches (GLUC-2025-XXX).
