## Expression Levels and Stability

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA SUMMARY)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.3: CONTROL OF MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: EXPRESSION LEVELS AND GENETIC STABILITY

---

## 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This subsection provides a comprehensive evaluation of the expression levels and genetic stability of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line utilized for the production of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). In accordance with **ICH Q5B (Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products)** and **ICH Q5D (Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products)**, Google Health Sciences has conducted rigorous longitudinal studies to ensure that the production phenotype and the integrity of the expression construct remain constant from the Research Cell Bank (RCB) through the Master Cell Bank (MCB), Working Cell Bank (WCB), and beyond the Limit of In Vitro Cell Age (LIVCA) for commercial production.

Glucogen-XR is expressed as a synthetic GLP-1 receptor agonist peptide fused to a proprietary solubility-enhancing and half-life extending polypeptide chain. The expression system leverages the Glutamine Synthetase (GS) knockout CHO-K1 derivative, utilizing methionine sulfoximine (MSX) selection to achieve high-titer, stable integration.

---

## 2.0 EXPRESSION LEVEL ANALYSIS (PRODUCTIVITY)

### 2.1 Methodology for Determination of Specific Productivity (Qp)
The volumetric productivity ($P_v$) and cell-specific productivity ($Q_p$) were calculated across multiple scales (5L, 50L, 500L, and 2000L) to demonstrate scalability and stability.

**Mathematical Formulas Applied:**
The Specific Productivity ($Q_p$) is calculated as the integral of viable cell density (IVCD) over time:
$$Q_p = \frac{P_{final} - P_{initial}}{\int_{t_0}^{t_f} X_v \, dt}$$
Where:
- $P$ = Product concentration (mg/L)
- $X_v$ = Viable cell density (cells/mL)
- $t$ = Time (days)

### 2.2 Table of Productivity Data (Clinical and Registration Batches)
The following data represents the performance of the Glucogen-XR expression system across key manufacturing milestones.

| Batch Number | Scale (L) | Peak VCD ($10^6$ cells/mL) | Viability at Harvest (%) | Final Titer (g/L) | Calculated $Q_p$ (pg/cell/day) |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 50L (Pilot) | 22.4 | 92.1 | 4.85 | 32.5 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 50L (Pilot) | 21.9 | 91.5 | 4.78 | 31.9 |
| **GLUC-2025-005** | 500L (Eng) | 23.1 | 90.8 | 5.12 | 33.1 |
| **GLUC-2025-010** | 2000L (GMP) | 24.5 | 89.5 | 5.45 | 34.2 |
| **GLUC-2025-011** | 2000L (GMP) | 24.2 | 89.9 | 5.41 | 33.8 |
| **GLUC-2025-012** | 2000L (GMP) | 24.8 | 88.7 | 5.52 | 34.5 |

**Note:** All batches utilized Google Health Sciences proprietary Feed-Media GHS-M4 and Supplement GHS-S2.

---

## 3.0 GENETIC STABILITY TESTING PROTOCOLS

To confirm the stability of the Glucogen-XR expression construct, Google Health Sciences performed a suite of molecular biology assays on cells at the WCB level and cells at the LIVCA (defined as 15 generations beyond the standard manufacturing process duration).

### 3.1 Protocol for Copy Number Analysis via Droplet Digital PCR (ddPCR)
**Objective:** To quantify the number of integrated copies of the Glucogen-XR gene expression cassette per host cell genome.

1. **Genomic DNA Extraction:** Cells are harvested from the bioreactor, washed in PBS, and DNA is extracted using the QIAamp DNA Mini Kit (Equipment ID: GHS-EQ-0982).
2. **Restriction Digestion:** DNA is digested with *HpaII* to ensure optimal template accessibility without fragmenting the target sequence.
3. **Droplet Generation:** Samples are partitioned into 20,000 nanoliter-sized droplets.
4. **Target Gene:** Glucogen-XR Leader-Peptide sequence.
5. **Reference Gene:** Endogenous CHO *Glucagon Receptor* (single copy control).
6. **Analysis:** Ratio of Target/Reference determines the copy number per cell.

### 3.2 Protocol for mRNA Transcript Analysis (Northern Blotting)
**Objective:** To confirm that a single transcript of the expected size is produced.

1. **RNA Isolation:** Total RNA is isolated using the RNeasy kit (Qiagen).
2. **Electrophoresis:** 10 µg of total RNA is separated on a 1.2% formaldehyde-agarose gel.
3. **Transfer:** RNA is transferred to a positively charged nylon membrane via capillary action for 16 hours.
4. **Hybridization:** The membrane is probed with a $^{32}$P-labeled cDNA fragment specific to the Glucogen-XR coding sequence.
5. **Imaging:** Phosphorimager analysis (Typhoon 9410) is used to detect band intensity and molecular weight.

---

## 4.0 GENETIC STABILITY DATA SUMMARY

### 4.1 Comparative Analysis: MCB vs. LIVCA
Stability was assessed by comparing the Master Cell Bank (MCB) to the End of Production Cells (EOPC) at the Limit of In Vitro Cell Age (LIVCA = 65 population doublings).

| Parameter | Assay Method | MCB Result (Batch MCB-001) | LIVCA Result (Batch GLUC-2025-010-EOP) | Acceptance Criteria |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| **Gene Copy Number** | ddPCR | 12.4 ± 0.5 copies | 12.1 ± 0.4 copies | Within ± 20% of MCB |
| **mRNA Size** | Northern Blot | 1.8 kb | 1.8 kb | Consistent with Control |
| **Cassette Integrity** | Restriction Mapping | Matches Theoretical | Matches Theoretical | No visible rearrangements |
| **Sequence Identity** | NGS (Sanger verify) | 100% Match | 100% Match | No amino acid substitutions |
| **Productivity** | Titer (HPLC) | 5.4 g/L | 5.2 g/L | > 80% of initial |

### 4.2 Southern Blot Analysis of Genomic Integration
To assess the structural integrity of the integrated DNA, Southern blot analysis was performed using three distinct restriction enzymes: *EcoRI*, *XbaI*, and *HindIII*.

*   **Lane 1:** Molecular Weight Marker
*   **Lane 2:** MCB DNA + *EcoRI* (Primary Band at 4.2 kb)
*   **Lane 3:** LIVCA DNA + *EcoRI* (Primary Band at 4.2 kb)
*   **Lane 4:** MCB DNA + *XbaI* (Primary Band at 6.8 kb)
*   **Lane 5:** LIVCA DNA + *XbaI* (Primary Band at 6.8 kb)

**Observation:** The banding patterns between MCB and LIVCA are identical, confirming no large-scale deletions, insertions, or translocations occurred within the Glucogen-XR expression cassette during long-term culture.

---

## 5.0 PHENOTYPIC STABILITY AND GROWTH CHARACTERISTICS

The phenotypic stability of GHS-CHO-001 was monitored by assessing growth kinetics, metabolite profiles, and nutrient consumption rates across the expansion phase.

### 5.1 Growth Kinetic Parameters

| Generation Number | Doubling Time (hr) | Specific Glucose Uptake (pmol/cell/day) | Specific Lactate Production (pmol/cell/day) |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| **Gen 10 (WCB)** | 21.2 | 4.5 | 2.1 |
| **Gen 30 (Mid-process)** | 21.5 | 4.6 | 2.0 |
| **Gen 50 (Standard Harvest)** | 21.8 | 4.8 | 2.2 |
| **Gen 65 (LIVCA)** | 22.1 | 4.7 | 2.3 |

**Statistical Significance:** No statistically significant difference ($p > 0.05$ via One-way ANOVA) was observed in the growth rates or metabolic efficiency of the cells from the start of the process through the LIVCA.

---

## 6.0 SEQUENCE INTEGRITY (C-TERMINAL AND N-TERMINAL)

To ensure that the expression level did not compromise the quality of the peptide, N-terminal sequencing (Edman Degradation) and C-terminal sequencing (Mass Spectrometry) were performed on product derived from cells at the beginning and end of the stability study.

1. **N-Terminal Sequence (1-10):** H-G-E-G-T-F-T-S-D-V (Matches Glucogen-XR Master Sequence).
2. **C-Terminal Sequence:** Confirmed intact fusion to the GHS-Polypeptide-Tail.
3. **Post-Translational Modifications (PTMs):** Glycosylation profiles (N-linked) were monitored via HILIC-FLD and remained consistent within ± 3% across the generational study.

---

## 7.0 CONCLUSION

The data presented in this subsection "Expression Levels and Stability" demonstrate that the GHS-CHO-001 expression system for Glucogen-XR is highly stable and robust. 

1. **Productivity:** Volumetric titers remain consistent at > 5.0 g/L at the 2000L scale, with no decline in cell-specific productivity through the LIVCA.
2. **Genetic Stability:** DNA copy number, mRNA transcript size, and genomic integration patterns remain constant, meeting all ICH Q5B requirements.
3. **Consistency:** The manufacturing process, when initiated from either the MCB or WCB, yields a product of consistent quality and purity, regardless of the population doubling level at the time of harvest.

Google Health Sciences maintains that the GHS-CHO-001 cell line is suitable for the commercial manufacture of Glucogen-XR under the conditions described in Module 3.

---
**References:**
- *ICH Q5B: Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products.*
- *USP <1048>: Quality of Biotechnological Products: Analysis of the Expression Construct in Cells Used for Production of rDNA Derived Protein Products.*
- *FDA Guidance for Industry: Characterization and Qualification of Cell Substrates and Other Biological Materials Used in the Production of Viral Vaccines for Infectious Disease Indications.*

# Manufacturing Process Development History

## Process Evolution from R&D to Commercial

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA AND INFORMATION)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE
### 3.2.S.2: MANUFACTURE
#### 3.2.S.2.6: MANUFACTURING PROCESS DEVELOPMENT HISTORY

---

### SUBSECTION: PROCESS EVOLUTION FROM R&D TO COMMERCIAL

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection provides a granular, comprehensive history of the manufacturing process development for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a novel GLP-1 receptor agonist produced by Google Health Sciences. The evolution of the process—from the initial Proof-of-Concept (PoC) at the bench scale to the finalized Phase III/Commercial scale—is detailed herein. This narrative demonstrates the systematic application of Quality by Design (QbD) principles, as per ICH Q8(R2), ICH Q11, and the lifecycle management principles of ICH Q12.

The development of Glucogen-XR was driven by the objective of achieving a high-titer, high-purity product with a specific glycosylation profile essential for its extended-release pharmacokinetic properties. The process evolved across four primary generations (Gen 1 through Gen 4), each marked by specific refinements in cell culture media, purification chromatography, and viral clearance strategies.

---

#### 2.0 CHRONOLOGICAL OVERVIEW OF MANUFACTURING SCALES
The manufacturing process for Glucogen-XR underwent six scale-up events, summarized in Table 2.0-1.

**Table 2.0-1: Summary of Process Evolution and Scale-Up Milestones**

| Development Phase | Process Version | Site of Manufacture | Scale (L) | Batch Number Prefix | Primary Objective |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Discovery/R&D** | Gen 1.0 | Mountain View R&D Lab 4 | 2L / 10L | RND-GLUC-001 | Lead candidate selection & initial characterization |
| **Pre-clinical (GLP)** | Gen 1.1 | SSF Innovation Drive (Bldg 1) | 50L | GLP-GLUC-2022 | Toxicology supply and stability studies |
| **Phase I/II Clinical** | Gen 2.0 | SSF Innovation Drive (Bldg 2) | 250L | GLUC-2023-XXX | Process robustness & initial IND filing |
| **Process Opt.** | Gen 3.0 | SSF Innovation Drive (Bldg 2) | 500L | GLUC-2024-XXX | Media optimization & Titer enhancement |
| **Phase III / PPQ** | Gen 4.0 | SSF Manufacturing Center | 2000L | GLUC-2025-XXX | Final Commercial Process Validation |

---

#### 3.0 GENERATION 1: EARLY RESEARCH AND PRE-CLINICAL DEVELOPMENT
##### 3.1 Gen 1.0: Bench-Scale Discovery (2021-2022)
The initial development utilized the GHS-CHO-001 cell line, a proprietary Glutamine Synthetase (GS) knockout derivative of CHO-K1. The primary focus was the optimization of the vector construct to ensure stable expression of the glucapeptide sequence.

*   **Upstream Parameters (Gen 1.0):**
    *   Basal Media: CD-CHO (Commercial Formulation)
    *   Feed Strategy: Bolus feed on Days 3, 5, 7.
    *   Temperature: Constant 37.0°C.
    *   Peak Titer: 0.85 g/L.
*   **Downstream Parameters (Gen 1.0):**
    *   Capture: Protein A affinity chromatography.
    *   Polishing: Single Cation Exchange (CEX) step.
    *   Yield: 45% overall.

##### 3.2 Gen 1.1: GLP Toxicology Supply (Batch GLP-GLUC-2022-01 to 05)
To support IND-enabling toxicology studies, the process was scaled to 50L. During this phase, it was observed that the C-terminal glycan heterogeneity significantly impacted the half-life of the peptide.

**Table 3.2-1: Gen 1.1 Analytical Results (Scale: 50L)**

| Batch ID | Viability at Harvest (%) | Harvest Titer (g/L) | Monomer Purity (SEC) | HCP (ppm) | DNA (pg/mg) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLP-GLUC-2022-01 | 88.4 | 0.92 | 94.2% | 1,250 | 45 |
| GLP-GLUC-2022-02 | 87.9 | 0.95 | 93.8% | 1,310 | 52 |
| GLP-GLUC-2022-03 | 89.1 | 0.98 | 94.5% | 1,180 | 38 |
| **Mean** | **88.5** | **0.95** | **94.2** | **1247** | **45** |

---

#### 4.0 GENERATION 2: PHASE I/II CLINICAL DEVELOPMENT (GLUC-2023 SERIES)
The transition to Phase I required a process that was not only scalable but also compliant with cGMP requirements. Gen 2.0 introduced the first significant modifications to the upstream feed strategy to control the glycosylation profile.

##### 4.1 Upstream Process Refinements: Shift to Biphasic Temperature
A biphasic temperature strategy was implemented to prolong culture viability and increase specific productivity ($q_p$).
*   **Phase 1 (Growth):** 37.0°C until VCD (Viable Cell Density) reaches $12 \times 10^6$ cells/mL.
*   **Phase 2 (Production):** Temperature shift to 33.0°C to reduce metabolic waste accumulation (Lactate and Ammonia).

##### 4.2 Downstream Process: Implementation of Orthogonal Viral Clearance
Following FDA guidance on Viral Safety (ICH Q5A), the downstream process was updated to include:
1.  **Low pH Inactivation:** Solvent/Detergent (S/D) treatment was replaced by Low pH (3.5 ± 0.1) for 60 minutes.
2.  **Viral Filtration:** Implementation of Planova 20N nanofiltration.

**Table 4.2-1: Step-by-Step Procedure for Low pH Viral Inactivation (Gen 2.0)**

| Step | Operation | Parameters | Target/Range |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | Titration | Add 1M Phosphoric Acid | pH 3.50 ± 0.05 |
| 2 | Incubation | Controlled Stirring (Room Temp) | 60 - 90 minutes |
| 3 | Re-equilibration | Add 1M Tris-Base | pH 5.50 ± 0.10 |
| 4 | Filtration | Depth Filter (Millipore X0SP) | Flux < 100 LMH |

---

#### 5.0 GENERATION 3: PROCESS OPTIMIZATION (GLUC-2024 SERIES)
Gen 3.0 represented the "Optimization Peak" where Google Health Sciences applied Machine Learning (ML) models—leveraging Google Cloud's Vertex AI—to predict nutrient consumption rates.

##### 5.1 The GHS-Media-04 Feed Strategy
The transition from commercial media to a proprietary chemically defined (CD) media (GHS-Media-04) resulted in a 40% increase in titer.

**Formula 5.1-1: Specific Glucose Consumption Rate ($q_{Glc}$)**
$$q_{Glc} = \frac{1}{VCD} \cdot \frac{d[Glc]}{dt}$$
*Where:*
*   $VCD$ = Viable Cell Density ($10^6$ cells/mL)
*   $[Glc]$ = Glucose concentration (g/L)
*   $t$ = Time (hours)

By maintaining $q_{Glc}$ between 0.02 and 0.04 pg/cell/day via continuous micro-feeding, lactate production was minimized ($< 2.0$ g/L).

##### 5.2 Downstream Optimization: Introduction of Mixed-Mode Chromatography
To improve the removal of high-molecular-weight (HMW) aggregates, a Capto Adhere (Mixed-Mode) step was inserted between the Protein A and CEX steps.

**Table 5.2-1: Comparison of Gen 2.0 vs Gen 3.0 Purity Profile**

| Attribute | Gen 2.0 (2-Step) | Gen 3.0 (3-Step) | Improvement (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Monomer Purity | 96.5% | 99.2% | +2.7% |
| HMW Aggregates | 2.8% | 0.6% | -78.6% |
| HCP (ppm) | 120 | 12 | -90.0% |
| Pro-A Leached (ng/mg) | 8.5 | 1.2 | -85.9% |

---

#### 6.0 GENERATION 4: COMMERCIAL SCALE (GLUC-2025-XXX)
The Gen 4.0 process is the "Final Commercial Process" used for Phase III clinical supplies and Process Performance Qualification (PPQ). It is executed at the 2000L scale at the SSF Manufacturing Center.

##### 6.1 Finalized Upstream Process (2000L)
The process utilizes a N-1 perfusion seed train to achieve high starting VCD in the production bioreactor (N).

**Table 6.1-1: Final Upstream Batch Records (Representative Batch GLUC-2025-001)**

| Parameter | Specification | Result (GLUC-2025-001) | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Inoculum Density | $0.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL | $0.52 \times 10^6$ | Pass |
| Peak VCD | $18.0 - 22.0 \times 10^6$ | $20.4 \times 10^6$ | Pass |
| Harvest Viability | $> 80\%$ | 86.4% | Pass |
| Harvest Day | Day 14 ± 1 | Day 14 | Pass |
| Final Titer | Report | 3.42 g/L | N/A |

##### 6.2 Detailed Step-by-Step Commercial Downstream Protocol (Gen 4.0)
The following protocol outlines the critical steps for the commercial manufacture of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance.

**Protocol 6.2-A: Protein A Capture (Unit Op 1)**
1.  **Column:** MabSelect PrismA (Bed height 20 cm, Diameter 60 cm).
2.  **Equilibration:** 5 CV of 20mM Sodium Phosphate, 150mM NaCl, pH 7.2.
3.  **Loading:** Clarified harvest at 250 cm/hr, loading capacity 40 g/L resin.
4.  **Wash 1:** 3 CV Equilibration buffer.
5.  **Wash 2 (Impurity Removal):** 4 CV 20mM Sodium Citrate, 1M NaCl, pH 6.0.
6.  **Elution:** 20mM Sodium Citrate, pH 3.0.
7.  **Collection:** Based on $A_{280}$ (100 mAU to 100 mAU).

**Protocol 6.2-B: Anion Exchange (AEX) Chromatography (Flow-Through Mode)**
1.  **Column:** Capto Q.
2.  **Buffer:** 50mM Tris, pH 8.0.
3.  **Operation:** Product passes through; DNA and acidic impurities bind to the resin.
4.  **Step Yield:** 98.5%.

---

#### 7.0 EVALUATION OF CRITICAL QUALITY ATTRIBUTES (CQAs) ACROSS GENERATIONS
To ensure comparability between the clinical material (Gen 2/3) and the commercial material (Gen 4), a comprehensive comparability study was performed.

**Table 7.0-1: Comparability Data Across Process Versions**

| Quality Attribute | Gen 1.1 (Pre-clin) | Gen 2.0 (Ph I/II) | Gen 4.0 (Commercial) | Analytical Method |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary Sequence** | Confirmed | Confirmed | Confirmed | LC-MS/MS |
| **Glycan Profile (G0F)** | 45% | 48% | 49% | HILIC-FLD |
| **Sialic Acid Content** | 1.2 mol/mol | 2.1 mol/mol | 2.3 mol/mol | HPLC (DMB) |
| **Oxidation (Met14)** | 2.4% | 1.8% | 0.9% | Peptide Map |
| **Deamidation** | 3.1% | 2.5% | 1.4% | cIEF |
| **Potency (Cell-based)** | 92% | 98% | 102% | cAMP Induction |

*Statistical Note:* A Two-One-Sided Test (TOST) was applied for equivalence testing between Gen 3 and Gen 4. For potency, the 90% Confidence Interval (CI) of the difference fell within the range of [-10%, +10%], confirming comparability.

---

#### 8.0 JUSTIFICATION OF PROCESS CHANGES
The evolution of the Glucogen-XR process was necessitated by the requirement for increased purity and the mitigation of risk factors identified during development.

1.  **Removal of Antibiotics (Gen 1 to Gen 2):** Penicillin/Streptomycin used in R&D were eliminated in Gen 2.0 to comply with regulatory expectations (USP <1117>).
2.  **Shift to Single-Use Technology (SUT):** To reduce cross-contamination risk and validation timelines (cleaning validation), the process shifted to 100% SUT for the 500L and 2000L scales.
3.  **Buffer Preparation (Gen 4):** Implementation of Inline Dilution (ILD) for the 2000L scale to reduce floor space requirements for buffer tanks.

---

#### 9.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDELINES
All process development activities were conducted in alignment with the following:
*   **ICH Q11:** Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances (Chemical Entities and Biotechnological/Biological Entities).
*   **ICH Q8(R2):** Pharmaceutical Development.
*   **FDA Guidance:** "Process Validation: General Principles and Practices" (2011).
*   **USP <1043>:** Ancillary Materials for Cell, Gene, and Tissue-Engineered Products.

---

#### 10.0 CONCLUSION
The development history of Glucogen-XR demonstrates a robust and scientifically driven evolution from a 2L R&D process to a 2000L commercial-scale operation. The Gen 4.0 process, characterized by high-yield upstream productivity (3.4 g/L) and a sophisticated 3-step purification train, ensures the consistent production of a high-purity glucapeptide with a well-defined CQA profile. The integration of Google Cloud Life Sciences' computational capabilities allowed for the acceleration of media optimization, resulting in a process that is both efficient and capable of meeting global market demand for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapy.

**ID: GHS-GLUC-M3-DS-2.6-001**
**Confidential - Google Health Sciences Proprietary Information**

## Scale-Up Studies

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S DRUG SUBSTANCE)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.6 MANUFACTURING PROCESS DEVELOPMENT
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.2.6.4 SCALE-UP STUDIES

---

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.1 Introduction and Scope of Scale-Up Strategy

The scale-up of the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) manufacturing process from laboratory development (2L and 10L) to clinical/commercial scale (2,000L) represents a critical milestone in the development of Google Health Sciences’ Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapeutic portfolio. The primary objective of the scale-up program was to demonstrate that the Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs) of the drug substance remain consistent across a 200-fold increase in volume, while maintaining yield and process efficiency.

The scale-up strategy was governed by **ICH Q11: Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances** and utilized a **Quality by Design (QbD)** approach. The transition followed a stepwise increment:
1.  **Bench Scale:** 2L – 10L (Process Characterization)
2.  **Pilot Scale:** 50L – 200L (Clinical Phase I/II Supply)
3.  **Commercial/Pivotal Scale:** 2,000L (Clinical Phase III and Commercial launch)

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.2 Engineering Principles and Scale-Up Methodology

The scale-up for Glucogen-XR focused on maintaining constant oxygen mass transfer ($k_La$) and Tip Speed ($\pi DN$), while monitoring the Power Input per Volume ($P/V$) to ensure cell viability in the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line.

##### 3.2.S.2.6.4.2.1 Mass Transfer and Aeration Strategy
The $k_La$ (volumetric mass transfer coefficient) was characterized across all scales using the following empirical correlation:
$$k_La = \alpha \cdot (P/V)^\beta \cdot (v_s)^\gamma$$
Where:
*   $P/V$ = Power input per volume ($W/m^3$)
*   $v_s$ = Superficial gas velocity ($m/s$)
*   $\alpha, \beta, \gamma$ = Dimensionless constants specific to the GHS-CHO-001 media composition.

**Table 1: Scale-Up Geometric and Operational Parameters (Upstream)**

| Parameter | Bench Scale (10L) | Pilot Scale (200L) | Commercial Scale (2,000L) | Scale Factor |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Vessel ID** | GHS-BIO-10L-04 | GHS-BIO-200L-02 | GHS-BIO-2000L-01 | - |
| **Working Volume (L)** | 10 | 200 | 2,000 | 200x |
| **Tank Diameter (m)** | 0.22 | 0.62 | 1.35 | 6.13x |
| **Impeller Type** | 2x Rushton | 2x Elephant Ear | 3x Elephant Ear | - |
| **Impeller Diameter (m)** | 0.08 | 0.23 | 0.51 | 6.37x |
| **Agitation (RPM)** | 180 - 250 | 85 - 110 | 45 - 65 | - |
| **Tip Speed (m/s)** | 0.75 - 1.05 | 1.02 - 1.32 | 1.20 - 1.70 | Matches |
| **Power/Volume (W/m³)** | 15 - 25 | 18 - 22 | 18 - 24 | Constant |
| **Sparge Rate (VVM)** | 0.01 - 0.05 | 0.01 - 0.05 | 0.005 - 0.03 | Decreased |

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.3 Pilot Scale Evaluation (200L) - Phase II Bridging

The transition to the 200L scale (Pilot Scale) was conducted at the Google Health Sciences Facility (South San Francisco). Three batches (GLUC-2025-P01 through GLUC-2025-P03) were produced to establish the baseline for the extended-release glucapeptide profile.

**Table 2: Performance Summary of 200L Pilot Batches**

| Batch Number | Inoculation Viability (%) | Peak VCD (x10⁶ cells/mL) | Harvest Viability (%) | Titer (g/L) | Glycosylation Profile (Man5 %) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-P01** | 98.4 | 18.2 | 84.1 | 4.12 | 2.1 |
| **GLUC-2025-P02** | 99.1 | 19.5 | 82.5 | 4.35 | 1.9 |
| **GLUC-2025-P03** | 97.8 | 17.9 | 83.3 | 4.08 | 2.3 |
| **Mean** | 98.4 | 18.5 | 83.3 | 4.18 | 2.1 |
| **% CV** | 0.67 | 4.54 | 0.96 | 3.48 | 9.5 |

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.4 Commercial Scale-Up Studies (2,000L)

The scale-up to 2,000L utilized the **GHS-FLEX-2000** Single-Use Bioreactor (SUB) platform. The primary challenge during this phase was managing the CO₂ stripping efficiency to prevent hypercapnia, which negatively impacts the N-glycosylation of Glucogen-XR.

##### 3.2.S.2.6.4.4.1 Protocol for 2,000L Bioreactor Preparation (SOP-GHS-DS-0442)
1.  **Warming:** Medium pre-heated to 36.5°C prior to transfer.
2.  **Inoculation:** Seed train N-1 (200L) transferred via sterile single-use connector at a target VCD of $0.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL.
3.  **pH Control:** Initial setpoint 7.00 ± 0.05. CO₂ sparging used for acidification; 1M $Na_2CO_3$ for base addition.
4.  **Feeding Strategy:** Bolus feeds of GHS-Feed-A (glucose-based) and GHS-Feed-B (amino acid-rich) starting on Day 3, based on metabolic demand.

**Table 3: 2,000L Commercial Scale Batch Results (GLUC-2025-C01 to C03)**

| Attribute | Specification / Target | GLUC-2025-C01 | GLUC-2025-C02 | GLUC-2025-C03 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Run Duration** | 14 Days | 14 Days | 14 Days | 14 Days |
| **Viable Cell Density (Max)** | Report | $22.4 \times 10^6$ | $21.8 \times 10^6$ | $23.1 \times 10^6$ |
| **Lactate (Peak)** | < 4.0 g/L | 2.8 g/L | 3.1 g/L | 2.6 g/L |
| **Ammonia (Peak)** | < 8.0 mM | 6.2 mM | 6.5 mM | 5.9 mM |
| **Harvest Titer** | > 3.5 g/L | 4.45 g/L | 4.38 g/L | 4.52 g/L |
| **HCP (Harvest)** | < 500,000 ng/mg | 320,000 | 345,000 | 312,000 |

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.5 Downstream Scale-Up: Chromatography and Filtration

Downstream scale-up followed the principle of constant residence time and bed height.

##### 3.2.S.2.6.4.5.1 Protein A Capture (Step 1)
The Protein A capture step (MabSelect SuRe LX) was scaled using a column diameter increase from 10cm (Pilot) to 60cm (Commercial).
*   **Linear Velocity:** Maintained at 300 cm/h.
*   **Loading Capacity:** Validated at 35 g/L of resin.
*   **Yield Comparison:** 10L (94%), 200L (93%), 2,000L (92.5%).

**Table 4: Downstream Step Yields Across Scales**

| Process Step | Lab (10L) Yield % | Pilot (200L) Yield % | Commercial (2000L) Yield % |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Centrifugation/Depth Filtration** | 92.1 | 90.5 | 89.8 |
| **Protein A Capture** | 94.2 | 93.8 | 93.5 |
| **Viral Inactivation** | 98.5 | 98.1 | 98.0 |
| **Cation Exchange (CEX)** | 88.4 | 87.2 | 87.5 |
| **Anion Exchange (AEX)** | 95.1 | 94.8 | 94.2 |
| **Nanofiltration (VF)** | 99.2 | 98.9 | 98.7 |
| **UF/DF** | 97.4 | 96.5 | 96.2 |
| **Overall Yield** | **70.5%** | **66.8%** | **65.5%** |

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.6 Comparability of Drug Substance (Critical Quality Attributes)

To confirm successful scale-up, the three commercial batches (GLUC-2025-C01/02/03) were compared against the reference clinical batches (GLUC-2024-CLIN01/02).

**Table 5: CQA Comparability Matrix**

| Attribute | Method | Clinical Mean (n=2) | Commercial Mean (n=3) | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Purity (Monomer %)** | SE-HPLC | 99.1 | 98.9 | $\ge$ 98.0% |
| **Main Peak (%)** | CEX-HPLC | 74.5 | 73.8 | 70.0 - 80.0% |
| **Total Aggregates** | SE-HPLC | 0.4 | 0.5 | $\le$ 1.0% |
| **Specific Activity** | In vitro Bioassay | 102% | 104% | 80 - 120% |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> | < 0.05 EU/mg | < 0.05 EU/mg | $\le$ 0.1 EU/mg |
| **Host Cell Protein** | ELISA | 12 ppm | 14 ppm | $\le$ 20 ppm |

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.7 Deviations and Continuous Process Improvement (CPI)

During the scale-up of batch **GLUC-2025-C02**, a minor temperature excursion (±0.8°C) occurred during the induction phase. The investigation (CAPA-2025-044) utilized Google Cloud's AI-driven predictive modeling to determine the impact on protein folding. The model predicted no significant impact, which was subsequently confirmed by circular dichroism (CD) and peptide mapping.

#### 3.2.S.2.6.4.8 Conclusion

The scale-up studies for Glucogen-XR demonstrate a robust and reproducible manufacturing process. The implementation of identical equipment geometries and the use of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line enabled a seamless transition from 10L to 2,000L. The consistency in CQA profiles across all scales confirms that the therapeutic efficacy and safety profile established during clinical trials are maintained at commercial scale.

## Comparability Assessments

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (MODALITIES: BIOLOGICS/PEPTIDES)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2.6 MANUFACTURING PROCESS DEVELOPMENT
### SUBSECTION: COMPARABILITY ASSESSMENTS (3.2.S.2.6.4)

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE OF COMPARABILITY PROGRAM

This section provides a comprehensive evaluation of the comparability between Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) drug substance (DS) manufactured using the Phase 2 process (Process Version 2.1) and the proposed commercial process (Process Version 3.0, "Scale-Up and Optimization"). 

The comparability program was designed in strict accordance with **ICH Q5E: Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products Subject to Changes in their Manufacturing Process**, and **FDA Guidance for Industry: Q5E Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products**. Given that Glucogen-XR is a recombinant glucapeptide (GLP-1 receptor agonist) expressed in the proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative cell line (GHS-CHO-001) and conjugated to an extended-release copolymeric moiety, the assessment encompasses primary sequence integrity, post-translational modification (PTM) profiles, higher-order structure (HOS), impurity profiles (product-related and process-related), and biological potency.

The transition from Process V2.1 to V3.0 involved:
1.  Increase in bioreactor scale from 500L to 2,000L.
2.  Implementation of a continuous perfusion-fed batch hybrid strategy.
3.  Transition from manual chromatography skids to automated DeltaV-controlled systems.
4.  Optimization of the conjugation chemistry to improve the polydispersity index (PDI) of the extended-release moiety.

#### 2.0 COMPARABILITY STRATEGY AND ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA

The comparability strategy followed a tiered approach:
*   **Tier 1: Analytical Characterization (Primary and Higher Order Structure)**
*   **Tier 2: Product Quality Attributes (PQAs) and Impurity Profiles**
*   **Tier 3: Biological Activity and Potency**
*   **Tier 4: Accelerated and Stress Stability Studies**

##### 2.1 Statistical Approach for Acceptance Criteria
Acceptance criteria were established based on the historical data from 12 batches of Process V2.1. For quantitative attributes, the comparability range was defined as the Mean ± 3 Standard Deviations (SD) of the reference process, or where appropriate, based on clinical relevance and specification limits.

**Formula for Statistical Equivalence (TOST):**
To confirm equivalence for critical quality attributes (CQAs), a Two One-Sided T-test (TOST) was employed with an equivalence margin ($\theta$) of 1.5 * SD of the reference process.
$$ \Delta = |\bar{X}_{test} - \bar{X}_{ref}| < \theta $$

#### 3.0 BATCH ANALYSIS AND MANUFACTURING HISTORY

The following batches were utilized for the comparability exercise. All batches were manufactured at the Google Health Sciences Facility (3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA).

**Table 1: Batches Utilized in Comparability Assessment**

| Batch Number | Process Version | Scale (L) | Purpose | Date of Manufacture | Site |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | V2.1 | 500 | Phase 2 Clinical | 12-JAN-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg1 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | V2.1 | 500 | Phase 2 Clinical | 05-FEB-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg1 |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | V2.1 | 500 | Phase 2 Clinical | 01-MAR-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg1 |
| **GLUC-2025-101** | V3.0 | 2,000 | PPQ / Commercial | 15-JUN-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg2 |
| **GLUC-2025-102** | V3.0 | 2,000 | PPQ / Commercial | 10-JUL-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg2 |
| **GLUC-2025-103** | V3.0 | 2,000 | PPQ / Commercial | 02-AUG-2025 | GHS-SSF-Bldg2 |

---

#### 4.0 PHYSICOCHEMICAL CHARACTERIZATION

##### 4.1 Primary Structure and Amino Acid Sequence
Sequence integrity was verified using Liquid Chromatography with Tandem Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) following tryptic and Asp-N enzymatic digestion.

**Protocol GHS-PROT-QC-098: Peptide Mapping by LC-UV-MS/MS**
1. **Reduction/Alkylation:** 100 µg DS reduced with 10 mM DTT at 56°C for 45 min; alkylated with 25 mM Iodoacetamide at RT in the dark.
2. **Digestion:** Sequence-grade Trypsin (1:20 w/w ratio) in 50 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.8, 16 hours at 37°C.
3. **LC Parameters:** Column: Waters ACQUITY UPLC BEH C18, 1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm. Mobile Phase A: 0.1% FA in H2O; B: 0.1% FA in ACN.
4. **MS Parameters:** Orbitrap Exploris 480; Resolution 120,000; HCD fragmentation.

**Table 2: Peptide Mapping and Sequence Coverage**

| Attribute | V2.1 Mean (n=3) | V3.0 Mean (n=3) | Acceptance Criteria | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Sequence Coverage | 100.0% | 100.0% | ≥ 98.0% | Pass |
| Retention Time (T1 peptide) | 14.22 min | 14.24 min | ± 0.5 min | Pass |
| Mass Accuracy (Intact) | 1.2 ppm | 1.1 ppm | < 5.0 ppm | Pass |

##### 4.2 Post-Translational Modifications (PTMs)
Glucogen-XR contains a critical N-glycosylation site at Asn-24. The glycan profile is essential for the pharmacokinetics (PK) of the extended-release formulation.

**Table 3: Comparison of N-Glycan Profiles (Relative Area %)**

| Glycan Species | GLUC-2025-001 (Ref) | GLUC-2025-101 (Test) | GLUC-2025-102 (Test) | Range (V2.1) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| G0F | 42.1% | 41.8% | 42.3% | 38.5 - 45.2% |
| G1F | 35.6% | 36.1% | 35.8% | 32.1 - 39.4% |
| G2F | 8.2% | 8.4% | 8.1% | 6.5 - 10.2% |
| Sialylated Glycans | 4.1% | 4.3% | 4.2% | 3.0 - 5.5% |

*Note: Sialylation levels are critical as they influence the hepatic clearance via the asialoglycoprotein receptor.*

---

#### 5.0 PRODUCT-RELATED AND PROCESS-RELATED IMPURITIES

##### 5.1 Size Variants (SEC-HPLC)
Aggregation is a critical risk factor for GLP-1 agonists due to potential immunogenicity. Size-Exclusion Chromatography (SEC) was performed using a TOSOH TSKgel G3000SWxl column.

**Table 4: SEC-HPLC Purity Data**

| Batch ID | Monomer (%) | High Mol. Weight (HMW) (%) | Low Mol. Weight (LMW) (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 99.42 | 0.48 | 0.10 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 99.38 | 0.52 | 0.10 |
| **GLUC-2025-101** | 99.51 | 0.40 | 0.09 |
| **GLUC-2025-102** | 99.49 | 0.41 | 0.10 |
| **Criteria** | **≥ 98.0%** | **≤ 1.5%** | **≤ 0.5%** |

##### 5.2 Process-Related Impurities (HCP, rProtein A, DNA)
Residual Host Cell Protein (HCP) was measured using a third-generation CHO HCP ELISA kit (Cygnus Technologies, F550), validated specifically for the GHS-CHO-001 cell line.

**Table 5: Process Impurity Clearance**

| Impurity | GLUC-2025-001 (V2.1) | GLUC-2025-101 (V3.0) | Limit |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| HCP (ppm) | 12.4 | 9.8 | < 100 ppm |
| Residual DNA | 1.2 pg/mg | 0.8 pg/mg | < 10 pg/mg |
| rProtein A | < LOD | < LOD | < 5 ppm |
| Residual Solvent (ACN) | 120 ppm | 115 ppm | < 410 ppm |

---

#### 6.0 BIOLOGICAL POTENCY ASSAYS

Comparability of biological activity was assessed using the **GLP-1 Receptor Activation Bioassay (GHS-SOP-BIO-442)**. This assay utilizes a HEK293 cell line stably transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor and a luciferase reporter gene under the control of a cAMP-response element (CRE).

##### 6.1 Potency Calculation and Statistical Comparison
Relative potency is calculated using a 4-parameter logistic (4-PL) model.

**Formula for 4-PL Model:**
$$ y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B} $$
Where:
*   $A$ = Bottom asymptote
*   $B$ = Hill slope
*   $C$ = EC50
*   $D$ = Top asymptote

**Table 6: Potency Comparability Results**

| Batch Number | EC50 (nM) | Relative Potency (%) | 95% CI (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Reference Standard (RS04)** | 0.88 | 100% | N/A |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 0.89 | 98.9% | 94.2 - 103.1 |
| **GLUC-2025-101** | 0.87 | 101.1% | 97.5 - 105.8 |
| **GLUC-2025-102** | 0.90 | 97.8% | 93.1 - 102.4 |

**Statistical Equivalence:** The 90% confidence interval for the ratio of the means (V3.0/V2.1) was [0.96, 1.04], which falls within the predefined equivalence margin of [0.80, 1.25].

---

#### 7.0 HIGHER ORDER STRUCTURE (HOS) ANALYSIS

##### 7.1 Circular Dichroism (CD)
Far-UV CD spectra (190–260 nm) were acquired to assess alpha-helical content, which is characteristic of the GLP-1 peptide backbone.

*   **V2.1 Mean Alpha-Helix:** 44.2%
*   **V3.0 Mean Alpha-Helix:** 43.9%
*   **Weighted Spectral Difference (WSD):** 0.012 (Threshold < 0.05)

##### 7.2 Microcalorimetry (DSC)
Differential Scanning Calorimetry (DSC) was used to determine the thermal transition temperature ($T_m$).
*   **V2.1 $T_m$:** 68.4°C
*   **V3.0 $T_m$:** 68.6°C
*   **Conclusion:** Thermal stability profiles are identical within the precision of the instrument (± 0.5°C).

---

#### 8.0 FORCED DEGRADATION AND STABILITY COMPARABILITY

To ensure that the process changes did not alter the degradation pathways of Glucogen-XR, side-by-side forced degradation studies were conducted.

**Conditions:**
1.  **Thermal:** 40°C / 75% RH for 30 days.
2.  **Photolytic:** 1.2 million lux-hours (ICH Q1B).
3.  **Oxidative:** 0.3% H2O2 for 24 hours.
4.  **Low pH:** pH 3.0 for 48 hours.

**Table 7: Forced Degradation Results (SEC-HPLC % Purity)**

| Condition | V2.1 (Batch 001) | V3.0 (Batch 101) | Main Degradant Observed |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Control (T=0) | 99.4% | 99.5% | N/A |
| Thermal (30d) | 94.2% | 94.1% | High MW Aggregates |
| Photolytic | 96.8% | 97.0% | Oxidation (Trp-oxid) |
| Oxidative | 88.5% | 88.2% | Met-sulfoxide |
| Low pH | 91.2% | 91.5% | Deamidation (Asn) |

The degradation rates and species generated were comparable across both processes, confirming that the V3.0 process does not introduce new liabilities regarding product stability.

---

#### 9.0 REGULATORY CONFORMANCE AND CONCLUSIONS

The comprehensive comparability assessment between the Phase 2 process (V2.1) and the commercial scale-up process (V3.0) for Glucogen-XR demonstrates:
1.  **Identity:** The primary amino acid sequence and glycoform distribution remain consistent.
2.  **Purity:** The impurity profile, including process-related residuals (HCP, DNA), shows improved clearance in the V3.0 process due to optimized chromatography resins.
3.  **Potency:** Biological activity remains within the 80-125% equivalence window.
4.  **Stability:** No changes in the degradation kinetics or profiles were observed under stress conditions.

**Final Determination:** Based on the data presented, Glucogen-XR Drug Substance manufactured by Process V3.0 is highly comparable to the material used in Phase 2 clinical trials. The manufacturing changes are deemed low-risk and are validated to support the licensure of Glucogen-XR for the treatment of Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus.

---

1.  *ICH Q5E: Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products.*
2.  *ICH Q6B: Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.*

# Peptide Sequence Rationale

## AI-Assisted Sequence Design (Google DeepMind)

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE (GLUCAPEPTIDE)
### 3.2.S.1 GENERAL INFORMATION
#### 3.2.S.1.2 Peptide Sequence Rationale
##### 3.2.S.1.2.4 AI-Assisted Sequence Design (Google DeepMind)

---

### 1.0 Executive Summary of AI-Driven Molecular Engineering

The development of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** represents a paradigm shift in the rational design of Glucagon-Like Peptide-1 Receptor Agonists (GLP-1 RAs). Unlike traditional iterative mutagenesis or phage display techniques, the primary sequence of Glucogen-XR was optimized through a multi-layered computational framework developed in collaboration between **Google Health Sciences** and **Google DeepMind**.

This section details the application of the **AlphaFold-Multimer (v3.1)** and **ProtLM (Protein Language Model)** architectures to the design of the GHS-772-B lead candidate. The objective was to achieve three critical pharmacological parameters simultaneously:
1.  **Supraphysiological Affinity:** Optimization of the binding enthalpy ($ΔH$) between the peptide ligand and the extracellular domain (ECD) of the human GLP-1 receptor (hGLP-1R).
2.  **Proteolytic Resistance:** Targeted elimination of the Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-4) cleavage site and Neutral Endopeptidase (NEP) 24.11 recognition motifs through non-canonical amino acid substitution modeling.
3.  **Extended Pharmacokinetics:** Computational modeling of a site-specific C18 fatty acid diacid acylation to facilitate reversible albumin binding.

---

### 2.0 Computational Architecture and Methodology

#### 2.1 The DeepMind "Ensemble-Fold" Framework
The design process utilized an ensemble of three proprietary neural networks integrated into the Google Cloud Life Sciences TPU v4 cluster located in the South San Francisco facility.

| Model Component | Primary Function | Version/Commit ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **AlphaFold-P (Peptide)** | High-resolution structural prediction of the GLP-1R/Glucogen-XR complex. | AF-P-2024.08.12 |
| **G-Binder-Net** | Graph neural network for calculating binding free energy ($ΔG_{bind}$). | GBN-v4.2.1 |
| **Tox-Net 3.0** | Predictive modeling of peptide immunogenicity and MHC-II binding. | TN-2024-Q3 |
| **Stab-LM** | Language model for predicting metabolic stability in human plasma. | SLM-8.4 |

#### 2.2 In-Silico Mutagenesis Protocol (Protocol ID: GHS-COMP-001)

The following step-by-step procedure was executed to generate the final sequence for the GLUC-2025 series of clinical batches.

1.  **Input Sequence Initialization:** The native human GLP-1 (7-37) sequence was used as the seed template ($HAEGTFTSDVSSYLEGQAAKEFIAWLVKGRG$).
2.  **Space Search Expansion:** The AI model explored a combinatorial space of $20^{31}$ natural amino acids plus 14 selected non-canonical amino acids (Aib, Sar, D-Ala, etc.).
3.  **Refinement Loop (Iterative):**
    *   **Step A:** Prediction of $pKa$ shifts in the N-terminal Histidine to prevent DPP-4 recognition.
    *   **Step B:** Simulation of the steric hindrance provided by the C18-diacid-γGlu spacer at position Lys-26.
    *   **Step C:** Optimization of the alpha-helical propensity ($P_α$) in the C-terminal region (residues 22-31).
4.  **Selection Criteria:** Candidates were filtered based on a predicted $K_i < 0.1$ nM and a predicted half-life ($T_{1/2}$) in human serum $> 160$ hours.

---

### 3.0 Sequence Optimization Data and Results

#### 3.1 Comparative Binding Affinity Simulations
Table 3.1 displays the predicted vs. experimental binding parameters for the lead GLUC-2025-001 candidate compared to the reference medicinal chemistry standards (Semaglutide and Tirzepatide).

**Table 3.1: Predicted Binding Energetics (DeepMind G-Binder-Net)**

| Sequence Identifier | Modification at Pos 8 | Modification at Pos 26 | Predicted $ΔG$ (kcal/mol) | Predicted $K_d$ (pM) | Confidence Score (pLDDT) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Wild Type GLP-1** | Ala | None | -8.4 | 840.0 | 92.1 |
| **Reference A** | Aib | C18 diacid | -12.2 | 22.4 | 94.5 |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | **α-Me-Pro** | **C18-PEG2-γGlu** | **-14.8** | **4.2** | **98.8** |

*Note: The use of α-methyl-proline at position 8 was an AI-suggested modification to lock the N-terminus into a "Bio-Active Hook" conformation, significantly reducing entropic loss upon binding.*

#### 3.2 Metabolic Stability Mapping (Stab-LM Results)
The AI model identified a high-risk cleavage site at the $Trp^{31}-Leu^{32}$ bond. The "Stab-LM" module proposed an Isostere substitution.

**Table 3.2: Stability Index of In-Silico Variants**

| Variant ID | Sequence Change | Predicted $T_{1/2}$ (Plasma) | Cathepsin B Sensitivity | Batch Reference |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GHS-V1 | Leu32 -> Val | 110 hrs | Moderate | N/A (Digital) |
| GHS-V2 | Trp31 -> 1-Nal | 145 hrs | Low | N/A (Digital) |
| **GHS-772-B** | **Trp31-Isostere** | **188 hrs** | **Negligible** | **GLUC-2025-001** |

---

### 4.0 Structural Validation of the AI-Designed Lead (GHS-772-B)

#### 4.1 AlphaFold-Multimer Visualization Results
The AlphaFold-Multimer v3.1 output for the GLUC-2025-001 ligand interacting with the hGLP-1R (PDB ID for reference: 6X18) demonstrated a unique "Deep-Pocket Insertion" profile.

*   **Hydrogen Bonding Network:** The AI design introduced three additional H-bonds between the peptide's Gln-17 and the receptor's Arg-121.
*   **Hydrophobic Anchoring:** The acylated side chain at Lys-26 was predicted to occupy a specific hydrophobic groove in the receptor's extracellular domain, which was previously unexploited by traditional GLP-1 RAs.

#### 4.2 Statistical Analysis of Design Accuracy
To validate the AI's predictive power, Google Health Sciences performed a Root-Mean-Square Deviation (RMSD) analysis between the AI-predicted structure and the subsequent Cryo-EM structure obtained from the pilot batch GLUC-2025-002.

$$RMSD = \sqrt{\frac{1}{N} \sum_{i=1}^{N} \delta_i^2}$$

Where:
*   $N$ = Number of backbone atoms (Cα, N, C, O)
*   $\delta$ = Distance between predicted and experimental coordinates

**Result:** The Global RMSD was **0.64 Å**, indicating "Atomic-Level Precision" in the AI-assisted design phase.

---

### 5.0 Regulatory Compliance and Quality Control of AI Outputs

In alignment with **FDA Guidance for Industry: "Software as a Medical Device (SaMD)"** and the emerging framework for **Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning (AI/ML) in Drug Development**, Google Health Sciences has implemented the following controls:

1.  **Algorithm Traceability:** Every sequence modification suggested by DeepMind is logged with a unique "Reasoning Hash" (e.g., `SHA-256: 8f3e2...`) that links the mutation to specific protein-folding energy gradients.
2.  **Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) Verification:** All AI-designed sequences (including GHS-772-B) were reviewed by a panel of three Ph.D. biochemists with $>15$ years of experience in peptide synthesis before moving to GMP manufacturing (Batch GLUC-2025-003).
3.  **Training Data Integrity:** The models were trained exclusively on curated, high-resolution datasets from the Protein Data Bank (PDB) and internal Google G-Symmetrics proprietary assay data, ensuring no "hallucinations" in the peptide backbone.

---

### 6.0 References

1.  Jumper, J. et al. (2021). "Highly accurate protein structure prediction with AlphaFold." *Nature*, 596(7873), 583-589.
2.  Google DeepMind (2024). "Technical Report on Multimer Peptide Docking v3.1." *Internal Regulatory Document GHS-TR-2024-001*.
3.  FDA Guidance (Draft 2023). "Using Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning in the Development of Drug and Biological Products."

## Receptor Binding Optimization

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA AND DOCUMENTATION)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE
### 3.2.S.1: GENERAL INFORMATION
#### 3.2.S.1.2: PEPTIDE SEQUENCE RATIONALE
---
### **SUBSECTION: RECEPTOR BINDING OPTIMIZATION**

#### **1.0 OVERVIEW OF STRATEGIC DESIGN OBJECTIVES**
The development of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) by Google Health Sciences (GHS) represents a paradigm shift in the structural engineering of Glucagon-Like Peptide-1 Receptor Agonists (GLP-1RAs). The primary objective of the Receptor Binding Optimization (RBO) program was to decouple the high-affinity binding kinetics from the rapid internalization/downregulation pathways typically associated with native GLP-1(7-36)amide.

The RBO strategy focused on three specific functional domains:
1.  **The N-Terminal Activation Domain (His7-Gly22):** Modification to enhance DPP-IV resistance while maintaining critical hydrogen bonding with the GLP-1R extracellular domain (ECD).
2.  **The Amphipathic Alpha-Helix Core (Gln23-Lys34):** Optimization of the hydrophobic face to enhance interaction with the transmembrane (TM) bundles TM1, TM2, and TM7.
3.  **The C-Terminal Extension (CEX) and Linker Region:** Engineering a "stay-put" kinetic profile through the incorporation of a non-natural amino acid spacer and a C18 diacid fatty acid moiety for reversible albumin binding.

---

#### **2.0 COMPUTATIONAL MODELING AND IN SILICO AFFINITY MAPPING**
Prior to wet-lab synthesis (Batch Series GLUC-2025-PRE), GHS utilized the Google Cloud Life Sciences AlphaFold-Multimer platform (Version 3.2.1) to simulate the Glucogen-XR/GLP-1R complex.

##### **2.1 Molecular Dynamics (MD) Simulation Parameters**
MD simulations were conducted using the AMBER22 force field with the following specifications:
*   **Solvent Model:** TIP3P explicit water box.
*   **Neutralization:** 0.15 M NaCl.
*   **Temperature:** 310.15 K (Physiological).
*   **Pressure:** 1.0 bar (Parrinello-Rahman barostat).
*   **Time Step:** 2.0 fs.
*   **Total Production Run:** 5.0 microseconds (μs) per variant.

##### **2.2 Binding Free Energy Calculations (MM-PBSA)**
Calculations were performed to estimate the binding free energy ($\Delta G_{bind}$) using the formula:
$$\Delta G_{bind} = G_{complex} - (G_{receptor} + G_{ligand})$$
Where:
*   $\Delta G_{bind} = \Delta H - T\Delta S$
*   $\Delta H = \Delta E_{MM} + \Delta G_{solv}$

**Table 1: In Silico Predicted Binding Affinities for Candidate Variants (Series GLUC-2025-SIM)**

| Variant ID | Sequence Modification | $\Delta E_{vdW}$ (kcal/mol) | $\Delta E_{elec}$ (kcal/mol) | $\Delta G_{bind}$ (kcal/mol) | Predicted $K_i$ (nM) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GHS-001 (Native) | GLP-1 (7-36) | -52.4 | -210.3 | -14.2 | 0.85 |
| GHS-007 (Semaglutide) | Aib8, Arg34, C18-Linker | -58.9 | -225.1 | -16.8 | 0.38 |
| **GLUC-2025-OPT** | **Proprietary GHS-CHO-001 Optimized** | **-64.2** | **-248.7** | **-19.1** | **0.12** |
| GHS-012 | C-term truncated | -42.1 | -185.4 | -11.5 | 4.50 |

---

#### **3.0 SITE-DIRECTED MUTAGENESIS AND BINDING KINETICS**
To validate the *in silico* models, GHS performed site-directed mutagenesis on the GLP-1 receptor (human isoform, NCBI RefSeq: NP_002053.3).

##### **3.1 Surface Plasmon Resonance (SPR) Protocol (SOP-GHS-RD-502)**
Binding kinetics were determined using a Biacore™ T200 instrument.
1.  **Chip Preparation:** Series S Sensor Chip CM5.
2.  **Immobilization:** Amine coupling of GLP-1R (Extracellular Domain, residues 24-145) to a density of 500-800 RU.
3.  **Running Buffer:** HBS-EP+ (10 mM HEPES, 150 mM NaCl, 3 mM EDTA, 0.05% v/v Surfactant P20, pH 7.4).
4.  **Flow Rate:** 30 μL/min.
5.  **Association/Dissociation:** 180s / 600s.
6.  **Regeneration:** 10 mM Glycine-HCl pH 2.0 for 30s.

**Table 2: SPR Kinetic Constants for Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-005)**

| Batch Number | $k_a$ ($M^{-1}s^{-1} \times 10^5$) | $k_d$ ($s^{-1} \times 10^{-4}$) | $K_D$ (pM) | $R_{max}$ (RU) | $\chi^2$ (Fit Quality) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 2.45 | 1.12 | 45.7 | 42.1 | 0.15 |
| GLUC-2025-002 | 2.41 | 1.09 | 45.2 | 41.8 | 0.18 |
| GLUC-2025-003 | 2.48 | 1.15 | 46.4 | 43.0 | 0.12 |
| GLUC-2025-004 | 2.44 | 1.10 | 45.1 | 42.5 | 0.14 |
| GLUC-2025-005 | 2.46 | 1.13 | 45.9 | 42.9 | 0.16 |
| **Mean** | **2.45** | **1.12** | **45.7** | **42.5** | **N/A** |

*Note: The extremely low $k_d$ (dissociation rate) is a direct result of the optimized C-terminal anchor residues.*

---

#### **4.0 RECEPTOR INTERNALIZATION AND RECYCLING ASSAYS**
Unlike traditional GLP-1RAs, Glucogen-XR was engineered to favor "biased signaling," prioritizing cAMP production over $\beta$-arrestin recruitment to minimize receptor internalization.

##### **4.1 $\beta$-Arrestin 2 Recruitment Protocol**
1.  **Cell Line:** PathHunter® CHO-K1 GLP1R $\beta$-Arrestin Cell Line (Eurofins).
2.  **Incubation:** Cells seeded at $2 \times 10^4$ cells/well in 96-well plates.
3.  **Treatment:** Glucogen-XR concentrations ranging from $10^{-12}$ M to $10^{-6}$ M.
4.  **Detection:** Enzyme Fragment Complementation (EFC) chemiluminescence.

**Table 3: Biased Agonism Profile - cAMP vs. $\beta$-Arrestin Recruitment**

| Analyte | Pathway | $EC_{50}$ (pM) | $E_{max}$ (% of GLP-1) | Transduction Coefficient ($\log(\tau/\beta)$) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Native GLP-1 | cAMP | 15.4 | 100 | 0.00 |
| Native GLP-1 | $\beta$-Arrestin | 120.2 | 100 | 0.00 |
| **Glucogen-XR** | **cAMP** | **8.2** | **112** | **+1.45** |
| **Glucogen-XR** | **$\beta$-Arrestin** | **840.5** | **42** | **-2.10** |

**Interpretation:** The bias factor ($>100$-fold selectivity for cAMP) ensures that the GLP-1 receptor remains at the plasma membrane for extended periods, contributing to the "XR" (Extended Release) pharmacodynamic profile.

---

#### **5.0 CRITICAL AMINO ACID SUBSTITUTION ANALYSIS (ALANINE SCANNING)**
To define the Quantitative Structure-Activity Relationship (QSAR), each residue in the Glucogen-XR sequence was systematically replaced with Alanine.

##### **5.1 QSAR Results (Batch GLUC-2025-QSAR-01)**
The following residues were identified as critical for receptor binding:
1.  **His7 (Position 1):** Essential for N-terminal activation. $Ala7$ mutant showed $>1000$-fold loss in potency.
2.  **Gly8 $\rightarrow$ Aib8:** Substitution with Alpha-aminoisobutyric acid (Aib) provided steric hindrance against DPP-IV protease cleavage (Ref: USP <1223>).
3.  **Phe28:** High-impact hydrophobic residue. $Ala28$ substitution resulted in a 45-fold increase in $K_d$.
4.  **Lys34 (C18 Linkage):** The attachment point for the hexadecanedioic acid side chain. This modification increases albumin affinity ($K_D \approx 12 \mu M$), effectively creating a circulating reservoir of the drug.

---

#### **6.0 CONFORMATIONAL STABILITY AND SECONDARY STRUCTURE**
The secondary structure of Glucogen-XR was assessed using Circular Dichroism (CD) Spectroscopy to ensure the optimized sequence maintained its alpha-helical content under varying pH conditions.

##### **6.1 CD Spectroscopy Procedure**
*   **Instrument:** Jasco J-1500 CD Spectrometer.
*   **Path Length:** 1 mm.
*   **Wavelength Range:** 190 nm to 260 nm.
*   **Buffers:** Phosphate buffer (pH 7.4) and Acetate buffer (pH 4.5).

**Table 4: Helical Content as a Function of Sequence Optimization**

| Sequence ID | pH | $[\theta]_{222nm}$ (deg $cm^2/dmol$) | % Alpha-Helix | $T_m$ (°C) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-Ref-Alpha | 7.4 | -22,400 | 64% | 52.1 |
| **GLUC-2025-OPT** | **7.4** | **-28,900** | **82%** | **68.4** |
| GLUC-2025-OPT | 4.5 | -27,200 | 78% | 65.2 |

The data confirms that the optimized sequence maintains superior structural integrity compared to the reference, which is vital for maintaining the binding epitope during long-term storage and following subcutaneous injection.

---

#### **7.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDELINES**
All receptor binding optimization studies were conducted in accordance with:
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** "Nonclinical Safety Evaluation of Drug-induced Liver Injury (DILI)" (where applicable to GLP-1R cross-reactivity).
*   **USP <121>:** Insulin Assays (adapted for GLP-1 potency).

All raw data including SPR sensorgrams and MD trajectory files are archived in the Google Cloud Life Sciences Vault (GHS-REG-DATA-2025) and are available for FDA inspection upon request.

---
**END OF SUBSECTION**

## Stability Enhancements

### **3.2.S.1.2.2.1 Stability Enhancements via Primary Sequence Optimization and Post-Translational Modification Strategies**

#### **1. Introduction and Rationale for Structural Modification**
The primary amino acid sequence of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) represents a pinnacle of rational protein engineering designed to overcome the inherent pharmacokinetic limitations of native human Glucagon-Like Peptide-1 (GLP-1). Native GLP-1 (7-36) amide exhibits an extremely short plasma half-life ($t_{1/2} < 2$ minutes) due to rapid proteolytic cleavage and renal clearance. 

The structural modifications implemented by Google Health Sciences (GHS) target four critical degradation pathways:
1.  **Proteolytic Degradation:** Specifically by Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-IV) and Neutral Endopeptidase (NEP 24.11).
2.  **Chemical Instability:** Asparagine deamidation and Methionine oxidation.
3.  **Physical Aggregation:** Isoelectric point (pI) shifting to prevent fibril formation at physiological pH.
4.  **Renal Clearance:** Increasing the hydrodynamic radius through site-specific lipidation and molecular weighting.

---

#### **2. Modification Strategy: The "GHS-STAB" Framework**

The Glucogen-XR peptide sequence incorporates a triad of stability-enhancing modifications, collectively referred to as the "GHS-STAB" framework.

##### **2.1 DPP-IV Resistance via Alpha-Methyl Substitution**
The N-terminus of GLP-1 is the primary target for DPP-IV, which cleaves the $His^7-Ala^8$ dipeptide. In Glucogen-XR, the $Ala^8$ residue has been substituted with an unnatural amino acid, **Alpha-aminoisobutyric acid (Aib)**.

**Table 1: Comparative Kinetic Analysis of DPP-IV Degradation (GLUC-2025-001 vs. Native GLP-1)**
*Assay Conditions: 50 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.5, 37°C, Enzyme:Substrate ratio 1:1000.*

| Batch Number | Variant ID | Amino Acid at Position 8 | $k_{obs}$ ($min^{-1}$) | Half-life ($t_{1/2}$) in Human Plasma | Stability Improvement Factor |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| N/A | Native GLP-1 | L-Alanine | $0.345 \pm 0.02$ | 1.8 mins | 1.0x |
| GLUC-2025-001 | Glucogen-XR (Draft) | Aib | $0.00012 \pm 0.00001$ | > 168 hours | > 5,000x |
| GLUC-2025-002 | Glucogen-XR (GMP) | Aib | $0.00011 \pm 0.00001$ | > 168 hours | > 5,000x |

**Statistical Analysis of DPP-IV Resistance:**
The substitution of $Ala^8$ with Aib introduces steric hindrance at the $P_1'$ site. According to the Michaelis-Menten kinetics calculated during the GHS-V01 validation study:
$$V_{max} = \frac{k_{cat} \cdot [E]_0 \cdot [S]}{K_m + [S]}$$
Where $K_m$ for Glucogen-XR was found to be $>5000 \mu M$, effectively rendering the peptide a non-substrate for the enzyme.

---

#### **3. Site-Specific Lipidation and Linker Chemistry**
To achieve extended-release kinetics, Glucogen-XR utilizes a proprietary C18 di-acid fatty acid chain attached to $Lys^{26}$ via a $\gamma$-Glu-OEG-OEG linker.

##### **3.1 Linker Composition and Rationale**
The linker consists of:
*   **$\gamma$-Glutamic Acid ($\gamma$-Glu):** Enhances solubility and provides a negative charge to prevent peptide self-association.
*   **2x [2-(2-aminoethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid (OEG):** Provides flexibility and extends the reach of the fatty acid to facilitate optimal albumin binding.

##### **3.2 Albumin Binding Kinetics**
The C18 di-acid moiety facilitates non-covalent binding to Human Serum Albumin (HSA). This binding serves two purposes:
1.  **Protection:** Albumin masks the peptide from remaining circulating endopeptidases.
2.  **Retention:** The large molecular weight of the Glucogen-XR-Albumin complex (~70 kDa) prevents glomerular filtration.

**Table 2: Surface Plasmon Resonance (SPR) Data for Albumin Binding (Biacore T200)**
*Chip: CM5 Sensor Chip; Ligand: Recombinant Human Albumin (Batch HSA-2024-09).*

| Parameter | Batch GLUC-2025-010 | Batch GLUC-2025-011 | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| $k_a$ ($M^{-1}s^{-1}$) | $1.2 \times 10^4$ | $1.1 \times 10^4$ | $1.0 - 1.5 \times 10^4$ |
| $k_d$ ($s^{-1}$) | $8.5 \times 10^{-6}$ | $8.7 \times 10^{-6}$ | $\leq 1.0 \times 10^{-5}$ |
| $K_D$ (nM) | 0.708 | 0.791 | $< 1.0$ |

---

#### **4. Prevention of Asparagine Deamidation**
Native GLP-1 contains Asparagine at position 28 ($Asn^{28}$), which is prone to deamidation to $Asp$ or $iso-Asp$, leading to loss of potency. Glucogen-XR replaces this with Glutamine ($Gln^{28}$) or Glu ($Glu^{28}$) depending on the specific derivative profile. In the final clinical candidate, the substitution is $Asn^{28} \rightarrow Arg^{34}$ (shift in sequence numbering due to C-terminal expansion).

##### **4.1 Protocol for Deamidation Assessment (GHS-SOP-662)**
1.  **Incubation:** Buffer the drug substance at pH 9.0 (accelerated stress) for 72 hours at 40°C.
2.  **Digestion:** Perform Trypsin digestion (1:50 ratio) in $NH_4HCO_3$ buffer.
3.  **LC-MS Analysis:** Use Orbitrap Exploris 480 to detect mass shift of +0.984 Da.
4.  **Calculation:** 
    $$\% \text{Deamidation} = \frac{Area_{\text{deamidated}}}{Area_{\text{native}} + Area_{\text{deamidated}}} \times 100$$

**Table 3: Accelerated Deamidation Results (pH 9.0, 40°C)**

| Sample ID | 0 Hours | 24 Hours | 48 Hours | 72 Hours |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-015 | 0.02% | 0.15% | 0.32% | 0.45% |
| Native Reference | 0.15% | 4.50% | 12.80% | 22.10% |

---

#### **5. Physical Stability and Aggregation Inhibition**
Glucogen-XR is formulated at pH 7.4. To prevent the formation of $\beta$-sheet amyloid fibrils (common in GLP-1 peptides), the sequence was modified to increase net negative charge.

##### **5.1 Isoelectric Point (pI) Optimization**
The theoretical pI of Glucogen-XR was shifted from 5.2 (Native GLP-1) to 4.4 through the addition of the $\gamma$-Glu linker and the fatty acid tail. This ensures that at physiological pH (7.4), the peptide maintains a strong net negative charge, promoting electrostatic repulsion between monomers.

**Table 4: Dynamic Light Scattering (DLS) Characterization of Aggregation States**

| Batch Number | Concentration | Polydispersity Index (PdI) | Rh (Hydrodynamic Radius) | Interpretation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-020 | 1 mg/mL | 0.08 | 3.2 nm | Monodisperse |
| GLUC-2025-021 | 5 mg/mL | 0.12 | 3.5 nm | Monodisperse |
| GLUC-2025-022 | 10 mg/mL | 0.15 | 4.1 nm | Predominantly Monomeric |

---

#### **6. Regulatory Compliance and Quality Standards**
The stability enhancement strategies for Glucogen-XR comply with the following regulatory frameworks:
*   **ICH Q1A(R2):** Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.
*   **ICH Q5E:** Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products Subject to Changes in their Manufacturing Process.
*   **USP <121>:** Insulin Assays (as a benchmark for peptide hormonal stability).
*   **FDA Guidance:** "Guidance for Industry: Assay Development and Validation for Immunogenicity Testing of Therapeutic Protein Products."

##### **6.1 Forced Degradation Summary**
The stability of Glucogen-XR has been demonstrated under a variety of stress conditions, including photostability (ICH Q1B), thermal stress, and mechanical agitation. 

**Table 5: Forced Degradation Matrix (DS Batch GLUC-2025-100)**

| Stress Condition | Duration | Method | Result (Main Peak Recovery) | Key Degradant |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Acid (0.1M HCl) | 24h | RP-HPLC | 98.4% | Small C-term hydrolysis |
| Base (0.1M NaOH) | 24h | RP-HPLC | 96.2% | Deamidation products |
| Peroxide (3% $H_2O_2$) | 2h | LC-MS | 99.1% | Minimal Oxidation |
| Thermal (60°C) | 7 days | SEC | 97.5% | HMWP < 1.0% |
| Light (1.2M lux-hr) | Per ICH | RP-HPLC | 99.8% | No change |

---

#### **7. Conclusion of Rationale**
The cumulative effect of the $Aib^8$ substitution, $Lys^{26}$ lipidation via the $\gamma$-Glu-OEG-OEG linker, and $Arg^{34}$ substitution provides Glucogen-XR with unprecedented molecular stability. These enhancements not only support a once-weekly dosing regimen but also ensure the drug substance remains stable for up to 36 months under refrigerated conditions ($2-8^\circ C$) and 30 days at room temperature ($25^\circ C$), meeting the high quality and reliability standards expected of Google Health Sciences products.

***

**End of Section 3.2.S.1.2.2.1**

# PEGylation Strategy

## PEG Molecular Weight Selection

### 3.2.S.2.6 Manufacturing Process Development (Continued)
#### 3.2.S.2.6.4 PEGylation Strategy and Rationale
##### 3.2.S.2.6.4.1 PEG Molecular Weight Selection and Polydispersity Optimization

---

**Proprietary Information - Confidential**
**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-XR-M3-DS-0042
**Revision:** 01
**Author:** Global Regulatory Affairs, Google Health Sciences
**Date:** 24 May 2024

---

### 1.0 Executive Summary of PEG Selection
The selection of the polyethylene glycol (PEG) moiety for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) was a multi-factorial optimization process designed to balance pharmacological efficacy, renal clearance kinetics, subcutaneous absorption rates, and manufacturing scalability. Google Health Sciences (GHS) conducted an extensive "Matrix-Array" screening of linear and branched PEG architectures ranging from 5 kDa to 60 kDa. 

The finalized selection—a **40 kDa branched (Y-shaped) Methoxy-PEG-NHS ester**—was chosen based on its superior ability to shield the glucapeptide from dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) degradation while maintaining an optimal hydrodynamic radius ($R_h$) to prevent rapid glomerular filtration.

### 2.0 Technical Rationale for Molecular Weight (MW) Selection

#### 2.1 The "Goldilocks" Zone of Renal Clearance
The primary challenge in GLP-1 receptor agonist (GLP-1RA) therapy is the short half-life of the native peptide ($t_{1/2} \approx 2$ minutes). To achieve the Target Product Profile (TPP) of once-weekly subcutaneous dosing, the hydrodynamic volume of the Glucogen-XR conjugate must exceed the renal filtration threshold ($\approx 30$–50 kDa for globular proteins, but significantly higher for highly hydrated PEG chains).

GHS utilized the **Stokes-Einstein Equation** to correlate PEG MW with the hydrodynamic radius ($R_h$):

$$R_h = a(MW)^b$$

Where:
*   $R_h$ = Hydrodynamic radius in Angstroms ($\text{\AA}$)
*   $a$ = Pre-exponential factor (0.191 for branched PEG)
*   $b$ = Scaling exponent (0.58 for PEG in aqueous buffer)

**Table 1: Calculated vs. Observed Hydrodynamic Radii for Candidate PEG Constructs**

| PEG Architecture | Nominal MW (kDa) | Calculated $R_h$ ($\text{\AA}$) | Observed $R_h$ (DLS) ($\text{\AA}$) | Renal Clearance (mL/min/kg) | Human $t_{1/2}$ (Est.) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Linear | 5 | 18.4 | 19.1 | 1.45 | 4 hours |
| Linear | 10 | 27.5 | 28.3 | 0.82 | 12 hours |
| Linear | 20 | 41.2 | 43.5 | 0.12 | 48 hours |
| Branched (2-arm) | 30 | 51.8 | 54.1 | 0.04 | 96 hours |
| **Branched (2-arm)** | **40** | **61.4** | **63.8** | **<0.01** | **168 hours** |
| Branched (4-arm) | 60 | 78.2 | 81.4 | <0.01 | 192 hours |

*Footnote: The 40 kDa branched architecture (Batch GLUC-2025-PEG-P1) demonstrated the optimal balance between prolonged circulation and viscosity constraints for 29G needle subcutaneous delivery.*

---

### 3.0 Comparative Evaluation of PEG Chain Lengths (Study GHS-RD-2023-992)

#### 3.1 Study Objectives
To evaluate the impact of PEG MW on:
1.  **In-vitro Potency:** GLP-1 Receptor (GLP-1R) activation using a cAMP reporter gene assay.
2.  **Proteolytic Stability:** Resistance to DPP-4 and Neutral Endopeptidase (NEP) 24.11.
3.  **Viscosity:** Impact on high-concentration formulation (100 mg/mL).

#### 3.2 Data Matrix: Impact of PEG MW on Glucogen-XR Performance

| Batch Number | PEG MW | Architecture | PDI ($M_w/M_n$) | $EC_{50}$ (nM) | DPP-4 Stability ($t_{1/2}$ hr) | Viscosity @ 100 mg/mL (cP) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001A | 10 kDa | Linear | 1.02 | 0.045 | 12.4 | 2.1 |
| GLUC-2025-001B | 20 kDa | Linear | 1.03 | 0.120 | 28.9 | 5.8 |
| GLUC-2025-001C | 30 kDa | Branched | 1.04 | 0.210 | 44.1 | 12.4 |
| **GLUC-2025-001D** | **40 kDa** | **Branched** | **1.04** | **0.345** | **>72.0** | **18.2** |
| GLUC-2025-001E | 60 kDa | Branched | 1.06 | 1.250 | >72.0 | 45.9 |

**Detailed Analysis of Result GLUC-2025-001D:**
The 40 kDa branched variant showed a 7.6-fold reduction in $EC_{50}$ compared to native peptide (0.045 nM), which is an acceptable trade-off for the massive increase in metabolic stability. The viscosity of 18.2 cP at 100 mg/mL allows for comfortable patient self-administration using the Google Health Smart-Pen device.

---

### 4.0 Polydispersity Index (PDI) Optimization and Control

Per **ICH Q6B**, the heterogeneity of the polymer must be strictly controlled. Google Health Sciences has implemented a proprietary Ultra-Low PDI (ULP) synthesis protocol for the 40 kDa PEG-NHS ester.

#### 4.1 Specification Limits for PEG MW Distribution
The PEG starting material is sourced from a qualified vendor with the following rigorous specifications for Batch Series GLUC-2025-XXX:

1.  **Number Average Molecular Weight ($M_n$):** 38,500 – 41,500 Da
2.  **Weight Average Molecular Weight ($M_w$):** 39,000 – 42,000 Da
3.  **Polydispersity Index ($M_w/M_n$):** ≤ 1.05
4.  **Active Ester Substitution:** ≥ 98% (By 1H-NMR)

#### 4.2 Analytical Protocol for MW Determination (Method GHS-AN-0092)
**Equipment:** Agilent 1260 Infinity II GPC/SEC System with Multi-Angle Light Scattering (MALS) detector.

**Procedure:**
1.  **Column:** 2 x Shodex OHpak SB-804 HQ in series.
2.  **Mobile Phase:** 0.1M $NaNO_3$, 0.02% $NaN_3$.
3.  **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
4.  **Injection Volume:** 100 µL of 2 mg/mL sample.
5.  **Calibration:** NIST-traceable PEG standards (5 kDa to 100 kDa).

**Table 2: Validation of PEG MW Consistency across Clinical Batches**

| Batch Number | $M_n$ (Da) | $M_w$ (Da) | PDI | % Active Ester | Residual PEG-OH (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-010 | 39,920 | 40,810 | 1.022 | 99.1 | 0.4 |
| GLUC-2025-011 | 40,150 | 41,050 | 1.022 | 98.8 | 0.5 |
| GLUC-2025-012 | 39,880 | 40,790 | 1.023 | 99.4 | 0.3 |
| **Acceptance** | **38k-42k** | **39k-43k** | **<1.05** | **>98.0** | **<1.0** |

---

### 5.0 Justification for Branched vs. Linear Architecture

The selection of a **branched (Y-shaped)** 40 kDa PEG over a **linear** 40 kDa PEG was driven by the "Protective Umbrella" effect.

#### 5.1 Steric Shielding Calculations
Research conducted at Google Health Sciences' South San Francisco facility (Study GHS-ST-2024-01) demonstrated that the branched architecture provides a 40% larger "excluded volume" compared to a linear chain of identical MW. 

**Formula for Excluded Volume ($V_e$):**
$$V_e = \frac{4}{3} \pi (R_h)^3$$

*   **Linear 40 kDa:** $R_h \approx 48 \text{\AA} \rightarrow V_e \approx 463,000 \text{\AA}^3$
*   **Branched 40 kDa:** $R_h \approx 64 \text{\AA} \rightarrow V_e \approx 1,098,000 \text{\AA}^3$

This increased excluded volume significantly reduces the accessibility of proteolytic enzymes (DPP-4) to the N-terminal His-Gly motif of the glucapeptide, without fully blocking the GLP-1R binding pocket.

#### 5.2 Immunogenicity Considerations
Literature suggests that branched PEGs may exhibit lower immunogenicity (anti-PEG antibody formation) compared to linear PEGs of the same MW, due to the reduced visibility of the PEG backbone ends. Google Health Sciences clinical trial GLUC-CT-P1-002 monitored anti-PEG IgM/IgG titers; no significant treatment-emergent immunogenicity was observed in the 40 kDa branched cohort.

---

### 6.0 Manufacturing and Process Scale-up Stability
The 40 kDa PEG-NHS ester (GHS-PEG-40K-NHS) was evaluated for stability during the conjugation process (pH 8.5, 4°C).

#### 6.1 Hydrolysis Rate Protocol
**Method:** HPLC-CAD (Charged Aerosol Detection) to monitor the conversion of PEG-NHS to PEG-COOH (inactive).

**Step-by-Step Procedure:**
1.  Reconstitute 500 mg of PEG-NHS in 50 mL Sodium Borate Buffer (pH 8.5).
2.  Incubate at 4°C, 20°C, and 37°C.
3.  Withdraw 1 mL aliquots at T=0, 15, 30, 60, 120, 240 minutes.
4.  Quench with 10% TFA to pH 3.0.
5.  Analyze via Reverse-Phase HPLC.

**Table 3: Hydrolysis Half-life of 40 kDa PEG-NHS vs. Temperature**

| Temperature | $k_{obs}$ ($min^{-1}$) | Half-life ($t_{1/2}$) | Recommendation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **4°C** | **0.0028** | **247 minutes** | **Standard conjugation temp** |
| 20°C | 0.0154 | 45 minutes | Not recommended |
| 37°C | 0.0866 | 8 minutes | Avoid |

*Regulatory Note: Based on these data, the Glucogen-XR conjugation step is strictly controlled at 2-8°C, and the PEG addition is performed within 30 minutes of reconstitution to ensure >95% coupling efficiency (Refer to Section 3.2.S.2.2).*

---

### 7.0 References and Regulatory Compliance
1.  **US FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Liposome Drug Products: Chemistry, Manufacturing, and Controls; Human Pharmacokinetics and Bioavailability; and Labeling Documentation (2018)* - Applied by analogy for PEGylated proteins.
2.  **USP <731>:** Loss on Drying.
3.  **USP <789>:** Particulate Matter in Ophthalmic Solutions (Applied to SC injectables for PEG purity).
4.  **ICH Q1A(R2):** Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.
5.  **Google Health Internal Standard:** GHS-SOP-PEG-QUAL-01 (Qualification of PEG raw materials).
