---

## Conjugation Site Selection

### **Module 3: Quality - 3.2.S Drug Substance**
**Section: 3.2.S.2.6 Manufacturing Process Development**
**Sub-section: 2.6.4 PEGylation Strategy and Conjugation Site Selection**

---

#### **1.0 Introduction and Rationale for Site-Specific Conjugation**
The therapeutic efficacy of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is fundamentally dependent on the precise spatial orientation of the 40 kDa Methoxy-Polyethylene Glycol (mPEG) moiety. Unlike first-generation PEGylated biologics, which often utilized non-specific ε-amino group (Lysine) conjugation resulting in heterogeneous mixtures, Google Health Sciences (GHS) has implemented a site-specific conjugation strategy at the **Cys-32** residue of the glucapeptide backbone.

The selection of the conjugation site was driven by three primary objectives:
1.  **Preservation of Pharmacophore Integrity:** Ensuring the GLP-1 receptor-binding domain (His7 to Gly22) remains sterically accessible.
2.  **Optimization of Pharmacokinetics (PK):** Achieving a hydrodynamic radius ($R_h$) sufficient to exceed the renal glomerular filtration threshold (~30-50 kDa).
3.  **Stability and Immunogenicity:** Minimizing the exposure of potential neo-epitopes and preventing proteolytic degradation by Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-4).

---

#### **2.0 Comparative Evaluation of Potential Conjugation Sites**
During the Lead Optimization Phase (LOP-2023), six potential variants of the glucapeptide were synthesized using solid-phase peptide synthesis (SPPS) to evaluate the impact of PEG attachment points.

##### **Table 2.6.4-1: In Vitro Potency and PK Screening of PEGylation Site Variants**
| Variant ID | Conjugation Site | PEG Chemistry | EC50 (pM) [GLP-1R] | $T_{1/2}$ (Rat, hr) | $R_h$ (nm) | Purity (SEC-HPLC) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GHS-V1** | N-terminus (His7) | Amine/NHS | 450.2 ± 12 | 12.4 | 4.2 | 88.5% |
| **GHS-V2** | Lys26 | Amine/NHS | 112.8 ± 8 | 58.2 | 5.1 | 91.2% |
| **GHS-V3** | Lys34 | Amine/NHS | 95.4 ± 5 | 62.1 | 5.3 | 92.4% |
| **GHS-V4** | **Cys32 (Subst)** | **Maleimide/Thiol** | **18.5 ± 2** | **144.5** | **6.4** | **99.1%** |
| **GHS-V5** | Cys40 (Ext) | Maleimide/Thiol | 22.1 ± 3 | 140.2 | 6.5 | 98.7% |
| **GHS-V6** | Gln20 (Enz) | TGase/Azide | 255.0 ± 15 | 88.0 | 5.8 | 94.0% |

*Note: EC50 values were determined using a cAMP-based reporter gene assay in HEK293 cells expressing the human GLP-1 receptor. Data normalized to native GLP-1 (7-36) amide (EC50 = 12.0 pM).*

---

#### **3.0 Detailed Analysis of Site: Cys-32 (The Selected Site)**
The selection of Cys-32 (replacing the native Valine at position 32) was finalized based on Molecular Dynamics (MD) simulations performed on the Google Cloud Life Sciences High-Performance Computing (HPC) cluster.

##### **3.1 Structural Simulation and Steric Hindrance Mapping**
MD simulations (GROMACS 2023.1, OPLS-AA force field) indicated that a 40 kDa branched PEG at position 32 projects away from the $N$-terminal helices (residues 7-15) which are critical for receptor activation. 

**Calculated Solvent Accessible Surface Area (SASA):**
*   **Native Glucapeptide:** 3,240 Å²
*   **PEG-Cys32 Conjugate:** 12,450 Å² (Effective shielding of hydrophobic patches at residues 22-25)

##### **3.2 Impact on DPP-4 Susceptibility**
The proximity of the 40 kDa PEG at position 32 provides "umbrella shielding" over the Ala8-Glu9 peptide bond. 
*   **Protocol Ref:** GHS-SOP-QC-442 (In vitro DPP-4 degradation assay)
*   **Results:** Under standard conditions (37°C, 2 hours), Glucogen-XR showed <0.5% degradation, compared to >95% for native GLP-1.

---

#### **4.0 Conjugation Process Parameters and Characterization**
The conjugation utilizes a Michael Addition reaction between the free thiol of Cys-32 and a 40 kDa branched Maleimide-mPEG.

##### **4.1 Reaction Stoichiometry and Yield Data (Pivotal Batches)**
Optimization studies (Study Report GHS-RD-2024-012) determined that a molar ratio of 1:1.2 (Peptide:PEG) minimizes the presence of unreacted peptide while preventing the formation of multi-PEGylated impurities.

##### **Table 2.6.4-2: Conjugation Efficiency Across Clinical Manufacturing Batches**
| Batch Number | Scale (L) | Peptide Conc (g/L) | PEG:Peptide Ratio | Reaction Time (min) | Conversion (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 50 | 2.45 | 1.22:1 | 180 | 98.2% |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 50 | 2.44 | 1.20:1 | 185 | 98.5% |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 200 | 2.51 | 1.21:1 | 182 | 97.9% |
| **GLUC-2025-004** | 200 | 2.48 | 1.20:1 | 190 | 98.8% |

---

#### **5.0 Analytical Verification of Site Occupancy**
To confirm that PEGylation occurred exclusively at Cys-32, Google Health Sciences employs a "Mapping by Subtraction" technique using LC-MS/MS.

##### **5.1 Tryptic Digestion Protocol (GHS-SOP-AN-772)**
1.  **Denaturation:** 6M Guanidine HCl, pH 8.0.
2.  **Reduction/Alkylation:** (Omitted to preserve PEG-maleimide bond).
3.  **Digestion:** Tryptic/Glu-C protease mixture at 1:20 ratio, 16 hours at 37°C.
4.  **Analysis:** Orbitrap Fusion Lumos Mass Spectrometer.

**Analytical Results:**
The fragment $[T1-T3]$ (residues 7-26) was identified with high mass accuracy (< 2 ppm), showing no mass shift. The fragment $[T4]$ (residues 27-35) containing Cys-32 was notably absent from the UV chromatogram but appeared as a broad high-molecular-weight signal in the MS-Total Ion Chromatogram, confirming specific attachment.

---

#### **6.0 Critical Quality Attributes (CQA) Related to Site Selection**
The selection of Cys-32 impacts the following CQAs, which are monitored in the release specification (3.2.S.4.1):

1.  **Free PEG Content:** Managed by ultrafiltration/diafiltration (UF/DF) post-conjugation. Limit: ≤ 2.0%.
2.  **Unreacted Peptide:** Limit: ≤ 1.5% (determined by RP-HPLC).
3.  **Positional Isomers:** Because Cys-32 is the only cysteine in the sequence, positional isomerism is theoretically eliminated, enhancing product consistency compared to Lysine-based PEGylation.

---

#### **7.0 Regulatory Compliance and Guidelines**
The conjugation strategy was developed in alignment with:
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Non-Clinical Studies for the Development of Pharmaceutical Conjugates (2022).*
*   **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Proteins.

---

#### **8.0 Conclusion**
The selection of **Cys-32** for the attachment of the 40 kDa mPEG moiety in Glucogen-XR is scientifically justified through extensive computational modeling, in vitro bioactivity assays, and robust analytical characterization. This site-specific approach ensures maximum biological potency while achieving the long-acting pharmacokinetic profile required for once-weekly (or bi-monthly) administration in Type 2 Diabetes patients. The process has been proven scalable and reproducible across clinical batches (GLUC-2025-001 through 004).

---

## PEGylation Chemistry

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S DRUG SUBSTANCE)
## SECTION 3.2.S.2: MANUFACTURE
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.2.2: DESCRIPTION OF MANUFACTURING PROCESS AND PROCESS CONTROLS

---

# 3.2.S.2.2.8 PEGYLATION CHEMISTRY AND CONJUGATION STRATEGY

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND RATIONALE
The therapeutic efficacy of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is fundamentally dependent on the site-specific covalent attachment of a high-molecular-weight Polyethylene Glycol (PEG) moiety to the recombinant glucapeptide backbone. Google Health Sciences (GHS) utilizes a 40 kDa branched PEG-maleimide reagent to achieve precise conjugation at a genetically engineered C-terminal cysteine residue (Cys-31). This site-specific modification is designed to extend the terminal half-life of the peptide from minutes to approximately 168 hours, enabling a once-weekly dosing regimen.

The PEGylation process is executed under GMP conditions at the GHS South San Francisco facility (Building 4, Suite 202). This section details the chemical mechanisms, stoichiometry, process parameters, and analytical controls governing the transformation of the Glucogen Intermediate (GHS-GI-01) into the PEGylated Glucogen Bulk (GHS-GB-01).

---

#### 2.0 RAW MATERIAL SPECIFICATIONS: ACTIVATED PEG REAGENT
The starting material for the conjugation is a proprietary branched PEG derivative, designated as **GHS-PEG-40K-MAL**.

**Table 2.1: Specifications for 40 kDa Branched PEG-Maleimide (Lot: PEG-2025-ALPHA-01)**

| Parameter | Specification | Test Method | Typical Result (Batch 01) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | White to off-white powder | Visual Inspection | Conforms |
| **Identity (NMR)** | Matches reference spectrum | 1H-NMR (400 MHz) | Matches |
| **Average Mol. Weight (Mn)** | 38,000 – 42,000 Da | MALDI-TOF MS | 40,215 Da |
| **Polydispersity Index (PDI)** | ≤ 1.05 | GPC / SEC | 1.02 |
| **Maleimide Substitution** | ≥ 95.0% molar | 1H-NMR / Ellman's | 98.2% |
| **Free PEG Content** | < 2.0% | SEC-HPLC | 0.4% |
| **Residual Solvent (Toluene)** | < 890 ppm | GC-FID (USP <467>) | 110 ppm |
| **Endotoxin** | ≤ 0.5 EU/mg | LAL (USP <85>) | < 0.1 EU/mg |

---

#### 3.0 CHEMISTRY OF CONJUGATION
The conjugation of Glucogen-XR utilizes Michael addition chemistry. The maleimide functional group on the PEG reagent reacts selectively with the sulfhydryl (-SH) group of the C-terminal Cysteine (Cys-31) of the glucapeptide.

##### 3.1 Reaction Mechanism
The reaction is conducted at a controlled pH of 6.5 ± 0.2. At this pH, the nucleophilicity of the cysteine thiol is maximized relative to the ε-amino groups of lysine residues (pKa ~10.5) and the N-terminal amine, thereby ensuring site-specificity.

**Equation 3.1: Thiol-Maleimide Addition**
$$R-SH + \text{Maleimide-PEG} \rightarrow R-S-\text{Succinimide-PEG}$$

##### 3.2 Stoichiometry and Yield Calculations
The process is optimized at a molar ratio of 1.5:1 (PEG:Peptide).
*   **Target Peptide Mass:** 1000g (Batch Size)
*   **Theoretical Molar Equivalent:** $1000g / 3450 Da = 0.289 \text{ moles peptide}$
*   **PEG Required:** $0.289 \text{ moles} \times 1.5 \times 40,000 Da = 17,340g \text{ PEG}$

---

#### 4.0 DETAILED PEGYLATION PROTOCOL (PROCEDURE P-GHS-099)
The following protocol describes the commercial-scale conjugation process for a standard batch (e.g., GLUC-2025-001).

**Step 1: Intermediate Preparation and Thaw**
1.1 Retrieve frozen GHS-GI-01 (unconjugated peptide) from -80°C storage.
1.2 Thaw in a 25°C water bath for 4 hours until the solution reaches 20°C.
1.3 Transfer to a 100L Jacketed Stainless Steel Reactor (Equipment ID: REA-3001).

**Step 2: Buffer Exchange and pH Adjustment**
2.1 Exchange the storage buffer into Conjugation Buffer (50mM Sodium Phosphate, 2mM EDTA, pH 6.5) using Tangential Flow Filtration (TFF-101).
2.2 Target concentration: 10.0 mg/mL ± 0.5 mg/mL as determined by A280.
2.3 Verify pH using a calibrated Metrohm pH probe.

**Step 3: PEG Dissolution**
3.1 Weigh 17.34 kg of GHS-PEG-40K-MAL in a Class 100 laminar flow hood.
3.2 Dissolve PEG in 50L of Conjugation Buffer at 15-20°C under slow agitation (60 RPM) to prevent foaming.

**Step 4: Conjugation Reaction**
4.1 Initiate the addition of PEG solution to the Reactor REA-3001 at a flow rate of 1.5 L/min.
4.2 Maintain temperature at 22°C ± 2°C using the jacketed glycol system.
4.3 Agitate at 45 RPM for 4 hours.
4.4 Monitor reaction progress via IPC-SEC-HPLC at T=0, T=60, T=120, and T=240 minutes.

**Step 5: Quenching**
5.1 Quench the reaction by adding L-Cysteine HCl to a final concentration of 5mM.
5.2 Stir for 30 minutes to ensure all unreacted maleimide-PEG is deactivated.

---

#### 5.0 IN-PROCESS CONTROLS (IPC) AND STABILITY DATA
Critical Process Parameters (CPPs) and In-Process Tests (IPTs) are monitored to ensure consistent conjugation efficiency.

**Table 5.1: In-Process Control Limits for Conjugation (Batch GLUC-2025-001 through 003)**

| IPC ID | Parameter | Acceptance Criteria | Method | Result (GLUC-2025-001) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **IPC-01** | Peptide Conc. | 9.5 – 10.5 mg/mL | UV/Vis A280 | 10.1 mg/mL |
| **IPC-02** | pH Post-Adj. | 6.4 – 6.6 | Potentiometric | 6.52 |
| **IPC-03** | Conjugation Yield | ≥ 85.0% | SEC-HPLC | 91.2% |
| **IPC-04** | Residual Peptide | ≤ 5.0% | RP-HPLC | 1.8% |
| **IPC-05** | Di-PEGylated Imp. | ≤ 2.0% | SEC-HPLC | 0.4% |

---

#### 6.0 ANALYTICAL CHARACTERIZATION OF PEGYLATED SPECIES
Characterization of the PEGylated product is performed using a multi-orthogonal approach to confirm site-occupancy and PEG chain integrity.

##### 6.1 SEC-HPLC Analysis
The SEC-HPLC method (GHS-ANA-METH-04) utilizes a Tosoh TSKgel G4000SWxl column to separate the mono-PEGylated Glucogen-XR from high-molecular-weight aggregates and residual peptide.
*   **Mobile Phase:** 0.1M Sodium Phosphate, 0.2M NaCl, pH 7.0.
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
*   **Retention Time (Mono-PEG):** ~14.2 minutes.

##### 6.2 MALDI-TOF Mass Spectrometry
MALDI-TOF is utilized to confirm the molecular weight distribution. A broad peak centered at 43,450 Da confirms the addition of one 40 kDa PEG chain to the 3,450 Da peptide.

##### 6.3 Peptide Mapping with LC-MS/MS
Trypsin digestion of the PEGylated peptide followed by LC-MS/MS confirms that the C-terminal fragment (Gly-22 to Cys-31) carries the PEG moiety. The absence of PEGylation on the N-terminal fragment (His-1 to Lys-12) confirms the high regioselectivity of the maleimide-thiol reaction.

---

#### 7.0 PROCESS VALIDATION AND ROBUSTNESS
To ensure the robustness of the PEGylation chemistry, a Design of Experiments (DoE) study was conducted varying pH (6.0 – 7.0), temperature (15 – 30°C), and molar ratio (1.0 – 2.0).

**Table 7.1: DoE Results for Conjugation Efficiency**

| Run | pH | Temp (°C) | Molar Ratio | Yield (%) | Di-PEG (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | 6.0 | 15 | 1.2 | 78.4 | 0.1 |
| 2 | 7.0 | 15 | 1.2 | 82.1 | 0.8 |
| 3 | 6.0 | 30 | 1.8 | 89.5 | 1.2 |
| 4 | 7.0 | 30 | 1.8 | 94.2 | 3.5 (OOS) |
| **5 (CP)** | **6.5** | **22** | **1.5** | **91.8** | **0.5** |

*Note: High pH (>6.8) combined with high temperature and molar ratio leads to an increase in undesirable di-PEGylated species due to amine reactivity.*

---

#### 8.0 STORAGE AND HOLD TIMES
The crude PEGylated reaction mixture is stable at 2-8°C for up to 48 hours prior to downstream purification. Stability data (Table 8.1) shows no significant degradation or de-PEGylation (retro-Michael reaction) within this window.

**Table 8.1: Hold Time Stability for Crude PEGylated Intermediate (Lot: GLUC-2025-VAL-01)**

| Time Point | Purity (SEC) | Residual Peptide (%) | pH | Endotoxin (EU/mL) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T=0 | 92.1% | 1.9% | 6.51 | < 0.05 |
| T=24h | 92.0% | 2.0% | 6.52 | < 0.05 |
| T=48h | 91.8% | 2.1% | 6.50 | 0.06 |

---

#### 9.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDELINES
This conjugation process is designed in accordance with:
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **ICH Q11:** Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances.
3.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Nonclinical Studies for the Development of Pharmaceutical Conjugates (Draft 2021).
4.  **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Monoclonal Antibodies (for relevant SEC-HPLC parameters).

---

#### 10.0 CONCLUSION
The PEGylation chemistry employed for Glucogen-XR provides a highly reproducible, site-specific modification that is essential for the product's extended-release profile. Through rigorous control of pH, stoichiometry, and temperature, Google Health Sciences ensures that each batch of Glucogen-XR meets the stringent purity and potency requirements mandated for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapy.

**End of Subsection 3.2.S.2.2.8**

---

# Elucidation of Structure

## Primary Structure Confirmation

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.3.1)
## SECTION: ELUCIDATION OF STRUCTURE AND OTHER CHARACTERISTICS
### SUBSECTION: 3.2.S.3.1.1 PRIMARY STRUCTURE CONFIRMATION (Glucogen-XR)

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection provides a comprehensive characterization of the primary structure of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist produced by Google Health Sciences (GHS). The primary structure confirmation was conducted in accordance with **ICH Guideline Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q11** (Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances).

The drug substance, Glucogen-XR, consists of a 31-amino acid peptide sequence derived from human GLP-1(7-37), modified at position 8 (Ala to Aib) to confer resistance to Dipeptidyl Peptidase-4 (DPP-4) degradation, and further conjugated to a proprietary 40 kDa branched polyethylene glycol (PEG) moiety via a C-terminal lysine spacer to achieve the extended-release profile.

The characterization studies described herein utilize three (3) independent primary batches (GLUC-2025-001, GLUC-2025-002, and GLUC-2025-003) to demonstrate manufacturing consistency and structural integrity.

---

#### 2.0 AMINO ACID SEQUENCE ANALYSIS
The amino acid sequence of Glucogen-XR was verified using a multi-orthogonal approach, combining automated Edman degradation, High-Resolution Mass Spectrometry (HRMS), and Peptide Mapping by LC-MS/MS.

##### 2.1 N-Terminal Sequencing (Edman Degradation)
N-terminal sequencing was performed to confirm the identity of the first 25 residues and to ensure the absence of N-terminal truncation or alternative processing.

**2.1.1 Methodology**
Analysis was conducted using a Shimadzu PPSQ-53A Protein Sequencer utilizing Automated Edman Degradation. Samples (approx. 500 pmol) were loaded onto a polybrene-treated glass fiber filter. Phenylthiohydantoin (PTH) amino acids were separated by reverse-phase HPLC.

**Table 2.1.1-1: N-Terminal Sequence Results (Batch GLUC-2025-001)**
| Cycle | Observed PTH-AA | Predicted AA | Retention Time (min) | Yield (pmol) | Confidence (%) |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Histidine (H) | His | 4.12 | 412.5 | 99.8 |
| 2 | Aib* | Aib | 5.34 | 388.2 | 99.1 |
| 3 | Glutamic Acid (E) | Glu | 7.82 | 365.4 | 99.5 |
| 4 | Glycine (G) | Gly | 9.11 | 340.1 | 98.9 |
| 5 | Threonine (T) | Thr | 10.45 | 322.8 | 98.4 |
| ... | ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |
| 25 | Tryptophan (W) | Trp | 28.55 | 112.4 | 97.2 |

*\*Note: Alpha-aminoisobutyric acid (Aib) was identified via a custom PTH-standard calibration curve.*

##### 2.2 Peptide Mapping by LC-MS/MS
Complete sequence coverage was achieved through enzymatic digestion followed by Liquid Chromatography with Tandem Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS).

**2.2.1 Proteolytic Digestion Protocol**
1. **Denaturation:** 100 µg of Glucogen-XR was dissolved in 6M Guanidine-HCl, 50 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0).
2. **Reduction:** Addition of 10 mM Dithiothreitol (DTT) at 56°C for 45 minutes.
3. **Alkylation:** Addition of 25 mM Iodoacetamide (IAM) at room temperature in the dark for 30 minutes.
4. **Desalting:** Buffer exchange into 50 mM Ammonium Bicarbonate (pH 7.8) using Zeba Spin Columns.
5. **Digestion:** Samples were digested using Trypsin (Gold, Mass Spec Grade) at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio at 37°C for 16 hours. A secondary digestion using Glu-C was performed on a separate aliquot to confirm the mid-chain sequences.

**2.2.2 Instrumentation**
*   **LC:** Thermo Scientific Vanquish UHPLC
*   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY BEH C18 (1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm)
*   **MS:** Thermo Scientific Orbitrap Exploris 480
*   **Software:** BioPharma Finder™ 4.1

**Table 2.2.2-1: Identified Tryptic and Glu-C Peptides**
| Fragment ID | Sequence | Observed m/z (z=2) | Theoretical m/z | Mass Error (ppm) | Method |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| T1 | H(Aib)EGTFTSDVSSYLEGQAAK | 984.4752 | 984.4761 | -0.9 | Trypsin |
| T2 | EFIAWLVK | 496.2891 | 496.2885 | 1.2 | Trypsin |
| T3 | GRG-PEG40k | N/A (Polymer) | N/A | N/A | MALDI-TOF |
| G1 | H(Aib)E | 369.1765 | 369.1774 | -2.4 | Glu-C |
| G2 | GTFTSDVSSYLE | 652.3114 | 652.3108 | 0.9 | Glu-C |

---

#### 3.0 MOLECULAR WEIGHT DETERMINATION
The molecular weight of the Glucogen-XR peptide backbone and the intact glyco-conjugated form was determined using Matrix-Assisted Laser Desorption/Ionization Time-of-Flight (MALDI-TOF) and ESI-MS.

##### 3.1 Intact Mass Analysis (De-PEGylated Control)
To confirm the protein backbone mass independently of the polydisperse PEG moiety, a controlled chemical cleavage of the PEG linker was performed for analytical purposes on batch GLUC-2025-002.

**Table 3.1-1: Intact Mass Spectrometry Data**
| Batch Number | Calculated Neutral Mass (Da) | Observed Mass (Da) | Delta (Da) | Interpretation |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| GLUC-2025-001 | 3298.63 | 3298.65 | +0.02 | Matches Sequence |
| GLUC-2025-002 | 3298.63 | 3298.61 | -0.02 | Matches Sequence |
| GLUC-2025-003 | 3298.63 | 3298.64 | +0.01 | Matches Sequence |

---

#### 4.0 AMINO ACID COMPOSITION ANALYSIS
Amino acid composition analysis was performed to confirm the molar ratios of the constituent amino acids in Glucogen-XR.

**4.1.1 Procedure (USP <121.1>)**
Samples were hydrolyzed in 6N HCl at 110°C for 24, 48, and 72 hours under vacuum. Cysteine and Methionine were determined following performic acid oxidation. Tryptophan was determined after hydrolysis with 4M methanesulfonic acid containing 0.2% 3-(2-aminoethyl)indole.

**Table 4.1.1-1: Amino Acid Molar Ratios (Theoretical vs. Observed)**
| Amino Acid | Theoretical Number | Observed (GLUC-2025-001) | Deviation (%) |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| Asp/Asn (Asx) | 1 | 1.02 | +2.0 |
| Glu/Gln (Glx) | 4 | 3.98 | -0.5 |
| Ser | 3 | 2.89 | -3.6 |
| Gly | 3 | 3.05 | +1.6 |
| His | 1 | 0.97 | -3.0 |
| Aib | 1 | 1.00 | 0.0 |
| Thr | 2 | 1.94 | -3.0 |
| Ala | 2 | 2.03 | +1.5 |
| Tyr | 1 | 0.99 | -1.0 |
| Val | 2 | 1.96 | -2.0 |
| Phe | 1 | 1.01 | +1.0 |
| Ile | 1 | 0.98 | -2.0 |
| Leu | 2 | 2.02 | +1.0 |
| Lys | 2 | 1.99 | -0.5 |
| Arg | 1 | 1.02 | +2.0 |
| Trp | 1 | 0.91* | -9.0 |

*\*Tryptophan recovery is characteristically lower due to degradation during acid hydrolysis; values within 10% of theoretical are considered acceptable.*

---

#### 5.0 PEGYLATION SITE CONFIRMATION
The site of attachment for the 40 kDa branched PEG moiety was confirmed to be the C-terminal Lysine (Lys34) via Peptide Mapping and MS/MS fragmentation (CID).

**5.1 Fragment Ion Analysis**
Fragmentation of the C-terminal peptide (T3: GRG-Lys-PEG) showed a characteristic mass shift of +40,000 Da (average) associated with the Lysine residue. No PEGylation was observed at Lys26, confirming the regioselectivity of the conjugation reaction (Yield >99.5%).

---

#### 6.0 SPECTROSCOPIC CHARACTERIZATION
To ensure the primary structure is folded correctly into its secondary and tertiary conformations (which are dependent on the primary sequence), Circular Dichroism (CD) and FTIR were employed.

##### 6.1 Circular Dichroism (CD)
*   **Far-UV CD (190-250 nm):** Evaluates $\alpha$-helical content.
*   **Instrument:** Jasco J-1500.
*   **Results:** The spectrum for Glucogen-XR shows characteristic minima at 208 nm and 222 nm, consistent with a high $\alpha$-helical content (approx. 45% in 50% TFE/water).

---

#### 7.0 BATCH ANALYSIS SUMMARY (PRIMARY STRUCTURE)
Data from three consecutive conformance batches demonstrate that the primary structure is consistent and meets all pre-defined specifications.

**Table 7.0-1: Summary of Primary Structure Confirmation Across Batches**
| Parameter | Method | GLUC-2025-001 | GLUC-2025-002 | GLUC-2025-003 |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| **Sequence** | LC-MS/MS | Confirmed | Confirmed | Confirmed |
| **N-Terminus** | Edman | H-Aib-E-G... | H-Aib-E-G... | H-Aib-E-G... |
| **Purity** | RP-HPLC | 99.4% | 99.2% | 99.5% |
| **PEG Site** | MS/MS | Lys34 | Lys34 | Lys34 |
| **Main Band** | SDS-PAGE | Conforms | Conforms | Conforms |

---

#### 8.0 CONCLUSION
The primary structure of Glucogen-XR has been rigorously confirmed through multiple orthogonal analytical techniques. The amino acid sequence is as predicted from the GHS-CHO-001 cell line genetic construct, including the site-specific Aib substitution and C-terminal PEGylation. The data provided in this section demonstrate that Google Health Sciences maintains high-level control over the structural integrity of Glucogen-XR.

## PEG Attachment Site Mapping

### 3.2.S.3.1.2.4 PEG Attachment Site Mapping (Glucogen-XR)

#### 1.0 Executive Summary
The site-specific conjugation of a 40 kDa branched Polyethylene Glycol (PEG) moiety to the Glucogen-XR peptide backbone is a critical quality attribute (CQA) that ensures the extended-release pharmacokinetics and metabolic stability of the therapeutic. Glucogen-XR is a GLP-1 receptor agonist synthesized as a 31-amino acid peptide analog. To achieve the required half-life extension, a maleimide-functionalized PEG is covalently attached to a genetically engineered cysteine residue at position 24 (Cys24) of the sequence.

This section provides an exhaustive characterization of the PEG attachment site, confirming the high regioselectivity of the conjugation reaction, the absence of positional isomers, and the structural integrity of the peptide-linker-PEG interface. Analysis was performed on three primary registration batches (**GLUC-2025-001**, **GLUC-2025-002**, and **GLUC-2025-003**) using a multi-orthogonal approach involving bottom-up Liquid Chromatography-Tandem Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS), N-terminal sequencing, and enzymatic mapping.

#### 2.0 Theoretical Basis and Site Selection
The selection of the attachment site at position 24 was based on extensive Quantitative Structure-Activity Relationship (QSAR) modeling and crystal structure analysis of the GLP-1 receptor-ligand complex. 

*   **Sequence:** HAEGTFTSDVSSYLEGQAAK**C**(PEG)EFIAWLVRGRG
*   **Target Residue:** Cys24 (Engineered)
*   **Chemistry:** Thiol-maleimide Michael addition
*   **Calculated Monoisotopic Mass (Peptide):** 3,384.62 Da
*   **Calculated Nominal Mass (Conjugate):** ~43,385 Da (based on 40 kDa polydisperse PEG)

#### 3.0 Analytical Methodology: Multi-Attribute Site Mapping

##### 3.1 Orthogonal Strategy Overview
Due to the significant mass and polydispersity of the 40 kDa PEG moiety, traditional intact mass spectrometry is insufficient to confirm site-specific occupancy with the precision required for regulatory filing. Google Health Sciences employs the following hierarchical testing strategy:

1.  **Enzymatic Digestion (Trypsin/Glu-C):** Release of the PEGylated fragment from the peptide backbone.
2.  **Size-Exclusion Chromatography (SEC)-LC-MS/MS:** Separation of the large PEG-peptide fragment from non-PEGylated fragments.
3.  **Collision-Induced Dissociation (CID) and Electron Transfer Dissociation (ETD):** Fragmenting the peptide backbone while maintaining the PEG linkage.
4.  **MALDI-TOF MS:** High-resolution mass profiling of the isolated PEG-peptide fragment.

##### 3.2 Protocol: Tryptic Mapping of PEGylated Glucogen-XR
**Equipment:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC I-Class coupled to a Thermo Scientific Orbitrap Exploris 480 MS.
**Software:** Chromeleon 7.3 CDS and BioPharma Finder 4.1.

**Procedure Step-by-Step:**
1.  **Sample Preparation:** Dilute 500 µg of Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-001) in 100 mM Tris-HCl buffer (pH 7.5).
2.  **Denaturation:** Add 6M Guanidine-HCl. Incubate at 37°C for 30 minutes.
3.  **Reduction/Alkylation (Negative Control Check):** While the Cys24 is conjugated, a separate aliquot is treated with 10 mM DTT followed by 20 mM Iodoacetamide to ensure no free thiols exist on the backbone.
4.  **Digestion:** Add Sequencing Grade Modified Trypsin at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio. Incubate for 16 hours at 37°C.
5.  **Quenching:** Add 10% Trifluoroacetic acid (TFA) to reach pH 2.0.
6.  **UPLC Conditions:** 
    *   Column: C18 1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm.
    *   Mobile Phase A: 0.1% FA in Water.
    *   Mobile Phase B: 0.1% FA in Acetonitrile.
    *   Gradient: 5% B to 65% B over 60 minutes.

#### 4.0 Results: Identification of the PEGylated Peptide Fragment

Analysis of the tryptic digest yields a specific "gap" in the UV chromatogram at the expected elution time of the T3 fragment (residues 21-26: `AAKCEF`), which is shifted to a higher elution volume (or remains at the solvent front depending on column chemistry) due to the PEG moiety.

**Table 1: Predicted vs. Observed Tryptic Fragments of Glucogen-XR**

| Fragment ID | Amino Acid Sequence | Theoretical Mass (Da) | Observed Mass (m/z) | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **T1** | HAEGTFTSDVSSY | 1414.61 | 708.31 (z=2) | Confirmed |
| **T2** | LEGQAAK | 686.36 | 344.19 (z=2) | Confirmed |
| **T3-PEG** | **EFIAWLVR** | **43,000 - 45,000** | **Polydisperse Envelope** | **Conjugated Site** |
| **T4** | GR | 231.13 | 116.57 (z=2) | Confirmed |
| **T5** | G | 75.03 | N/A | Detected (MS/MS) |

*Note: The Cys24 residue is located within the peptide sequence that spans the junction of the T3 region. Due to the PEGylation, the tryptic cleavage site at Lys20 and Arg28 provides a specific PEG-containing peptide fragment.*

#### 5.0 Quantitative Analysis of Site Occupancy (Positional Isomerism)
A critical regulatory concern is the potential for "off-target" conjugation to other nucleophilic residues (e.g., Lysine residues at positions 12, 16, or 20). 

##### 5.1 MS/MS Fragmentation Analysis
To confirm position 24 exclusively, ETD fragmentation was utilized. Unlike CID, ETD preserves the labile PEG-maleimide-cysteine bond, allowing for the mapping of c- and z-type ions.

**Table 2: ETD Fragment Ion Analysis for Fragment T3 (AAKCEFIAWLVR)**
*Batch Analyzed: GLUC-2025-001*

| Ion Type | Theoretical m/z (Non-PEG) | Observed m/z (PEGylated) | Mass Delta (Da) | Conclusion |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| c1 (A) | 72.04 | 72.04 | 0 | No PEG |
| c2 (AA) | 143.08 | 143.08 | 0 | No PEG |
| c3 (AAK) | 271.18 | 271.18 | 0 | No PEG |
| **c4 (AAKC)** | **374.19** | **~40,374** | **~40,000** | **PEG Detected** |
| z1 (R) | 175.12 | 175.12 | 0 | No PEG |
| z2 (VR) | 274.19 | 274.19 | 0 | No PEG |
| z3 (LVR) | 387.27 | 387.27 | 0 | No PEG |

The shift in mass observed exclusively starting at the **c4** ion and remaining through the sequence confirms that the 40 kDa PEG is covalently attached to **Cys24**.

#### 6.0 Comparative Batch Data (GLUC-2025-XXX Series)
Data from three consecutive drug substance batches demonstrate the consistency of the conjugation process.

**Table 3: Summary of Site-Specific Conjugation Consistency**

| Batch Number | Manufacturing Date | Site Purity (Cys24) | Free Peptide (%) | Off-Target Lys-PEG (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 12-JAN-2025 | 99.8% | < 0.1% (LOD) | < 0.1% (LOD) |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 19-JAN-2025 | 99.7% | < 0.1% (LOD) | 0.12% |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 26-JAN-2025 | 99.9% | < 0.1% (LOD) | < 0.1% (LOD) |
| **Specification** | **N/A** | **≥ 98.0%** | **≤ 1.0%** | **≤ 0.5%** |

#### 7.0 Statistical Evaluation of Linker Stability
The maleimide-thiol bond is subject to potential retro-Michael reactions. Stability studies were conducted at pH 7.4 (physiological) and pH 4.0 (storage).

*   **Calculation of De-PEGylation Rate:**
    $k_{obs} = \ln(Area_{t0} / Area_{tn}) / t$
    Where $Area$ represents the peak area of the PEGylated T3 fragment.

The calculated degradation rate at 5°C is $1.2 \times 10^{-6} hr^{-1}$, supporting a shelf-life of over 24 months with minimal loss of the PEG moiety.

#### 8.0 Conclusion
The PEG attachment site mapping studies definitively confirm that for Glucogen-XR, the 40 kDa branched PEG is conjugated exclusively to Cys24. The use of ETD-MS/MS provides high-confidence sequence coverage, and batch-to-batch analysis demonstrates that the Google Health Sciences manufacturing process is highly controlled, yielding a homogeneous product with negligible positional isomers or unreacted species. This profile supports the safety and efficacy of the GLP-1 receptor agonist by ensuring a uniform pharmacokinetic profile.

#### 9.0 References
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Proteins.
3.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Liposome Drug Products (2018) - *Referenced for polydispersity standards.*
4.  Roberts, M. J., et al. (2012). "Chemistry for Peptide and Protein PEGylation." *Advanced Drug Delivery Reviews.*

---

## Higher-Order Structure Analysis

### 3.2.S.3.1.2 Higher-Order Structure (HOS) Analysis

The higher-order structure (HOS) of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is a critical quality attribute (CQA) directly linked to its pharmacodynamic profile as a GLP-1 receptor agonist. Given the complex nature of the glucapeptide sequence and the proprietary extended-release motifs incorporated by Google Health Sciences, HOS analysis is performed to ensure the three-dimensional conformation (secondary, tertiary, and quaternary structure) is consistent across clinical and commercial batches (GLUC-2025-XXX series).

Any perturbation in the HOS—specifically the transition from an alpha-helical conformation to a beta-sheet-rich aggregate—can significantly impact receptor binding affinity, metabolic stability, and immunogenic potential.

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.1 Secondary Structure Assessment by Far-UV Circular Dichroism (CD)

Circular Dichroism (CD) spectroscopy is utilized to characterize the secondary structural elements of Glucogen-XR. The glucapeptide backbone exhibits a characteristic spectrum in the far-UV region (190–250 nm), primarily dominated by alpha-helical and random coil contributions.

**A. Instrumentation and Parameters**
Measurements were conducted using a Jasco J-1500 Spectropolarimeter (Equipment ID: GHS-ANA-CD-04) equipped with a Peltier temperature controller.

| Parameter | Specification/Value |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Wavelength Range** | 190 nm to 260 nm |
| **Data Pitch** | 0.1 nm |
| **Bandwidth** | 1.0 nm |
| **Response Time** | 1.0 second |
| **Scanning Speed** | 20 nm/min |
| **Accumulations** | 5 scans (averaged) |
| **Cell Pathlength** | 0.1 mm (High-precision Quartz) |
| **Sample Concentration** | 0.5 mg/mL (diluted in 10 mM Sodium Phosphate, pH 7.4) |
| **Temperature** | 25°C ± 0.1°C |

**B. Data Processing and Secondary Structure Deconvolution**
Raw ellipticity ($\theta$, in mdeg) is converted to Mean Residue Ellipticity ($[\theta]_{MRE}$) using the following formula:

$$[\theta]_{MRE} = \frac{\theta_{obs} \cdot MRW}{10 \cdot l \cdot c}$$

Where:
*   $\theta_{obs}$ = Observed ellipticity (mdeg)
*   $MRW$ = Mean Residue Weight (Molecular Weight / Number of amino acids)
*   $l$ = Pathlength (cm)
*   $c$ = Concentration (mg/mL)

Secondary structure fractions were calculated using the CONTIN/LL algorithm via the SELCON3 protein secondary structure analysis package (Reference: Sreerama & Woody, 2000).

**C. Comparative Batch Analysis (Table 3.2.S.3.1.2-1)**

| Batch Number | Alpha-Helix (%) | Beta-Sheet (%) | Turns (%) | Unordered (%) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 48.2 | 12.1 | 14.5 | 25.2 | Conformant |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 47.9 | 12.4 | 14.2 | 25.5 | Conformant |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 48.5 | 11.9 | 14.8 | 24.8 | Conformant |
| **GLUC-2025-004** | 48.1 | 12.0 | 14.6 | 25.3 | Conformant |
| **Mean (n=4)** | **48.18** | **12.10** | **14.53** | **25.20** | N/A |
| **SD** | 0.25 | 0.22 | 0.25 | 0.29 | N/A |

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.2 Tertiary Structure Assessment by Near-UV CD and Intrinsic Fluorescence

To ensure the correct folding and orientation of the aromatic side chains (Tyrosine and Tryptophan) within the Glucogen-XR peptide, Near-UV CD and Intrinsic Fluorescence are employed.

**A. Near-UV CD (250–320 nm)**
Near-UV CD provides a fingerprint of the tertiary environment of aromatic residues. For Glucogen-XR, the spectrum is dominated by the Trp residues at positions 25 and 31 (relative to the GLP-1 consensus sequence).

*   **Protocol:** Samples are prepared at 2.0 mg/mL. A 1.0 cm pathlength cell is used to maximize signal-to-noise ratio.
*   **Observation:** A distinct negative cotton effect is observed at 280-290 nm, indicative of a constrained hydrophobic environment for the Tryptophan residues, confirming the "closed" tertiary conformation required for receptor docking.

**B. Intrinsic Fluorescence (Tryptophan Fluorescence)**
Fluorescence spectroscopy (Agilent Cary Eclipse, GHS-ANA-FL-09) is used to monitor the solvent accessibility of the indole ring.

*   **Excitation Wavelength:** 280 nm
*   **Emission Range:** 300–450 nm
*   **Parameters:** Slit widths set to 5 nm; Scan speed 120 nm/min.

| Batch Number | Emission Max ($\lambda_{max}$) | Intensity (A.U.) | Quenching Constant ($K_{sv}$)* |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 334.2 nm | 842.1 | 1.12 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 334.5 nm | 839.8 | 1.14 |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 334.1 nm | 845.5 | 1.10 |
| **Reference Std** | 334.3 nm | 841.0 | 1.11 |

*\*Stern-Volmer quenching constant ($K_{sv}$) determined using Acrylamide as a neutral quencher to assess surface exposure.*

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.3 Fourier Transform Infrared (FTIR) Spectroscopy

FTIR serves as an orthogonal method to CD for the quantification of secondary structure, specifically focusing on the Amide I (1600–1700 cm⁻¹) and Amide II (1510–1580 cm⁻¹) bands. This is particularly relevant for the "Extended Release" formulation where the peptide exists at high concentrations.

**A. Analytical Procedure (Attenuated Total Reflection - ATR-FTIR)**
1.  **Equipment:** Bruker Tensor II with a BioATR II cell.
2.  **Background:** 128 scans against formulation buffer.
3.  **Sample:** 20 $\mu$L of Glucogen-XR (20 mg/mL).
4.  **Processing:** Second derivative analysis and Fourier self-deconvolution (FSD) used to resolve overlapping sub-components.

**B. Component Band Assignment**
*   **1650–1658 cm⁻¹:** Alpha-helix (Primary Peak for Glucogen-XR)
*   **1620–1640 cm⁻¹:** Beta-sheet (Indicative of aggregation if >15%)
*   **1660–1670 cm⁻¹:** 3₁₀-helices / Beta-turns
*   **1640–1648 cm⁻¹:** Random Coil

| Batch ID | Alpha-helix Area (%) | Beta-sheet Area (%) | Disordered Area (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 51.2 | 8.4 | 40.4 |
| GLUC-2025-005 | 50.9 | 8.7 | 40.4 |
| **Specification** | **45.0 – 55.0%** | **< 12.0%** | **Report Results** |

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.4 Thermal Stability and Conformational Flexibility (DSC)

Differential Scanning Calorimetry (DSC) is utilized to determine the melting temperature ($T_m$) and the enthalpy of unfolding ($\Delta H$). This provides a quantitative measure of the thermodynamic stability of the glucapeptide.

**A. Methodology**
*   **Instrument:** Malvern MicroCal PEAQ-DSC.
*   **Scan Rate:** 60°C/hour.
*   **Temperature Range:** 10°C to 110°C.
*   **Buffer Matching:** Identical lot of formulation buffer used in the reference cell.

**B. Thermodynamic Data (Table 3.2.S.3.1.2-2)**

| Batch Number | $T_{m1}$ (°C) | $T_{m2}$ (°C)* | $\Delta H$ (kcal/mol) | $\Delta C_p$ (cal/mol·K) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 68.4 | 84.1 | 142.5 | 2.1 |
| GLUC-2025-002 | 68.2 | 83.9 | 140.9 | 2.0 |
| GLUC-2025-003 | 68.5 | 84.2 | 143.2 | 2.2 |

*\*Note: $T_{m2}$ corresponds to the dissociation of the extended-release hydrophobic motif, unique to the Glucogen-XR construct.*

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.5 High-Resolution NMR Spectroscopy (Fingerprinting)

For Glucogen-XR, 1D ¹H-NMR and 2D ¹H-¹⁵N HSQC (at natural abundance or ¹⁵N-labeled pilot batches) are used as high-resolution "fingerprints" to ensure atomic-level conformational consistency.

**A. Parameters for 1D ¹H-NMR**
*   **Field Strength:** 600 MHz (Bruker Avance III).
*   **Solvent:** 90% $H_2O$ / 10% $D_2O$.
*   **Pulse Sequence:** Water suppression using excitation sculpting.
*   **Observation:** The dispersion of the amide proton signals (6.0 – 9.5 ppm) and the methyl signals (-0.5 – 1.5 ppm) are compared between batches.

**B. Statistical Analysis (PCA)**
Principal Component Analysis (PCA) is performed on the NMR spectra of batches GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-010. All commercial batches fall within the 95% confidence interval (Hotelling's T² ellipse) established by the reference standard, indicating no significant structural drift.

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.6 Quaternary Structure and Self-Association

Glucogen-XR is designed to form a reversible heptameric state upon subcutaneous injection to provide extended-release kinetics. The state of association in the drug substance is monitored via Analytical Ultracentrifugation (AUC) and Size-Exclusion Chromatography with Multi-Angle Light Scattering (SEC-MALS).

**A. SEC-MALS Analysis**
SEC-MALS (Wyatt DAWN HELEOS II) provides the absolute molecular weight independent of column retention time.

| Batch | Calculated MW (kDa) | Polydispersity ($M_w/M_n$) | Hydrodynamic Radius ($R_h$) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 32.4 | 1.002 | 3.1 nm |
| GLUC-2025-004 | 32.1 | 1.005 | 3.0 nm |
| **Theoretical (Monomer)** | **4.8** | **1.000** | **1.2 nm** |

*Interpretation: The data confirms that under formulation conditions (pH 7.4, high concentration), Glucogen-XR exists primarily as a hexameric/heptameric complex (Theoretical Heptamer = 33.6 kDa), which is the intended functional state.*

**B. Sedimentation Velocity Analytical Ultracentrifugation (SV-AUC)**
SV-AUC is used as the gold standard for quantifying the distribution of oligomeric states.

*   **Speed:** 45,000 RPM.
*   **Detection:** Interference and UV (280 nm).
*   **Analysis:** $c(s)$ distribution using Sedfit software.

| Species | Sedimentation Coeff ($s_{20,w}$) | Mass Fraction (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Monomer | 1.2S | 4.5% |
| Heptamer | 4.8S | 94.2% |
| Higher Aggregates | > 10S | 1.3% |

---

#### 3.2.S.3.1.2.7 Regulatory Compliance and Quality Control Reference

All HOS characterization studies were performed in accordance with:
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Characterization and Physicochemical Self-Similarity of Biosimilars (applied here for comparability of process changes).
3.  **USP <1217>:** Binding Assays (for HOS-function correlation).

**Summary of Higher-Order Structure Stability**
Comprehensive HOS analysis of Glucogen-XR batches (GLUC-2025-XXX) demonstrates a highly consistent alpha-helical architecture with a stable, reversible heptameric quaternary state. These data support the structural integrity of the drug substance and its suitability for long-term clinical use.

---

# Impurities and Degradation Products

## Process-Related Impurities

### **3.2.S.3.2 Impurities: Process-Related Impurities**

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.1 Introduction and Scope**
The characterization and control of process-related impurities for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), manufactured by Google Health Sciences (GHS), is managed in strict accordance with ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and ICH Q3A(R2) (Impurities in New Drug Substances). 

Given the nature of the Glucogen-XR production process—utilizing a proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line (a CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative) and an advanced high-throughput perfusion bioreactor system—the identification and quantification of process-related impurities are critical to ensuring product safety, immunogenicity mitigation, and clinical efficacy.

Process-related impurities are categorized into three primary sub-classes:
1.  **Cell Substrate-Derived Impurities:** Host Cell Proteins (HCP), Host Cell DNA (HCD), and endogenous retrovirus-like particles.
2.  **Cell Culture-Derived Impurities:** Antibiotics (none used in GHS process), growth factors, media constituents (e.g., Insulin, Methotrexate), and downstream process chemicals.
3.  **Downstream-Derived Impurities:** Protein A leachates, monoclonal antibody (mAb) fragments (if applicable to purification), process solvents, buffers, and column leachables.

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.2 Host Cell Proteins (HCP)**

**3.2.S.3.2.2.1 Strategy for HCP Identification and Control**
Google Health Sciences utilizes an orthogonal approach to HCP monitoring. While the primary release test employs a validated, platform-specific sandwich Enzyme-Linked Immunosorbent Assay (ELISA), GHS also performs Liquid Chromatography-Mass Spectrometry/Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) for the identification of specific "high-risk" HCPs that may co-elute with Glucogen-XR.

**3.2.S.3.2.2.2 ELISA Methodology (GHS-SOP-QC-7721)**
The HCP ELISA utilizes a polyclonal antibody population raised against a "mock" cell line (GHS-CHO-001-NULL) which contains the same genetic background as the production strain but lacks the Glucogen-XR expression vector.

*   **Sensitivity:** LOD = 0.5 ng/mg; LOQ = 1.2 ng/mg.
*   **Standard:** GHS-HCP-REF-2024 (Internal Reference Standard).

**Table 1: Cumulative HCP Clearance Data across Process Intermediates (Batch: GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-005)**

| Process Step | Sample Description | HCP Concentration (ng/mg) | Log Reduction Value (LRV) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Upstream** | Harvested Cell Culture Fluid (HCCF) | 450,000 ± 25,000 | N/A |
| **Capture** | Protein A Eluate (Neutralized) | 1,250 ± 110 | 2.55 |
| **Polishing I** | Cation Exchange (CEX) Pool | 85 ± 12 | 1.17 |
| **Polishing II** | Anion Exchange (AEX) Flow-through | < 5.0 (Below LOQ) | > 1.23 |
| **Final DS** | Ultrafiltration/Diafiltration (UF/DF) | < 1.0 (LOD) | Total Cumulative LRV: > 5.65 |

**3.2.S.3.2.2.3 LC-MS/MS Characterization of Residual HCPs**
To ensure the absence of problematic enzymes (e.g., Phospholipase B-Like 2 [PLBL2] or Cathepsin L) which could impact product stability or cause adverse reactions, GHS conducted a Deep Proteomic Profiling of the Drug Substance (DS).

*   **Instrument:** Thermo Scientific Orbitrap Exploris 480.
*   **Method:** 1D-LC with DDA (Data Dependent Acquisition).
*   **Result:** No individual HCP species was detected above the 1 ppm threshold in batches GLUC-2025-001, GLUC-2025-002, or GLUC-2025-003.

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.3 Host Cell DNA (HCD)**

**3.2.S.3.2.3.1 Quantification by qPCR (GHS-SOP-QC-8842)**
Residual HCD is quantified using a highly sensitive quantitative Polymerase Chain Reaction (qPCR) targeting a high-copy-number CHO-specific repetitive sequence (Alu-like element).

*   **Regulatory Limit:** < 100 pg DNA/dose (per FDA/WHO guidelines).
*   **GHS Target:** < 10 pg/mg of Glucogen-XR.

**Table 2: Residual HCD Analysis for Clinical Batches**

| Batch Number | Process Phase | DNA Content (pg/mg) | Recovery (%) | Spike/Recovery Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | Final Drug Substance | 1.42 | 98.5 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-002 | Final Drug Substance | 0.88 | 102.1 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-003 | Final Drug Substance | 1.15 | 95.4 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-004 | Final Drug Substance | < 0.50 (LOD) | 99.0 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-005 | Final Drug Substance | 1.02 | 100.8 | Pass |

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.4 Process-Derived Chemicals and Additives**

**3.2.S.3.2.4.1 Methotrexate (MTX)**
MTX is utilized in the GHS-CHO-001 GS-system for gene amplification. Although it is removed during downstream processing, it is monitored as a potential impurity.

*   **Detection Method:** High-Performance Liquid Chromatography (HPLC) with UV Detection at 302 nm.
*   **LOD:** 5 ppb.
*   **Results:** MTX was not detected in any DS batches (GLUC-2025-001 to GLUC-2025-010).

**3.2.S.3.2.4.2 Protein A Leachate**
During the initial capture step, the MabSelect SuRe LX resin may leach trace amounts of the Protein A ligand.

*   **Detection Method:** Commercial Protein A ELISA Kit (Repligen).
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** < 10 ppm (ng Protein A / mg Glucogen-XR).
*   **Summary Data:** 
    *   GLUC-2025-001: 2.1 ppm
    *   GLUC-2025-002: 1.8 ppm
    *   GLUC-2025-003: 2.4 ppm

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.5 Viral Impurities (Adventitious Agents)**
While viral clearance is detailed in Section 3.2.A.2, process-related viral impurities are considered here as a function of the cell substrate. The GHS-CHO-001 cell line is characterized for endogenous retrovirus-like particles (RVLPs).

**Table 3: Viral Clearance and Safety Margin Calculation**

| Virus Type | Model Virus | Step | Log Reduction Value (LRV) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Enveloped | XMuLV | Low pH Inactivation | > 4.8 |
| Enveloped | XMuLV | Protein A Chromatography | 3.2 |
| Non-Enveloped | MMV | Viral Filtration (Planova 20N) | > 5.5 |
| **Total LRV** | | | **> 13.5 (Enveloped)** |

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.6 Step-by-Step Analytical Protocol: Determination of Residual Benzonase**
Benzonase is used during the harvest (Step 2) to reduce viscosity by digesting nucleic acids. Residual Benzonase must be cleared to undetectable levels.

**Protocol GHS-ANA-331-B:**
1.  **Preparation:** Dilute Drug Substance sample to 10 mg/mL in PBS (pH 7.4).
2.  **Standards:** Prepare Benzonase reference standards from 0.1 ng/mL to 10 ng/mL.
3.  **Coating:** Coat 96-well microtiter plates with anti-Benzonase capture antibody (1:2000 dilution) for 12 hours at 4°C.
4.  **Blocking:** Block with 3% BSA in PBST for 2 hours.
5.  **Incubation:** Add samples and standards in triplicate; incubate for 90 minutes at Room Temperature (RT).
6.  **Detection:** Add HRP-conjugated secondary antibody; incubate for 60 minutes at RT.
7.  **Substrate:** Add TMB substrate; stop reaction with 2M H2SO4 after 15 minutes.
8.  **Analysis:** Measure absorbance at 450 nm. Calculate concentration via 4-parameter logistic (4PL) regression.

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.7 Leachables and Extractables (L&E)**
As Glucogen-XR is an extended-release peptide, its interaction with the Single-Use Technology (SUT) components in the manufacturing train is scrutinized.

*   **Component:** Bioprocess Bags (GHS-SUT-99).
*   **Method:** Solvent extraction followed by GC-MS and LC-MS.
*   **Key Impurity Monitored:** Bis(2-ethylhexyl) phthalate (DEHP).
*   **Limit:** < 0.1% w/w.
*   **Observation:** All DS batches showed DEHP levels below the limit of quantitation (50 ng/mL).

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.8 Statistical Analysis of Impurity Consistency**
A Process Capability Index (Cpk) was calculated for HCP clearance across 10 consecutive batches (GLUC-2025-001 to GLUC-2025-010).

$$Cpk = \min\left( \frac{USL - \mu}{3\sigma}, \frac{\mu - LSL}{3\sigma} \right)$$

*   **USL (Upper Specification Limit):** 20 ng/mg
*   **Mean ($\mu$):** 4.2 ng/mg
*   **Std Dev ($\sigma$):** 0.85 ng/mg
*   **Calculated Cpk:** 6.19

The Cpk of 6.19 indicates an extremely robust process with a very low probability of producing DS exceeding the HCP specification.

---

#### **3.2.S.3.2.9 References**
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **USP <1132>:** Residual Host Cell Protein Measurement in Biopharmaceuticals.
3.  **USP <1130>:** Nucleic Acid-Based Techniques—Approaches for Real-Time PCR.
4.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Characterization and Qualification of Cell Substrates.

---
**End of Subsection 3.2.S.3.2**

## Product-Related Substances

# SECTION 3.2.S.3.2: IMPURITIES – PRODUCT-RELATED SUBSTANCES
## DRUG SUBSTANCE: GLUCOGEN-XR (GLUCAPEPTIDE EXTENDED-RELEASE)

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This section provides a comprehensive characterization and quantification of product-related substances for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist produced by Google Health Sciences (GHS). In accordance with **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **ICH Q3A(R2) (Impurities in New Drug Substances)**, product-related substances are defined as molecular variants of the desired product formed during manufacture and/or storage, which are active and possess properties comparable to those of the desired product to ensure safety and efficacy.

For Glucogen-XR, these substances primarily include post-translational modifications (PTMs), truncated forms, and alternative folding isomers that maintain receptor binding affinity within a defined specification range.

### 2.0 REGULATORY FRAMEWORK AND ANALYTICAL STRATEGY

The identification and control of product-related substances for Glucogen-XR follow a risk-based approach as outlined in the Google Health Sciences Quality by Design (QbD) framework.

#### 2.1 Regulatory References
The following guidelines govern the data presented herein:
*   **ICH Q5E**: Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products Subject to Changes in their Manufacturing Process.
*   **ICH Q11**: Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances.
*   **USP <129>**: Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Monoclonal Antibodies (adapted for Peptide-Fc fusions).
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry**: Quality Considerations in Demonstrating Biosimilarity of a Therapeutic Protein Product to a Reference Product (2015).

#### 2.2 Analytical Hierarchy
The characterization of product-related substances utilizes a multi-tiered orthogonal approach:
1.  **Primary Structure Assessment**: RP-HPLC-MS/MS (Reduced/Non-reduced).
2.  **Charge Heterogeneity**: cIEF (Capillary Isoelectric Focusing) and CEX-HPLC.
3.  **Size Heterogeneity**: SE-HPLC and SDS-PAGE (CGE).
4.  **Biological Potency**: Cell-based GLP-1 receptor activation assay (cAMP induction).

---

### 3.0 IDENTIFICATION OF PRODUCT-RELATED SUBSTANCES

The manufacturing process for Glucogen-XR, utilizing the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line, results in a profile of molecular variants. These are classified into three primary categories:

#### 3.1 C-Terminal Lysine Variants
Glucogen-XR is expressed as a fusion protein. Incomplete processing of the C-terminal lysine residues by endogenous carboxypeptidases results in a distribution of species (K0, K1, and K2).

#### 3.2 Deamidated Variants
Deamidation of asparagine (Asn) residues, particularly at position Asn-28 of the glucapeptide domain, results in the formation of aspartate (Asp) and iso-aspartate (iso-Asp) isoforms.

#### 3.3 Oxidized Variants
Oxidation of methionine (Met) residues (specifically Met-14) to methionine sulfoxide represents a major degradation pathway and product-related substance.

---

### 4.0 ANALYTICAL METHODOLOGY AND QUANTIFICATION

#### 4.1 Reversed-Phase High-Performance Liquid Chromatography (RP-HPLC)
**Method ID: GHS-ANA-METH-042**

**Purpose:** Identification of oxidized and deamidated species.

**Apparatus and Conditions:**
*   **System:** Waters Acquity UPLC H-Class or equivalent.
*   **Column:** Waters CSH C18, 1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm.
*   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% TFA in H2O.
*   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.08% TFA in Acetonitrile.
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.3 mL/min.
*   **Gradient:** 25% B to 45% B over 60 minutes.
*   **Detection:** UV at 214 nm and 280 nm.

**Calculation Formula for Relative Percentage:**
$$ \% \text{Area} = \left( \frac{\text{Area of Impurity Peak}}{\sum \text{Total Area}} \right) \times 100 $$

#### 4.2 Capillary Isoelectric Focusing (cIEF)
**Method ID: GHS-ANA-METH-089**

**Purpose:** Resolution of charge variants (Acidic, Main, and Basic isoforms).

**Procedure Summary:**
1.  Sample is diluted to 1.0 mg/mL in 8M Urea.
2.  Ampholytes (pH 3–10) are added to create a linear gradient.
3.  Internal pI markers (4.1, 7.0, 9.5) are included for calibration.
4.  Focusing is performed at 1500V for 1 minute followed by 3000V for 10 minutes.

---

### 5.0 BATCH ANALYSIS DATA (PRODUCT-RELATED SUBSTANCES)

The following table summarizes the product-related substance profiles for three (3) representative GMP batches of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance manufactured at the South San Francisco facility.

**Table 1: Quantitative Profile of Product-Related Substances in Glucogen-XR Batches**

| Batch Number | Manufacture Date | C-Terminal K0 (%) | Deamidated (%) | Oxidized (Met14) (%) | High Mol. Wt. (HMW) (%) | Total Product Related (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 12-JAN-2025 | 98.4 | 0.8 | 0.4 | 0.2 | 1.4 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 04-FEB-2025 | 98.1 | 1.1 | 0.5 | 0.1 | 1.7 |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 28-FEB-2025 | 98.6 | 0.7 | 0.4 | 0.3 | 1.4 |
| **Specification** | **N/A** | **≥ 95.0** | **≤ 2.0** | **≤ 1.5** | **≤ 1.0** | **≤ 5.0** |

---

### 6.0 DETAILED CHARACTERIZATION OF VARIANTS

#### 6.1 Deamidation (Asn-28)
Deamidation at the Asn-28 site within the glucapeptide sequence is the primary chemical modification observed. Studies using forced degradation (pH 9.0, 40°C for 7 days) identified that the deamidated variant maintains 88% (± 5%) of the native biological activity.

**Table 2: Comparison of Main Peak vs. Deamidated Peak Potency**

| Attribute | Main Peak (Native) | Deamidated Variant (Asp-28) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Binding Affinity ($K_d$) | 1.2 nM | 1.4 nM |
| $EC_{50}$ (cAMP) | 0.85 nM | 0.98 nM |
| Relative Potency (%) | 100.0% (Control) | 86.7% |

#### 6.2 Oxidation (Met-14)
Oxidation of Met-14 to Methionine Sulfoxide results in a slight increase in hydrophilicity, allowing for resolution via RP-HPLC.

**Met-14 Oxidation Protocol (Experimental Verification):**
1.  **Standard Preparation:** Dilute Glucogen-XR to 2 mg/mL in PBS.
2.  **Oxidant Addition:** Add 0.1% $H_2O_2$.
3.  **Incubation:** 37°C for 4 hours.
4.  **Quenching:** Add L-methionine in 100-fold molar excess.
5.  **Analysis:** Inject into RP-HPLC system (GHS-ANA-METH-042).

**Calculation of Oxidation Rate Constant ($k$):**
$$ \ln\left(\frac{[Native]}{[Native]_0}\right) = -kt $$
Where $t$ is time in hours. For Glucogen-XR, $k = 0.012 \text{ hr}^{-1}$ under stress conditions.

---

### 7.0 PROCESS CONTROL STRATEGY

To ensure the levels of product-related substances remain within the established clinical limits, Google Health Sciences employs the following Critical Process Parameters (CPPs):

1.  **Bioreactor Temperature ($36.5^\circ\text{C} \pm 0.5^\circ\text{C}$):** Higher temperatures increase deamidation rates.
2.  **Harvest pH ($7.0 \pm 0.1$):** Controlled to prevent base-catalyzed succinimide formation.
3.  **Hold Time (Post-Protein A):** Limited to < 24 hours at $2\text{--}8^\circ\text{C}$ to prevent truncation.

#### 7.1 Action Limits for In-Process Controls (IPC)
| Process Step | IPC Parameter | Method | Action Limit |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Post-Clarification | Aggregate Level | SEC | < 5% |
| Final UF/DF | Concentration | A280 | $50 \pm 5 \text{ mg/mL}$ |
| Final Bulk | Purity | RP-HPLC | > 97% |

---

### 8.0 IMPACT ON SAFETY AND EFFICACY

The product-related substances identified in Glucogen-XR have been evaluated through the **GHS-2024-TOX-09** study.

*   **Immunogenicity:** No increased binding to anti-drug antibodies (ADA) was observed for the deamidated or oxidized forms compared to the main peak.
*   **Pharmacokinetics (PK):** In cynomolgus monkey models, the K1 and K2 C-terminal variants exhibited identical half-life ($t_{1/2}$) profiles to the K0 form.
*   **Conclusion:** Based on the similarity in biological activity and safety profiles, these variants are classified as product-related substances rather than product-related impurities.

---

### 9.0 STABILITY OF PRODUCT-RELATED SUBSTANCES

Long-term stability data (24 months at $5^\circ\text{C} \pm 3^\circ\text{C}$) indicates a slow, linear increase in deamidation.

**Linear Regression Analysis of Deamidation Rate:**
$$ Y = 0.042x + 0.78 $$
*   Where $Y = \text{Percent Deamidation}$
*   Where $x = \text{Time in months}$
*   $R^2 = 0.992$

At this rate, the specification limit of 2.0% deamidation will not be reached until Month 29, justifying the current 24-month shelf life.

---

### 10.0 REFERENCES

1.  **FDA (2021).** *Guidance for Industry: Statistical Approaches to Evaluating Analytical Similarity.*
2.  **USP <121>**. *Insulin Assays - Adaptation for GLP-1 Analogues.*
3.  **Google Health Sciences Internal Report GHS-RD-2023-455.** *Structural Characterization of Glucogen-XR Variants by Orbitrap Mass Spectrometry.*
4.  **ICH Q3A(R2).** *Impurities in New Drug Substances.*

## Degradation Product Characterization

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.3.2: IMPURITIES AND DEGRADATION PRODUCTS
### SUBSECTION: DEGRADATION PRODUCT CHARACTERIZATION

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.1 Executive Summary of Degradation Profile
In accordance with ICH Q6B (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*) and ICH Q3A(R2) (*Impurities in New Drug Substances*), Google Health Sciences (GHS) has conducted an exhaustive characterization of the degradation landscape for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). 

Glucogen-XR is a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line. Due to the inherent complexity of the peptide primary sequence and the C-terminal extension designed for extended release, the molecule is susceptible to specific chemical and physical degradation pathways. This section details the identification, structural elucidation, and quantification of these degradation products, categorized by their formation mechanism (e.g., deamidation, oxidation, isomerization, and proteolytic cleavage).

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.2 Force Degradation Studies (Stress Testing)
To define the degradation pathways and establish the stability-indicating nature of the analytical methods, stress studies were performed on Drug Substance (DS) Batch GLUC-2025-001 and GLUC-2025-002.

##### 3.2.S.3.2.2.1 Study Design and Conditions
The stress testing matrix followed the principles outlined in ICH Q1A(R2). Samples were exposed to environmental stressors exceeding standard ICH long-term and accelerated storage conditions.

**Table 3.2.S.3.2-1: Stress Testing Matrix for Glucogen-XR DS**

| Stress Condition | Parameters | Duration | Objective |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Thermal (Solid)** | 60°C ± 2°C | 14 Days | Determine solid-state thermal stability |
| **Thermal (Liquid)** | 40°C ± 2°C | 21 Days | Identify secondary structure unfolding / aggregation |
| **Photostability** | ICH Option 2 (>1.2M lux-hr, >200 W-hr/m²) | 7 Days | Evaluate UV/Visible light sensitivity |
| **Acid Hydrolysis** | 0.1 N HCl, pH 1.5 | 24 Hours | Identify Asp-Pro cleavage and deamidation |
| **Base Hydrolysis** | 0.1 N NaOH, pH 11.0 | 6 Hours | Evaluate deamidation and racemization |
| **Oxidation** | 0.3% H₂O₂ | 4 Hours | Characterize Met and Trp oxidation |
| **Freeze/Thaw** | -80°C to 25°C | 5 Cycles | Assess physical stability/aggregation |
| **Mechanical Stress** | 300 RPM Agitation | 48 Hours | Evaluate surface-induced denaturation |

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.3 Identification of Major Degradation Products (DP)
Through Liquid Chromatography-Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) and Peptide Mapping (N-terminal and C-terminal), four primary degradation species have been identified and assigned "DP" codes for regulatory tracking.

##### 3.2.S.3.2.3.1 DP-01: Asparagine Deamidation (Asn²⁸ to Asp²⁸/Iso-Asp²⁸)
Deamidation of the asparagine residue at position 28 (Asn²⁸) is the most prevalent chemical degradation pathway. This results in a mass increase of +0.984 Da.

*   **Mechanism:** Formation of a succinimide intermediate (cyclic imide) followed by hydrolysis into L-aspartyl and L-isoaspartyl forms.
*   **Analytical Method:** Ion-Exchange Chromatography (IEX-HPLC) and Reversed-Phase UPLC (RP-UPLC).
*   **Impact:** Minor reduction in GLP-1 receptor binding affinity (~12% decrease in EC₅₀).

##### 3.2.S.3.2.3.2 DP-02: Methionine Oxidation (Met⁸)
The methionine residue at position 8 (Met⁸) is susceptible to oxidation, forming Methionine Sulfoxide.

*   **Mechanism:** Introduction of oxygen via reactive oxygen species (ROS) or peroxide exposure, resulting in a +15.99 Da mass shift.
*   **Analytical Method:** RP-UPLC with UV detection (214 nm) and ESI-TOF Mass Spectrometry.
*   **Impact:** Significant impact on potency if oxidation exceeds 5% (Met⁸ is critical for hydrophobic pocket binding).

##### 3.2.S.3.2.3.3 DP-03: C-Terminal Truncation (Des-Gly³⁶)
Proteolytic cleavage of the C-terminal glycine residue.

*   **Mechanism:** Carboxypeptidase-like activity or hydrolytic cleavage at the proline-glycine junction.
*   **Analytical Method:** High-Resolution Mass Spectrometry (HRMS).
*   **Impact:** Negligible impact on PK/PD but monitored as a process-related/degradation marker.

##### 3.2.S.3.2.3.4 DP-04: High Molecular Weight Species (HMWS)
Covalent and non-covalent aggregation.

*   **Mechanism:** Dimerization via intermolecular disulfide shuffling or hydrophobic interaction-driven non-covalent association.
*   **Analytical Method:** Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC-HPLC) and Multi-Angle Light Scattering (MALS).

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.4 Quantitative Analysis of Degradation Batches
The following data represents the characterization of three pivotal batches under accelerated conditions (25°C / 60% RH).

**Table 3.2.S.3.2-2: Degradation Product Quantitative Summary (T=6 Months)**

| Batch Number | Storage | Main Peak (%) | Total Deamidation (%) | Total Oxidation (%) | HMWS (%) | Other (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 5°C | 99.2 | 0.3 | 0.1 | 0.2 | 0.2 |
| | 25°C | 96.5 | 1.8 | 0.4 | 0.8 | 0.5 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 5°C | 99.4 | 0.2 | 0.1 | 0.1 | 0.2 |
| | 25°C | 96.1 | 2.1 | 0.5 | 0.9 | 0.4 |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 5°C | 99.1 | 0.4 | 0.2 | 0.2 | 0.1 |
| | 25°C | 95.8 | 2.3 | 0.6 | 1.1 | 0.2 |

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.5 Analytical Protocols for Characterization

##### 3.2.S.3.2.5.1 Protocol GHS-ANA-088: Peptide Mapping by LC-MS/MS
This protocol is utilized for the site-specific identification of deamidation and oxidation.

1.  **Enzymatic Digestion:**
    *   Reconstitute 1 mg of Glucogen-XR DS in 6M Guanidine-HCl, 50 mM Tris-HCl (pH 7.8).
    *   Reduce with 10 mM DTT at 37°C for 45 minutes.
    *   Alkylate with 20 mM Iodoacetamide (IAM) in the dark for 30 minutes.
    *   Quench with excess DTT.
    *   Digest with Trypsin (TPCK-treated) at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio for 16 hours at 37°C.
2.  **Chromatographic Conditions:**
    *   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC BEH C18 (1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm).
    *   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% Formic Acid in Water.
    *   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.1% Formic Acid in Acetonitrile.
    *   **Gradient:** 2% B to 45% B over 60 minutes.
    *   **Flow Rate:** 0.2 mL/min.
3.  **Mass Spectrometry:**
    *   **Instrument:** Thermo Fisher Orbitrap Exploris 480.
    *   **Scan Range:** 300–2000 m/z.
    *   **Resolution:** 60,000 (MS1), 15,000 (MS2).
    *   **Analysis:** Comparison of observed fragment ions against the theoretical sequence using BioPharma Finder™ software.

##### 3.2.S.3.2.5.2 Protocol GHS-ANA-092: SEC-MALS for Aggregate Characterization
This protocol differentiates between reversible and irreversible (covalent) aggregates.

1.  **Mobile Phase:** 50 mM Sodium Phosphate, 200 mM Arginine-HCl, pH 6.5. (Arginine is included to suppress non-specific column interactions).
2.  **Column:** TSKgel G3000SWxl (7.8 mm ID x 30 cm).
3.  **Detection:** UV at 280 nm, Refractive Index (RI), and 18-angle Light Scattering.
4.  **Calculations:**
    *   The weight-average molecular weight ($M_w$) is calculated using the Zimm equation:
        $$\frac{Kc}{R(\theta, c)} = \frac{1}{M_w P(\theta)} + 2A_2 c$$
    *   Where $K$ is the optical constant, $R$ is the Rayleigh ratio, and $P(\theta)$ is the form factor.

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.6 Structural Elucidation of Unknown Impurities
During the stability study of Batch GLUC-2025-001 (T=12 months at 25°C), an unknown peak (RRT 1.14) was observed at 0.12%.

**Step-by-Step Elucidation:**
1.  **Isolation:** Semi-preparative RP-HPLC was used to isolate 50 µg of the impurity.
2.  **Mass Determination:** ESI-MS revealed a mass of 4,128.5 Da, exactly +18 Da higher than the native Glucogen-XR (4,110.5 Da).
3.  **Hypothesis:** Succinimide ring-opening via water addition or peptide bond hydrolysis.
4.  **MS/MS Sequencing:** Fragmentation of the $y$-ion series confirmed the modification at Asp²⁸.
5.  **Conclusion:** The impurity was identified as the hydrolysis product of the cyclic imide intermediate, specifically the β-aspartyl isoform (Iso-Asp²⁸).

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.7 Statistical Analysis of Degradation Rates
The degradation rate for total impurities ($k$) was calculated using first-order kinetics for the 25°C stability data:
$$\ln[C] = \ln[C_0] - kt$$
For Batch GLUC-2025-001:
*   $C_0$ (Purity at T0): 99.2%
*   $C$ (Purity at 6 Months): 96.5%
*   Calculated $k$: $0.0046 \text{ month}^{-1}$
*   Predicted Shelf Life ($t_{90}$): ~22.8 months at 25°C.

---

#### 3.2.S.3.2.8 Regulatory Compliance Statement
All characterization studies for Glucogen-XR degradation products were performed in compliance with:
1.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Q3A Impurities in New Drug Substances* (Revision 2).
2.  **USP <1049>:** *Content Release and Shelf Life of Biotechnology Products*.
3.  **ICH Q6B:** *Specifications for Biotechnological/Biological Products*.

Google Health Sciences confirms that all degradation products exceeding the identification threshold (0.10%) have been structurally characterized, and those exceeding the qualification threshold (0.15%) have been evaluated in non-clinical safety studies (See Module 4).

# Specifications Justification

## Critical Quality Attributes Definition

### 3.2.S.4.1.3 CRITICAL QUALITY ATTRIBUTES (CQA) DEFINITION AND RATIONALE

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.1 Introduction and Risk-Based Framework
The definition of Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), manufactured by Google Health Sciences (GHS), follows a structured, science-based approach consistent with **ICH Q8(R2) Pharmaceutical Development**, **ICH Q9 Quality Risk Management**, and **ICH Q11 Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances**. 

A CQA is defined as a physical, chemical, biological, or microbiological property or characteristic that should be within an appropriate limit, range, or distribution to ensure the desired product quality. For Glucogen-XR, a GLP-1 receptor agonist produced in the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line, the identification of CQAs is inextricably linked to the molecule’s primary mechanism of action (insulinotropic stimulation) and its extended-release pharmacokinetic profile achieved through site-specific PEGylation and peptide backbone optimization.

The following sections detail the methodology for CQA identification, the scoring matrix utilized for risk assessment, and the specific technical justifications for each attribute.

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.2 CQA Identification Methodology: The GHS-QRM Protocol
Google Health Sciences employs the **GHS-QRM-0047-V5** protocol for determining criticality. This protocol utilizes a Failure Mode and Effects Analysis (FMEA) modified for biotechnological drug substances.

**Step 1: Impact Assessment (Severity)**
The potential impact of each attribute on clinical safety and efficacy is ranked on a scale of 1 to 10.
*   **1–2 (Negligible):** No impact on bioactivity; no safety concern.
*   **3–5 (Minor):** Slight impact on PK/PD; manageable safety profile.
*   **6–8 (Moderate):** Significant change in half-life or potency; potential for immunogenicity.
*   **9–10 (Critical):** Loss of activity; severe adverse events; life-threatening immunogenicity.

**Step 2: Uncertainty Factor**
Given the novel nature of the glucapeptide sequence, an uncertainty factor (U) is applied based on the available literature and Phase I/II clinical data.
*   **U=1:** Well-characterized (e.g., pH, appearance).
*   **U=2:** Emerging data (e.g., specific O-glycosylation sites).

**Step 3: Criticality Score (CS)**
$CS = Impact \times Uncertainty$
*   **CS ≥ 7:** Classified as a CQA.
*   **CS < 7:** Classified as a Non-CQA (monitored via In-Process Controls).

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.3 Detailed Table of Quality Attribute Assessment
The following table summarizes the assessment for Glucogen-XR Drug Substance.

**Table 3.2.S.4.1.3-1: Comprehensive CQA Identification Matrix**

| Attribute ID | Quality Attribute | Category | Impact Score (1-10) | Uncertainty (1-2) | CS | Classification | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :---: | :---: | :---: | :--- | :--- |
| **CQA-01** | **Potency (In Vitro)** | Biological | 10 | 1.0 | 10 | **CQA** | Direct correlate to clinical efficacy in T2DM. |
| **CQA-02** | **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | Chemical | 8 | 1.2 | 9.6 | **CQA** | Related substances may impact PK/PD. |
| **CQA-03** | **PEGylation Site Occupancy** | Structural | 9 | 1.5 | 13.5 | **CQA** | Critical for "XR" (Extended Release) claims. |
| **CQA-04** | **Host Cell Protein (HCP)** | Process | 8 | 1.1 | 8.8 | **CQA** | Immunogenicity risk; GHS-CHO-001 specific. |
| **CQA-05** | **Aggregation (SEC)** | Physical | 9 | 1.1 | 9.9 | **CQA** | High risk for immunogenicity/infusion reaction. |
| **CQA-06** | **N-Terminal Truncation** | Chemical | 7 | 1.3 | 9.1 | **CQA** | Impact on DPP-IV resistance. |
| **CQA-07** | **Endotoxin** | Safety | 10 | 1.0 | 10 | **CQA** | Regulatory requirement (USP <85>). |
| **CQA-08** | **C-Terminal Amidation** | Structural | 4 | 1.2 | 4.8 | Non-CQA | Minor impact on stability; monitored by IPC. |
| **CQA-09** | **Residual Protein A** | Process | 3 | 1.0 | 3.0 | Non-CQA | Consistently cleared below LOD. |
| **CQA-10** | **Glycan Profile** | Structural | 5 | 1.4 | 7.0 | **CQA** | Threshold met; impact on clearance rates. |

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.4 Technical Justification for Biological CQAs

##### 3.2.S.4.1.3.4.1 Potency (In Vitro Bioassay)
**Description:** The potency of Glucogen-XR is determined by its ability to activate the Human GLP-1 Receptor (GLP-1R) in a cell-based luciferase reporter assay (Method MET-BIOPOT-001).

**Justification:**
The primary mechanism of action for Glucogen-XR is the potentiation of glucose-dependent insulin secretion. Any significant deviation in potency directly affects the Glycated Hemoglobin (HbA1c) reduction in patients. The potency is calculated relative to the GHS Internal Standard (Batch GLUC-2023-REF).

*   **Statistical Analysis:** A 4-parameter logistic (4-PL) model is used to compare the dose-response curves of the sample vs. standard.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** 80% to 125% of Reference Standard.
*   **Historical Data:**
    *   Batch GLUC-2025-001: 102%
    *   Batch GLUC-2025-002: 98%
    *   Batch GLUC-2025-003: 105%

##### 3.2.S.4.1.3.4.2 PEGylation Site Occupancy and Monodispersity
**Description:** Glucogen-XR utilizes a 40kDa branched PEG (Polyethylene Glycol) chain attached to Lysine-26.

**Justification:**
The "XR" (Extended Release) functionality is dependent on the hydrodynamic radius imparted by the PEG moiety. Under-PEGylated species (Mono-PEG at unintended sites or Non-PEGylated peptide) lead to rapid renal clearance and "dose-dumping" effects. Over-PEGylated species may sterically hinder the GLP-1R binding site, reducing efficacy.

*   **Analytical Control:** CE-SDS (Capillary Electrophoresis-Sodium Dodecyl Sulfate) under non-reducing conditions.
*   **Requirement:** ≥ 98.0% Main PEGylated Peak.

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.5 Technical Justification for Purity and Impurities

##### 3.2.S.4.1.3.5.1 High Molecular Weight Species (HMWS/Aggregates)
**Description:** Formation of dimers, trimers, and higher-order multimeric structures.

**Justification:**
Aggregates in peptide therapeutics are known to act as potent immunogens by cross-linking B-cell receptors. Given the long-term chronic administration of Glucogen-XR, HMWS must be strictly controlled to prevent the development of Anti-Drug Antibodies (ADAs).

*   **Methodology:** Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC-HPLC) using a TSKgel G3000SWxl column.
*   **Specifications:**
    *   Monomer: ≥ 99.0%
    *   HMWS: ≤ 0.5%
    *   LMWS: ≤ 0.5%

##### 3.2.S.4.1.3.5.2 Host Cell Proteins (HCP)
**Description:** Residual proteins from the GHS-CHO-001 host cell line.

**Justification:**
Residual HCPs can cause allergic reactions or act as adjuvants. GHS utilizes a third-generation, highly sensitive ELISA specific to the GHS-CHO-001 strain (Method MET-HCP-CHO-GHS).

**Table 3.2.S.4.1.3-2: HCP Clearance Data (Batch GLUC-2025-005)**
| Process Step | HCP Level (ppm) | Log Reduction Value (LRV) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Harvest | 450,000 | N/A |
| Protein A Eluate | 2,500 | 2.25 |
| Cation Exchange | 120 | 1.32 |
| Nanofiltration | 15 | 0.90 |
| **Final Drug Substance** | **< 5 (LOD)** | **Total LRV: 4.95** |

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.6 Technical Justification for Safety CQAs

##### 3.2.S.4.1.3.6.1 Bacterial Endotoxins
**Description:** Lipopolysaccharides from Gram-negative bacteria.

**Justification:**
Per **USP <85>**, endotoxin levels must be controlled for all parenteral products. For Glucogen-XR, the limit is set significantly tighter than the standard 5.0 EU/kg/hr to account for the large volume administered in the extended-release formulation.

*   **Calculation of Endotoxin Limit (L):**
    $L = K / M$
    Where $K = 5$ EU/kg (threshold) and $M = 0.5$ mg/kg (max clinical dose).
    $L = 10$ EU/mg.
    **GHS Internal Specification:** ≤ 0.5 EU/mg (20x safety factor).

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.7 Protocol for CQA Re-evaluation (Post-Approval Change Management)
Google Health Sciences maintains a living CQA register. Any change in the manufacturing process (e.g., scale-up from 2,000L to 10,000L in the South San Francisco facility) triggers a re-evaluation of the CQA matrix.

**Step-by-Step Procedure for CQA Update:**
1.  **Data Collection:** Compile analytical data from 3 consecutive validation batches (e.g., GLUC-2025-VAL-01, -02, -03).
2.  **Statistical Comparability:** Perform Equivalence Testing (Two One-Sided Tests, TOST) with a margin of 1.5 standard deviations of the clinical batches.
3.  **Risk Assessment Update:** Re-run the FMEA matrix using the GHS-QRM-0047-V5 protocol.
4.  **Regulatory Notification:** If a new CQA is identified or a range is widened, submit a Prior Approval Supplement (PAS) to the FDA.

---

#### 3.2.S.4.1.3.8 References
1.  **ICH Q8(R2):** Pharmaceutical Development (August 2009).
2.  **ICH Q11:** Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances (May 2012).
3.  **USP <121.1>:** Physico-chemical Analytical Procedures for Peptides.
4.  **Google Health Sciences Internal Standard Operating Procedure:** SOP-REG-0012: *Definition of Critical Quality Attributes for Biologics.*

**End of Subsection**
