## Acceptance Criteria Rationale

### **3.2.S.4.5 JUSTIFICATION OF SPECIFICATION (ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA RATIONALE)**

**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-XR-M3DS-0045  
**Product:** Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)  
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences  
**Date of Submission:** October 14, 2025  
**Subject:** Rationale for Selection of Acceptance Criteria for Drug Substance (DS)  

---

#### **1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE**

The establishment of acceptance criteria for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Drug Substance is based on a multifaceted approach integrating historical batch data, clinical trial experience, process capability assessments (Cp/Cpk), and rigorous characterization of the molecule’s critical quality attributes (CQAs). This rationale follows the guidelines set forth in **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q11** (Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances).

The acceptance criteria are designed to ensure that every lot of Glucogen-XR manufactured by Google Health Sciences (GHS) at the South San Francisco facility (3000 Innovation Drive) consistently meets defined standards for identity, purity, potency, and safety, thereby guaranteeing the clinical performance observed during Phase II/III trials.

---

#### **2.0 STATISTICAL METHODOLOGY FOR LIMIT SETTING**

Acceptance criteria were derived using a combination of "Clinical Trial Range" (CTR) and "Statistical Tolerance Intervals" (STI). For quantitative attributes, Google Health Sciences employed the following formulaic approach:

$$Limit = \mu \pm (k \cdot \sigma)$$

Where:
*   $\mu$ = Process Mean from Phase III Registration Batches.
*   $\sigma$ = Standard Deviation of the process.
*   $k$ = Coverage factor calculated for a 95% confidence level to include 99% of the population (k ≈ 3.4–4.2 depending on N).

##### **Table 2.1: Reference Batches for Specification Setting (Phase III/PPQ)**

| Batch Number | Scale | Purpose | Manufacturing Date | Site |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 2,000L | PPQ / Clinical | 12-Jan-2025 | SSF Site 1 |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 2,000L | PPQ / Clinical | 02-Feb-2025 | SSF Site 1 |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | 2,000L | PPQ / Stability | 22-Feb-2025 | SSF Site 1 |
| **GLUC-2025-004** | 2,000L | Validation | 15-Mar-2025 | SSF Site 1 |
| **GLUC-2025-005** | 2,000L | Validation | 05-Apr-2025 | SSF Site 1 |

---

#### **3.0 DETAILED RATIONALE BY ATTRIBUTE**

##### **3.1 Identity (ID)**
**Criterion:** Must match Reference Standard (GHS-STD-GLUC-01).

*   **Rationale:** Per ICH Q6B, identity tests must be highly specific. Glucogen-XR uses a dual-orthogonal approach:
    1.  **RP-HPLC Retention Time:** Comparison against the current Reference Standard. The window of $\pm 2.0\%$ is established to account for minor instrument-to-instrument variability (Agilent 1290 Infinity II vs. Waters ACQUITY UPLC).
    2.  **Peptide Mapping (LC-MS/MS):** Confirmation of the primary amino acid sequence including the extended-release linker attachment at Lys-26. This confirms the specific identity of the GHS-CHO-001 expression product.

##### **3.2 Purity and Impurities (Product-Related)**

###### **3.2.1 Monomer Content by SEC-HPLC**
**Criterion:** $\ge 98.0\%$

*   **Rationale:** Aggregation is a known risk for GLP-1 analogues, potentially impacting immunogenicity. Data from batches GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-005 consistently showed monomer levels $>99.2\%$. The limit of $\ge 98.0\%$ is set to provide a safety margin while ensuring that any trend toward dimer or high-molecular-weight species (HMWS) is flagged.
*   **Historical Data Summary:**
    *   Mean: 99.42%
    *   SD: 0.08%
    *   3-Sigma Lower Limit: 99.18%
    *   *Proposed Regulatory Limit:* $\ge 98.0\%$ (conservative for shelf-life stability).

###### **3.2.2 Purity by RP-UPLC (C18)**
**Criterion:** Total Purity $\ge 95.0\%$; Single Largest Impurity $\le 1.0\%$.

*   **Rationale:** This method detects deamidation (Asp-9) and oxidation (Met-14) variants. Clinical batches used in Study GHS-T2D-003 demonstrated total purity between 96.2% and 97.8%. The $95.0\%$ threshold is linked to the lowest purity batch used in Phase III clinical trials which showed no adverse safety signals.

##### **3.3 Process-Related Impurities**

###### **3.3.1 Host Cell Protein (HCP)**
**Criterion:** $\le 100$ ppm (ng/mg).

*   **Rationale:** Google Health Sciences utilizes a proprietary 3rd generation ELISA kit specific to the GHS-CHO-001 cell line.
*   **Data Analysis:**
    *   GLUC-2025-001: 12 ppm
    *   GLUC-2025-002: 9 ppm
    *   GLUC-2025-003: 15 ppm
*   While process capability supports a lower limit (e.g., 50 ppm), the 100 ppm limit is established per industry standard and USP <1132> to account for assay variability and potential minor shifts during scale-up to 10,000L commercial bioreactors.

###### **3.3.2 Residual DNA**
**Criterion:** $\le 10$ ng/dose.

*   **Rationale:** In accordance with FDA and WHO guidelines for biologics produced in continuous cell lines. Quantitation is performed via qPCR targeting a 100bp sequence of the CHO genome. All PPQ batches were $< 1$ pg/mg, which is significantly below the regulatory threshold.

---

#### **4.0 POTENCY AND BIOLOGICAL ACTIVITY**

##### **4.1 In Vitro Cell-Based Bioassay (cAMP Induction)**
**Criterion:** 80% to 125% of Reference Standard.

*   **Protocol Overview (GHS-SOP-QC-552):**
    1.  HEK293 cells transfected with human GLP-1R are seeded at $5 \times 10^4$ cells/well.
    2.  Glucogen-XR samples and standards are diluted in a 10-point curve (0.01 nM to 100 nM).
    3.  Intracellular cAMP is measured via TR-FRET.
    4.  Data is fitted using a 4-parameter logistic (4PL) model.
*   **Rationale:** The 80-125% range is the standard pharmaceutical industry acceptance width for biological activity. This ensures that the Gly-to-Ser substitution in the peptide sequence (designed for extended-release) maintains the required agonist activity for glycemic control.

---

#### **5.0 PHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES AND SAFETY**

##### **5.1 Bacterial Endotoxins (USP <85>)**
**Criterion:** $\le 0.5$ EU/mg.

*   **Calculation:**
    *   $K = 5$ EU/kg (threshold for parenteral drugs).
    *   $M = 0.1$ mg/kg (maximum clinical dose of Glucogen-XR).
    *   $L = K/M = 50$ EU/mg.
*   **Rationale:** Although the calculated limit is 50 EU/mg, GHS has applied a more stringent internal limit of 0.5 EU/mg based on the highly controlled purification process (Protein A + Ion Exchange Chromatography) and to align with the safety profile required for chronic subcutaneous administration.

##### **5.2 Sterility and Bioburden**
**Criterion:** Bioburden $< 1$ CFU/10 mL; Endotoxin $< 0.5$ EU/mg.

*   **Rationale:** The drug substance is "low bioburden," not necessarily sterile, as it undergoes final sterile filtration during Drug Product (DP) formulation. However, strict control at the DS stage prevents the accumulation of pyrogens.

---

#### **6.0 SUMMARY TABLE OF SPECIFICATIONS AND RATIONALE**

| Test | Method | Acceptance Criteria | Rationale Summary |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (USP <790>) | Clear to slightly opalescent; Colorless | Consistent with high-concentration peptide solution. |
| **pH** | Potentiometric (USP <791>) | 6.2 $\pm$ 0.3 | Optimized for peptide stability and patient comfort. |
| **Protein Conc.** | UV/Vis (A280) | 50.0 $\pm$ 2.5 mg/mL | Based on Extinction Coefficient $\epsilon = 1.45$. |
| **Charge Isoforms** | iCE3 (cIEF) | Main Peak $\ge 65.0\%$ | Justified by Cation Exchange chromatography capability. |
| **Residual Protein A** | ELISA | $\le 5$ ppm | Mitigation of immunogenicity from Protein A leaching. |

---

#### **7.0 REFERENCES**
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications for Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **USP <121>:** Insulin Assays (Adaptation for GLP-1).
3.  **FDA Guidance (2024):** Quality Considerations for Peptide Drug Substances.
4.  **Google Health Sciences Internal Report GHS-RPT-2025-044:** Statistical Analysis of Phase III Batch Data.

---
**END OF SECTION**

---

## Linkage to Clinical Safety and Efficacy

### **3.2.S.4.5 JUSTIFICATION OF SPECIFICATION: LINKAGE TO CLINICAL SAFETY AND EFFICACY**

---

#### **1.0 Introduction and Scope**
The establishment of acceptance criteria for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** is based on a multi-factorial approach that integrates historical manufacturing data, stability trends, and—critically—the correlation between Product Quality Attributes (PQAs) and observed clinical outcomes. This section provides the detailed scientific justification for the specifications of Glucogen-XR, establishing a direct bridge between the quality profile of the Drug Substance (DS) and the safety, immunogenicity, and efficacy data derived from the Phase 1, Phase 2 (GLUC-P2-202), and Phase 3 (GLUC-P3-501/502) clinical trials.

The justification follows the principles outlined in **ICH Q6B** (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*), **ICH Q11** (*Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances*), and **ICH Q8(R2)** (*Pharmaceutical Development*).

---

#### **2.0 Clinical Trial Material (CTM) Summary and Batch Pedigree**
The clinical relevance of the specifications is anchored in the "Clinically Validated Range" (CVR). All batches used in pivotal Phase 3 trials (GLUC-P3-501 and GLUC-P3-502) met the proposed commercial specifications. The following table summarizes the key batches that establish the linkage between manufacturing consistency and clinical performance.

**Table 1: Correlation of Manufacturing Batches to Clinical Study Phases**

| Batch Number | Scale | Manufacturing Site | Clinical Study ID | Purpose/Indication | Efficacy Result (HbA1c Δ) | Safety Profile |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 500L | SSF, CA (Pilot) | GLUC-P1-101 | Phase 1 (SAD/MAD) | N/A (Safety/PK) | Well Tolerated |
| **GLUC-2025-012** | 2000L | SSF, CA (GMP) | GLUC-P2-202 | Phase 2 Dose Ranging | -1.4% (Mean) | Minor GI Upset |
| **GLUC-2025-045** | 12000L | SSF, CA (Comm) | GLUC-P3-501 | Phase 3 Pivotal | -1.8% (Primary) | Confirmed Safety |
| **GLUC-2025-089** | 12000L | SSF, CA (Comm) | GLUC-P3-502 | Phase 3 Long-term | -1.75% (Year 1) | Low Immunogenicity |
| **GLUC-2025-102** | 12000L | SSF, CA (Comm) | GLUC-P3-502 | Phase 3 Extension | -1.72% (Year 2) | No SAEs related to DS |

---

#### **3.0 Justification of Potency and Biological Activity**
The potency of Glucogen-XR is defined by its ability to activate the GLP-1 receptor (GLP-1R), leading to glucose-dependent insulin secretion. The specification for potency is set at **80% to 125%** of the Reference Standard.

##### **3.1 Mechanism of Action (MoA) and Clinical Linkage**
The clinical efficacy of Glucogen-XR (reduction in HbA1c) is a direct function of the molecule’s binding affinity ($K_d$) and subsequent cyclic AMP (cAMP) induction. 

*   **Calculation of Relative Potency (RP):**
    The RP is calculated using a 4-parameter logistic (4-PL) model:
    $$f(x) = \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B} + D$$
    Where:
    - $A$ = Minimum asymptote
    - $B$ = Hill slope (steepness)
    - $C$ = $EC_{50}$ (Effective concentration for 50% response)
    - $D$ = Maximum asymptote

**Table 2: Clinical Efficacy vs. In-Vitro Potency (Batch GLUC-2025-045)**

| Attribute | Specification | Observed (Batch -045) | Phase 3 HbA1c Reduction | Linkage Conclusion |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Cell-based Potency** | 80-125% | 104% | 1.8% Reduction | Optimal efficacy at 100% ± 20% |
| **GLP-1R Binding** | Report Value | 98.2% | Consistent with MoA | Direct correlation established |

**Statistical Justification:** Analysis of Phase 2 data showed that batches with potency < 75% resulted in a non-statistically significant reduction in postprandial glucose levels. Thus, the lower limit of 80% ensures clinical efficacy.

---

#### **4.0 Purity and Impurity Profile: Linkage to Safety**
Glucogen-XR is produced in the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line. Potential impurities include Host Cell Proteins (HCP), Host Cell DNA (hcDNA), and product-related variants (aggregates/degradants).

##### **4.1 High Molecular Weight (HMW) Species / Aggregates**
Aggregates in peptide therapeutics are known to increase the risk of immunogenicity (Anti-Drug Antibodies - ADA).
*   **Specification:** $\leq 2.0\%$ (by SE-HPLC/SEC-MALS).
*   **Clinical Justification:** In study GLUC-P3-502, Batch **GLUC-2025-089** contained 1.8% HMW. The incidence of neutralizing antibodies (NAb) was < 0.5%, which is clinically negligible. Retrospective analysis of Phase 1 (Batch -001, 2.4% HMW) showed a slight increase in injection site redness, leading to the tightening of the limit to 2.0%.

**Table 3: Impact of HMW Species on Clinical Safety**

| Batch ID | HMW (%) | ADA Incidence (%) | Injection Site Reaction | Safety Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 2.4 | 4.2% | Moderate | Acceptable (Early) |
| GLUC-2025-045 | 1.1 | 0.8% | Low | Highly Favorable |
| GLUC-2025-089 | 1.8 | 0.9% | Low | Within Margin |

##### **4.2 Host Cell Proteins (HCP)**
The HCP limit is set at **$\leq 100$ ng/mg (ppm)** using a validated Google Health proprietary ELISA.
*   **Safety Linkage:** Clinical batches had HCP levels between 12 ppm and 45 ppm. No systemic hypersensitivity reactions or anaphylaxis were reported in the 2,500 patients exposed to these levels. The limit of 100 ppm provides a 2-fold safety margin over the highest level tested in Phase 3.

---

#### **5.0 Justification of Glycosylation and Post-Translational Modifications (PTMs)**
Glucogen-XR is a glycosylated peptide. The sialic acid content and N-glycan profile are critical for the extended-release (XR) properties and half-life ($\tau_{1/2}$).

##### **5.1 Sialic Acid Content**
*   **Specification:** $\geq 5.0$ mol/mol of protein.
*   **Pharmacokinetic (PK) Linkage:** Sialic acid prevents rapid renal clearance.
    - Batches with Sialic Acid < 4.5 mol/mol (Experimental Batch GLUC-EXP-99) showed a 30% reduction in $T_{1/2}$ in cynomolgus monkeys.
    - Batch **GLUC-2025-045** (5.8 mol/mol) maintained the target human $T_{1/2}$ of 168 hours (7 days), supporting once-weekly dosing.

---

#### **6.0 Process-Related Impurities: Residual Solvents and DNA**
##### **6.1 Residual Host Cell DNA**
*   **Specification:** $\leq 10$ pg/mg (by qPCR).
*   **Justification:** Aligns with WHO and FDA requirements for biological products to minimize oncogenic risk. All clinical batches were < 2 pg/mg.

##### **6.2 Residual Protein A**
*   **Specification:** $\leq 10$ ng/mg.
*   **Safety Linkage:** Protein A is a known immunogen. Levels in GLUC-2025-XXX series were consistently below the Limit of Quantitation (LOQ = 1.5 ng/mg), ensuring no clinical risk of Protein A-induced toxicity.

---

#### **7.0 Detailed Protocol for Potency Assessment (GHS-SOP-QC-442)**
To ensure the linkage to efficacy remains robust, the following potency protocol is utilized for all commercial release:

1.  **Cell Seeding:** CHO cells transfected with human GLP-1R are seeded in 96-well plates at $2 \times 10^4$ cells/well.
2.  **Incubation:** 24 hours at $37^\circ C$, 5% $CO_2$.
3.  **Sample Preparation:** Glucogen-XR (Batch GLUC-2025-XXX) is diluted in 8-point serial dilutions (Range: 0.01 nM to 1000 nM).
4.  **Activation:** Cells are treated with DS for 30 minutes.
5.  **Detection:** cAMP levels are measured via Time-Resolved Fluorescence Resonance Energy Transfer (TR-FRET) using the Cisbio HTRF kit.
6.  **Data Analysis:** Parallelism between sample and reference standard must be confirmed (F-test p > 0.05).

---

#### **8.0 Summary of Specification Rationale**

| Quality Attribute | Acceptance Criteria | Primary Rationale | Clinical Linkage |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Clear to slightly opalescent | Product Identity | Prevents administration of particulates |
| **Purity (SEC)** | $\geq 98.0\%$ Monomer | Safety/Immunogenicity | Linked to low ADA rates in Phase 3 |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | $\geq 95.0\%$ Main Peak | Efficacy/Stability | Ensures consistent peptide delivery |
| **Bioactivity** | 80-125% | Efficacy (HbA1c) | Validated against Phase 2 dose-response |
| **Endotoxin** | $\leq 0.5$ EU/mg | Safety (Pyrogenicity) | USP <85> compliance |
| **HCP** | $\leq 100$ ppm | Safety | No hypersensitivity in 2,500 patients |

---

#### **9.0 Conclusion**
The proposed specifications for Glucogen-XR are scientifically justified through a rigorous evaluation of clinical data from the GLUC-P3 program. The limits for purity, potency, and impurities are set to ensure that every commercial batch of Glucogen-XR delivered by Google Health Sciences will provide the same safety and efficacy profile as the materials proven successful in pivotal human trials.

---
**References:**
1.  *FDA Guidance for Industry: Quality Systems Approach to Pharmaceutical CGMP Regulations (2006).*
2.  *ICH Q6B: Specifications for Biological Products.*
3.  *Google Health Sciences Internal Report GHS-RR-2025-04: Correlation of HMW Species to Patient ADA Profiles.*
4.  *USP <1223> Validation of Alternative Microbiological Methods.*

# Analytical Methodology Overview

## Orthogonal Analytical Strategy

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA SUMMARY)
## SECTION 3.2.S.4.2: ANALYTICAL PROCEDURES
### SUBSECTION: ORTHOGONAL ANALYTICAL STRATEGY FOR GLUCOGEN-XR (GLUCAPEPTIDE EXTENDED-RELEASE)

---

#### 3.2.S.4.2.1 Executive Summary of Orthogonal Philosophy
In accordance with **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **ICH Q11 (Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances)**, Google Health Sciences (GHS) has implemented a multi-dimensional orthogonal analytical strategy for Glucogen-XR. 

The complexity of the glucapeptide molecule—a high-molecular-weight recombinant peptide synthesized via the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line and subsequently formulated into an extended-release matrix—necessitates a testing regimen where no single attribute relies on a single mode of detection or separation. The strategy is designed to ensure that potential impurities (product-related and process-related) are monitored through physically and chemically distinct mechanisms, thereby eliminating "blind spots" in the molecular profile.

#### 3.2.S.4.2.2 Mapping of Orthogonal Attributes
The following table (Table 4.2.1-1) delineates the primary analytical targets and the corresponding orthogonal methods employed to verify consistent quality across batches **GLUC-2025-001** through **GLUC-2025-050**.

**Table 4.2.1-1: Orthogonal Method Mapping Matrix**

| Quality Attribute | Primary Method (Release) | Orthogonal Method 1 (Characterization) | Orthogonal Method 2 (In-Process) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Purity / Related Substances** | RP-HPLC (C18, 0.1% TFA/ACN) | HILIC-MS (Hydrophilic Interaction) | Ion-Pairing UPLC |
| **Charge Heterogeneity** | cIEF (Capillary Isoelectric Focusing) | CEX-HPLC (Cation Exchange) | Nano-LC-MS/MS (Bottom-up) |
| **Molecular Weight / Identity** | SE-UPLC (Size Exclusion) | Intact Mass Spectrometry (ESI-TOF) | SDS-PAGE (Reducing/Non-Red) |
| **Higher Order Structure (HOS)** | Far-UV Circular Dichroism (CD) | 2D-NMR (H-N HSQC) | FT-IR (Amide I/II Bands) |
| **Glycosylation (if applicable)** | N-Glycan Mapping (HILIC-FLD) | CE-LIF (Capillary Electrophoresis) | Lectin Blotting |
| **Aggregation State** | SE-UPLC | Dynamic Light Scattering (DLS) | Analytical Ultracentrifugation (AUC) |
| **Biological Activity** | Cell-Based cAMP Reporter Assay | SPR (Surface Plasmon Resonance) | ELISA (Binding Affinity) |

---

#### 3.2.S.4.2.3 Detailed Methodological Protocols and Specifications

##### 3.2.S.4.2.3.1 Purity Assessment: RP-UPLC vs. HILIC-MS
The primary purity test for Glucogen-XR is Reverse Phase Ultra-Performance Liquid Chromatography (RP-UPLC). However, to ensure that hydrophilic degradation products or truncated variants are not co-eluting with the main peak, HILIC-MS is utilized as the orthogonal verification.

**Protocol GLUC-SOP-098: RP-UPLC Parameters**
*   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC Protein BEH C18, 1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm.
*   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.05% Trifluoroacetic acid (TFA) in Water (LC-MS Grade).
*   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.04% TFA in Acetonitrile.
*   **Gradient:** 5% B to 65% B over 45 minutes.
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.3 mL/min.
*   **Detector:** 214 nm and 280 nm.

**Protocol GLUC-SOP-099: HILIC-MS Parameters (Orthogonal)**
*   **Column:** SeQuant ZIC-pHILIC, 5 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm.
*   **Mobile Phase A:** 20 mM Ammonium Acetate in 95% Water / 5% ACN (pH 6.8).
*   **Mobile Phase B:** 100% Acetonitrile.
*   **Mass Spectrometer:** Agilent 6545 Q-TOF (ESI+ mode).
*   **Source Temp:** 325°C.
*   **Drying Gas:** 10 L/min.

**Table 4.2.1-2: Purity Correlation Data (Batch GLUC-2025-012)**

| Method | Main Peak Area (%) | Truncated Variants (%) | Deamidated Variants (%) | Oxidized Variants (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **RP-UPLC** | 98.42% | 0.45% | 0.82% | 0.31% |
| **HILIC-MS** | 98.38% | 0.48% | 0.80% | 0.34% |
| **Difference** | 0.04% | 0.03% | 0.02% | 0.03% |

*Statistical Note: The R² correlation between the two methods across 15 validation batches was 0.998, confirming the robustness of the RP-UPLC release method.*

---

##### 3.2.S.4.2.3.2 Structural Integrity: Intact Mass Spectrometry (MS)
To confirm the primary sequence and post-translational modifications (PTMs), Google Health Sciences employs High-Resolution Accurate Mass (HRAM) spectrometry.

**Analytical Procedure:**
1.  **Desalting:** Glucogen-XR samples are desalted using a ZipTip C4 prior to injection.
2.  **Instrumentation:** Thermo Scientific Q Exactive Plus Orbitrap.
3.  **Software:** Protein Metrics Intact Mass™ for deconvolution.
4.  **Target Mass:** 58,422.45 Da (Theoretical).

**Table 4.2.1-3: Mass Accuracy Verification (Batches GLUC-2025-015 to GLUC-2025-020)**

| Batch ID | Observed Mass (Da) | Theoretical Mass (Da) | Δ ppm | Confirmation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-015 | 58,422.51 | 58,422.45 | 1.02 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-016 | 58,422.48 | 58,422.45 | 0.51 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-017 | 58,422.60 | 58,422.45 | 2.56 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-018 | 58,422.42 | 58,422.45 | -0.51 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-019 | 58,422.46 | 58,422.45 | 0.17 | Pass |

---

##### 3.2.S.4.2.3.3 Aggregation Analysis: SE-UPLC vs. AUC vs. DLS
Glucapeptide extended-release formulations are sensitive to shear-induced aggregation. We employ a three-tier orthogonal approach to ensure the absence of sub-visible particles and soluble aggregates.

**Tier 1: SE-UPLC (Routine Release)**
*   **Column:** Tosoh TSKgel G3000SWxl.
*   **Buffer:** 50 mM Phosphate, 200 mM NaCl, pH 7.0.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Monomer > 99.0%, Aggregates < 0.5%.

**Tier 2: Analytical Ultracentrifugation (AUC-SEDPHAT)**
AUC is used as the "Gold Standard" orthogonal method because it does not require a stationary phase, thus preventing the "filter effect" sometimes seen in HPLC columns where large aggregates are trapped in the frit.
*   **Speed:** 45,000 RPM.
*   **Temperature:** 20°C.
*   **Detection:** Interference optics.

**Tier 3: Dynamic Light Scattering (DLS)**
Used to monitor the hydrodynamic radius ($R_h$) and polydispersity index (PdI).
*   **Instrument:** Malvern Zetasizer Nano ZS.
*   **Formula for Diffusion Coefficient ($D$):**
    $$D = \frac{k_B T}{6\pi\eta R_h}$$
    *Where $k_B$ is Boltzmann's constant, $T$ is temperature, and $\eta$ is viscosity.*

**Table 4.2.1-4: Orthogonal Aggregation Comparison**

| Batch Number | SE-UPLC (% Monomer) | AUC (% Monomer) | DLS (Z-Avg, nm) | DLS (PdI) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-001 | 99.8% | 99.7% | 6.2 nm | 0.04 |
| GLUC-2025-005 | 99.6% | 99.5% | 6.4 nm | 0.05 |
| GLUC-2025-010 | 99.7% | 99.8% | 6.1 nm | 0.03 |

---

#### 3.2.S.4.2.4 Biological Potency Orthogonality

The biological activity of Glucogen-XR is assessed through its interaction with the GLP-1 receptor. The primary release assay is a cell-based cAMP induction assay, but this is supplemented by Surface Plasmon Resonance (SPR) to determine binding kinetics ($K_D$).

##### 3.2.S.4.2.4.1 Cell-Based Bioassay (Primary)
*   **Cell Line:** HEK293 stably transfected with human GLP-1R and a luciferase reporter under the control of a cAMP-response element (CRE).
*   **Reference Standard:** GHS-GLUC-REF-002.
*   **Statistical Model:** 4-Parameter Logistic (4-PL) fit.
    $$y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B}$$
    *Where A=min, D=max, C=EC50, B=slope.*

##### 3.2.S.4.2.4.2 SPR Binding Kinetics (Orthogonal)
*   **Chip:** CM5 Sensor Chip (Amine Coupling).
*   **Ligand:** Recombinant Human GLP-1 Receptor Extracellular Domain.
*   **Analysis:** 1:1 Langmuir Binding Model.
*   **Requirement:** $K_D$ must be within $0.8 - 1.2 \times 10^{-9}$ M.

**Table 4.2.1-5: Potency vs. Affinity Correlation**

| Batch ID | Relative Potency (%) | $K_D$ (M) | Association ($k_a$) | Dissociation ($k_d$) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-021 | 102% | $1.05 \times 10^{-9}$ | $4.2 \times 10^5$ | $4.4 \times 10^{-4}$ |
| GLUC-2025-022 | 98% | $0.98 \times 10^{-9}$ | $4.1 \times 10^5$ | $4.0 \times 10^{-4}$ |
| GLUC-2025-023 | 105% | $1.10 \times 10^{-9}$ | $4.3 \times 10^5$ | $4.7 \times 10^{-4}$ |

---

#### 3.2.S.4.2.5 Charge Heterogeneity: cIEF and CEX-HPLC
Glucogen-XR contains multiple acidic residues susceptible to deamidation. Charge variants are monitored orthogonally to ensure that the isoelectric point (pI) remains within the specified range of 4.8 to 5.4.

**cIEF Procedure (GLUC-SOP-202):**
1.  Sample concentration: 1.0 mg/mL.
2.  Ampholytes: pH 3–10.
3.  Focusing: 1 min at 1500 V, 7 min at 3000 V.
4.  Internal Markers: pI 4.1 and pI 7.0.

**CEX-HPLC Procedure (GLUC-SOP-203):**
1.  Column: Dionex ProPac WCX-10.
2.  Buffer A: 20 mM MES, pH 6.0.
3.  Buffer B: 20 mM MES + 500 mM NaCl, pH 6.0.

**Comparison of Results (Batch GLUC-2025-030):**
*   **cIEF Main Peak:** 84.5%
*   **CEX-HPLC Main Peak:** 84.1%
*   **Interpretation:** The close alignment of these results confirms that both methods effectively capture the acidic and basic variant profile of the glucapeptide.

---

#### 3.2.S.4.2.6 Regulatory Compliance and Future Commitments
Google Health Sciences commits to maintaining this orthogonal strategy throughout the lifecycle of Glucogen-XR. Any significant changes to the manufacturing process (Post-Approval Change Management Plan - PACMP) will trigger a re-validation of these orthogonal correlations to ensure that "drift" is not introduced into the molecular profile.

**References:**
1.  **USP <121>:** Insulin Assays (for comparative methodology).
2.  **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Monoclonal Antibodies (adapted for peptides).
3.  **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
4.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Development of Therapeutic Protein Biosimilars (2015) - regarding orthogonal characterization.

*Document End - Section 3.2.S.4.2*

## Compendial Methods vs. Proprietary Methods

**MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)**
**SECTION 3.2.S.4.2: ANALYTICAL PROCEDURES**
**SUBSECTION: COMPENDIAL METHODS VS. PROPRIETARY METHODS**

---

### 1.0 Executive Summary of Analytical Strategy
Google Health Sciences (GHS), a division of Google Cloud Life Sciences, utilizes a dual-track analytical framework for the characterization and release testing of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). This strategy aligns with ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and ensures that the Drug Substance (DS) meets the highest standards of safety, identity, strength, quality, and purity.

The analytical matrix is bifurcated into:
1.  **Compendial Methods:** Standardized procedures derived from the United States Pharmacopeia (USP) and National Formulary (NF), utilized primarily for general tests (e.g., pH, appearance, osmolality, residual moisture).
2.  **Proprietary (Non-Compendial) Methods:** Highly specialized, product-specific assays developed by GHS to address the unique structural attributes of the glucapeptide molecule and its extended-release profile.

---

### 2.0 Structural Hierarchy of Analytical Methodology

The following Table 1.1 provides a high-level overview of the differentiation between compendial and proprietary methods utilized for Glucogen-XR.

**Table 1.1: Categorization of Analytical Methods for Glucogen-XR (DS Batch GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-100)**

| Quality Attribute | Methodology Type | Primary Reference | Method ID | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Compendial | USP <790> / <791> | GHS-COMP-01 | Visual clarity and color |
| **pH** | Compendial | USP <791> | GHS-COMP-02 | Potentiometric measurement |
| **Osmolality** | Compendial | USP <785> | GHS-COMP-03 | Freezing point depression |
| **Purity (Related Substances)** | Proprietary | RPLC-PDA-MS | GHS-PROP-RP01 | Detection of deamidation/oxidation |
| **Charge Heterogeneity** | Proprietary | icIEF | GHS-PROP-IE04 | Isoelectric point and variants |
| **Potency (Biological Activity)** | Proprietary | Cell-based Bioassay | GHS-PROP-BIO | GLP-1 Receptor Activation |
| **Molecular Weight** | Proprietary | LC-MS/MS (ESI) | GHS-PROP-MS02 | Exact mass confirmation |
| **Bacterial Endotoxins** | Compendial | USP <85> | GHS-COMP-05 | LAL Kinetic Chromogenic |
| **Bioburden** | Compendial | USP <61> | GHS-COMP-06 | Microbial enumeration |
| **Extended Release Profile** | Proprietary | In Vitro Release (IVR) | GHS-PROP-ER09 | Controlled elution kinetics |

---

### 3.0 Compendial Methods: Implementation and Verification

While compendial methods are considered "validated" by the USP, Google Health Sciences performs rigorous **Method Verification** as per USP <1226> to ensure the suitability of these methods under the specific matrix conditions of Glucogen-XR.

#### 3.1 pH Determination (USP <791>)
The pH of Glucogen-XR DS is critical for the stability of the peptide backbone and the integrity of the extended-release matrix.

*   **Equipment:** Metrohm 905 Titrando with i-Point Electrode (GHS-EQ-8821).
*   **Procedure:**
    1.  Standardize the pH meter using three NIST-traceable buffers (pH 4.01, 7.00, and 10.01).
    2.  Ensure temperature compensation is active at 25°C ± 0.5°C.
    3.  Aliquots of 2.0 mL from Batch GLUC-2025-XXX are analyzed in triplicate.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** 6.8 – 7.2.

#### 3.2 Bacterial Endotoxins (USP <85>)
Given the subcutaneous administration of Glucogen-XR, endotoxin control is paramount. GHS employs Method D (Kinetic Chromogenic Method).

*   **Calculations for Maximum Valid Dilution (MVD):**
    $$MVD = \frac{L \times C}{P}$$
    Where:
    *   $L$ = Endotoxin limit (0.5 EU/mg)
    *   $C$ = Concentration of DS (20 mg/mL)
    *   $P$ = Sensitivity of the lysate (0.005 EU/mL)
    *   **MVD Result:** 1:2000.
*   **Verification Data (Batch GLUC-2025-001):** Recovery of spiked endotoxin (0.5 EU/mL) was 105%, within the USP requirement of 50-200%.

---

### 4.0 Proprietary Methods: Advanced Characterization Protocols

The proprietary methods for Glucogen-XR are designed to monitor the **Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs)** that cannot be captured by compendial techniques.

#### 4.1 GHS-PROP-RP01: Reversed-Phase Ultra-High Performance Liquid Chromatography (RP-UHPLC)
This method is used for the quantification of purity and related substances, specifically focusing on the deamidation of Asn and Gln residues.

**Chromatographic Conditions:**
*   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC Protein BEH C4, 300Å, 1.7 µm, 2.1 mm X 150 mm.
*   **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% TFA in Water (Milli-Q Grade).
*   **Mobile Phase B:** 0.08% TFA in Acetonitrile (Optima Grade).
*   **Gradient Profile:**
    *   0-5 min: 25% B
    *   5-35 min: 25-45% B (Linear)
    *   35-40 min: 80% B (Wash)
    *   40-50 min: 25% B (Re-equilibration)
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.3 mL/min.
*   **Detection:** 214 nm and 280 nm.

**Statistical Precision Analysis for Batch GLUC-2025-005:**
The following data represents the repeatability of the Main Peak area percentage across six replicates.

| Injection | Main Peak Area (%) | Total Impurities (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | 98.45 | 1.55 |
| 2 | 98.42 | 1.58 |
| 3 | 98.48 | 1.52 |
| 4 | 98.44 | 1.56 |
| 5 | 98.46 | 1.54 |
| 6 | 98.45 | 1.55 |
| **Mean** | **98.45** | **1.55** |
| **%RSD** | **0.021** | **1.28** |

#### 4.2 GHS-PROP-BIO: Cell-Based GLP-1 Receptor Activation Bioassay
Since Glucogen-XR is a GLP-1 receptor agonist, potency must be measured via its biological activity rather than simple mass.

*   **Cell Line:** HEK-293 cells transfected with human GLP-1R and a cAMP-response element (CRE) luciferase reporter.
*   **Reference Standard:** GHS-GLUC-REF-2024.
*   **Procedure:**
    1.  Cells are seeded in 96-well plates at $5 \times 10^4$ cells/well.
    2.  Serial dilutions of DS (Batch GLUC-2025-XXX) are prepared (10-point curve).
    3.  Incubation for 4 hours at 37°C, 5% $CO_2$.
    4.  Luciferase activity is measured using a GloMax® Navigator Microplate Luminometer.
*   **Data Analysis:** A 4-parameter logistic (4PL) model is used to calculate the $EC_{50}$.
    $$y = \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B} + D$$
    Where $C$ is the $EC_{50}$ (Potency).
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Relative Potency (RP) must be 80% - 125% of the Reference Standard.

---

### 5.0 Comparative Matrix: Analytical Justification

The following section justifies why proprietary methods were developed over existing USP chapters for specific attributes.

**Table 1.2: Justification for Proprietary Methodology**

| Attribute | Compendial Method (USP) | GHS Proprietary Method | Justification for Proprietary Selection |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Purity** | USP <621> (General LC) | GHS-PROP-RP01 | USP <621> lacks the resolution required for the complex deamidation species of glucapeptide. |
| **Identity** | USP <197> (IR) | GHS-PROP-MS02 (MS) | IR is insufficient for large biologics. LC-MS/MS provides sequence-level confirmation. |
| **Charge Profile** | USP <129> (Standard CE) | GHS-PROP-IE04 (icIEF) | icIEF provides superior resolution of acidic/basic variants in the GHS-CHO-001 cell line. |

---

### 6.0 Detailed Protocol: GHS-PROP-ER09 (In Vitro Release)

This protocol is unique to the "Extended Release" (XR) designation of Glucogen-XR. It utilizes a proprietary dissolution apparatus designed at Google Health Sciences' South San Francisco facility.

**Step-by-Step Procedure:**
1.  **Medium Preparation:** Prepare 500 mL of Phosphate Buffered Saline (PBS) with 0.05% Tween 80, adjusted to pH 7.4.
2.  **Apparatus Setup:** Use USP Dissolution Apparatus 4 (Flow-Through Cell).
3.  **Loading:** Load 100 mg of DS (equivalent to 1 full dose) into the cell with 5mm glass beads.
4.  **Flow Rate:** Set to 2.0 mL/min (simulating subcutaneous interstitial fluid flow).
5.  **Sampling Intervals:** 1, 4, 8, 12, 24, 48, 72, 96, and 168 hours.
6.  **Analysis:** Quantify the released peptide using RP-HPLC (Method GHS-PROP-RP01).

**Target Release Profile (Release Kinetics):**
*   $T = 24h$: $15\% - 25\%$
*   $T = 72h$: $45\% - 65\%$
*   $T = 168h$: $\geq 85\%$

---

To demonstrate the consistency between compendial and proprietary results, data from three consecutive validation batches are provided below.

**Table 1.3: Comparison of Results for Batches GLUC-2025-001, 002, 003**

| Method | Specification | GLUC-2025-001 | GLUC-2025-002 | GLUC-2025-003 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **USP <791> (pH)** | 6.8 - 7.2 | 7.02 | 7.05 | 6.99 |
| **USP <85> (Endo)** | < 0.5 EU/mg | < 0.05 | < 0.05 | < 0.05 |
| **GHS-PROP-RP01 (Purity)** | ≥ 97.0% | 98.8% | 99.1% | 98.9% |
| **GHS-PROP-BIO (Potency)** | 0.8 - 1.25 RP | 1.05 | 0.98 | 1.12 |

## Method Lifecycle Management

# **MODULE 3: QUALITY**
## **3.2.S. DRUG SUBSTANCE**
### **3.2.S.4. Control of Drug Substance**
#### **3.2.S.4.2. Analytical Procedures**
---
### **SECTION: METHOD LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT (MLM)**

---

#### **1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE**
The Method Lifecycle Management (MLM) framework for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) establishes a holistic, risk-based approach to the development, qualification, validation, and continuous monitoring of analytical procedures. This program aligns with the principles of **ICH Q14 (Analytical Procedure Development)** and **ICH Q2(R2) (Validation of Analytical Procedures)**, ensuring that all methods utilized for the release and stability testing of Glucogen-XR remain fit for their intended purpose throughout the product life cycle.

Google Health Sciences (GHS) operates under a Stage-Gate lifecycle model, integrating Quality by Design (QbD) principles into analytical development. This document details the procedures for maintaining the Analytical Target Profile (ATP), managing method performance, and executing technical transfers across the Google Cloud Life Sciences manufacturing network.

---

#### **2.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDANCE ALIGNMENT**
The MLM strategy for Glucogen-XR is governed by the following regulatory frameworks:
*   **ICH Q2(R2):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
*   **ICH Q14:** Analytical Procedure Development.
*   **ICH Q8(R2):** Pharmaceutical Development.
*   **ICH Q9(R1):** Quality Risk Management.
*   **USP <1220>:** Analytical Procedure Lifecycle.
*   **USP <1210>:** Statistical Tools for Procedure Validation.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (July 2015).

---

#### **3.0 THE ANALYTICAL TARGET PROFILE (ATP)**
The ATP defines the performance requirements for the analytical method, focusing on the quality attributes of Glucogen-XR. It serves as the foundation for the lifecycle, defining the "what" rather than the "how."

##### **3.1 Primary ATP for Glucogen-XR Purity (RP-HPLC)**
The following table outlines the ATP for the determination of related substances and peptide purity.

**Table 3.1-1: Analytical Target Profile (ATP-001) for RP-HPLC Purity**

| Parameter | Performance Requirement | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Analyte** | Glucapeptide (active moiety) | Core therapeutic ingredient |
| **Matrix** | Extended-release polymer matrix / DS Buffer | Ensure no matrix interference |
| **Reportable Range** | 50% to 150% of target concentration (0.5 mg/mL) | Cover assay and impurity levels |
| **Accuracy (Recovery)** | 98.0% – 102.0% | Required for potency determination |
| **Precision (Repeatability)** | %RSD ≤ 1.0% (n=6) | High precision for peptide quantification |
| **Intermediate Precision** | %RSD ≤ 2.0% (n=12) | Consistency across analysts/days |
| **Specificity** | No interference > 0.05% at peptide RT | Critical for impurity identification |
| **Sensitivity (LOD/LOQ)** | LOQ ≤ 0.05% relative to main peak | Compliance with ICH Q3A(R2) |

---

#### **4.0 STAGE 1: ANALYTICAL PROCEDURE DEVELOPMENT AND DESIGN**
During Stage 1, GHS utilizes **Design of Experiments (DoE)** to establish the Method Operable Design Region (MODR).

##### **4.1 Risk Assessment (Failure Mode and Effects Analysis - FMEA)**
Prior to validation, a risk assessment is performed to identify variables impacting method performance.

**Table 4.1-1: FMEA for SEC-HPLC (Size Variation) Method**

| Process Step | Potential Failure Mode | Severity (S) | Occurrence (O) | Detectability (D) | RPN | Mitigation Strategy |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Mobile Phase Prep | pH variation ± 0.2 | 4 | 3 | 2 | 24 | Use calibrated pH meters; Auto-titration |
| Column Oven | Temp fluctuation ± 5°C | 3 | 2 | 2 | 12 | Standardize equilibration time (60 min) |
| Sample Prep | Aggregation due to vortexing | 5 | 2 | 2 | 20 | Use gentle inversion; specified temp (5°C) |
| Data Integration | Baseline drift | 3 | 4 | 1 | 12 | Automated integration with manual audit |

##### **4.2 Method Operable Design Region (MODR) Calculation**
The MODR for the Glucogen-XR RP-HPLC method was determined using a Central Composite Design (CCD).
*   **Factor A:** Methanol percentage in Mobile Phase B (70% - 90%)
*   **Factor B:** Column Temperature (35°C - 45°C)
*   **Factor C:** Flow Rate (0.8 - 1.2 mL/min)

**Statistical Model (Response Surface):**
$$Y (Resolution) = \beta_0 + \beta_1 A + \beta_2 B + \beta_3 C + \beta_{12} AB + \beta_{13} AC + \beta_{23} BC + \beta_{11} A^2 + \beta_{22} B^2 + \beta_{33} C^2 + \epsilon$$

---

#### **5.0 STAGE 2: ANALYTICAL PROCEDURE PERFORMANCE QUALIFICATION (VALIDATION)**
Validation confirms that the method meets the ATP requirements. GHS conducts validation using specific batch lots of Glucogen-XR.

##### **5.1 Validation Protocol: VP-GLUC-2025-001**
**Objective:** To validate the potency assay for Glucogen-XR Drug Substance.
**Test Site:** Google Health Sciences, 3000 Innovation Drive, SSF, CA.

**Table 5.1-1: Validation Batch Traceability**

| Material | Batch Number | Date of Manufacture | Use |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Glucogen-XR DS | GLUC-2025-001 | 15-JAN-2025 | Accuracy/Precision |
| Glucogen-XR DS | GLUC-2025-002 | 22-JAN-2025 | Robustness |
| Reference Standard | GHS-REF-PEP-09 | 01-DEC-2024 | Calibration/System Suitability |

##### **5.2 Specificity and Forced Degradation**
Specificity is demonstrated by the ability to assess the analyte in the presence of degradants. Glucogen-XR was subjected to stress conditions:
1.  **Acid Stress:** 0.1M HCl at 60°C for 24 hours.
2.  **Base Stress:** 0.1M NaOH at 60°C for 24 hours.
3.  **Oxidative Stress:** 3% H2O2 at Room Temperature for 12 hours.
4.  **Photolytic Stress:** 1.2 million lux-hours (ICH Q1B).

**Table 5.2-1: Forced Degradation Results (Batch GLUC-2025-001)**

| Condition | % Recovery | % Total Impurities | Peak Purity Index | Mass Balance (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Control | 100.0 | 0.22 | 0.9999 | 100.0 |
| Acid (0.1M HCl) | 88.4 | 11.2 | 0.9992 | 99.6 |
| Base (0.1M NaOH)| 75.2 | 23.9 | 0.9985 | 99.1 |
| Peroxide (H2O2) | 92.1 | 7.6 | 0.9995 | 99.7 |

---

#### **6.0 STAGE 3: ONGOING ANALYTICAL PROCEDURE PERFORMANCE VERIFICATION**
GHS employs a Continuous Performance Monitoring (CPM) program to track method stability over time.

##### **6.1 Statistical Process Control (SPC)**
Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) are tracked for every GMP run of Glucogen-XR.
*   **KPI 1:** Theoretical Plates (N) for main peak.
*   **KPI 2:** Tailing Factor (T).
*   **KPI 3:** Retention Time (RT) stability.
*   **KPI 4:** %RSD of Check Standard recoveries.

**Calculation for Process Capability Index (Cpk):**
$$Cpk = \min \left( \frac{USL - \mu}{3\sigma}, \frac{\mu - LSL}{3\sigma} \right)$$
*Where $\mu$ is the mean of the system suitability results and $\sigma$ is the standard deviation.*

##### **6.2 Control Chart Analysis (Example Batch Series GLUC-2025-101 to 120)**
**Table 6.2-1: Trending Data for System Suitability (Tailing Factor)**

| Batch ID | Analyst | Instrument | Tailing Factor | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-101 | J. Doe | Agilent 1290-A | 1.05 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-105 | A. Smith | Agilent 1290-B | 1.08 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-110 | J. Doe | Agilent 1290-A | 1.04 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-115 | R. Kumar | Waters Arc-01 | 1.12 | Pass |
| GLUC-2025-120 | A. Smith | Agilent 1290-B | 1.07 | Pass |

---

#### **7.0 ANALYTICAL METHOD TRANSFER (AMT) PROTOCOLS**
When Glucogen-XR testing is moved from GHS South San Francisco to a Contract Testing Laboratory (CTL), a formal AMT is required.

##### **7.1 Transfer Criteria (Comparative Testing)**
The receiving laboratory (RL) must test three batches in triplicate. The results are compared to the sending laboratory (SL) results using a Two-One Sided T-test (TOST) for equivalence.

**Equivalence Margin ($\theta$):** ± 2.0% for Assay.

**Table 7.1-1: Method Transfer Plan (SOP-QC-550)**

| Step | Action | Responsibility | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | Training on Glucogen-XR Prep | SL | Training logs signed |
| 2 | System Suitability Run | RL | Meets SOP-QC-SEC-01 |
| 3 | Testing Batch GLUC-2025-050 | RL | Result within 2% of SL |
| 4 | Intermediate Precision | RL | %RSD < 2.0% (n=6) |

---

#### **8.0 CHANGE CONTROL AND REVALIDATION STRATEGY**
Any modification to an established method triggers a "Method Impact Assessment" (MIA).

##### **8.1 Change Classification Matrix**
*   **Minor (Level 1):** Change in column serial number, different brand of equivalent HPLC vials. *Action: Document in instrument log.*
*   **Moderate (Level 2):** Adjustment of flow rate within MODR, update to integration software version. *Action: Verification run.*
*   **Major (Level 3):** Change in column stationary phase, change in detection wavelength, new API manufacturer. *Action: Full Revalidation.*

---

#### **9.0 REFERENCE STANDARDS LIFECYCLE**
The primary reference standard (GHS-RS-GLUC-01) is characterized using orthogonal techniques:
1.  **Mass Spectrometry (Orbitrap):** Molecular weight confirmation.
2.  **NMR (600 MHz):** Structural elucidation.
3.  **Amino Acid Analysis (AAA):** Absolute peptide content.
4.  **Karl Fischer:** Moisture content.

**Table 9.1-1: Reference Standard Re-qualification Schedule**

| Standard ID | Grade | Initial Purity | Last Testing Date | Next Re-test Date |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GHS-REF-PEP-09 | Primary | 99.85% | 01-JAN-2025 | 01-JAN-2026 |
| GHS-WRK-PEP-22 | Working | 99.72% | 15-FEB-2025 | 15-AUG-2025 |

---

#### **10.0 DATA INTEGRITY AND SOFTWARE VALIDATION**
All analytical data for Glucogen-XR is managed via Google Cloud Life Sciences' proprietary **GXP-Cloud LIMS**.
*   **Audit Trails:** Enabled for all chromatographic injections.
*   **Archiving:** Data is stored in redundant cloud regions with a 15-year retention policy.
*   **Electronic Signatures:** Compliant with 21 CFR Part 11.

---

#### **11.0 BIBLIOGRAPHY AND REFERENCES**
1.  **United States Pharmacopeia (USP)** Chapter <1224> Transfer of Analytical Procedures.
2.  **USP <1225>** Validation of Compendial Procedures.

# Regulatory History

## IND Application and Amendments

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S DRUG SUBSTANCE
### 3.2.S.1 GENERAL INFORMATION
#### 3.2.S.1.4 REGULATORY HISTORY: IND APPLICATION AND AMENDMENTS

---

### 1.4.1. Executive Summary of Regulatory Engagement
The regulatory history of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**, manufactured by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)**, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences, reflects a comprehensive and iterative dialogue with the **U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA)**, specifically the Center for Drug Evaluation and Research (CDER), Office of Tissues and Advanced Therapies (OTAT) [formerly], and the Division of Diabetes, Lipid Disorders, and Obesity.

The development program was initiated under **IND #168,422**, submitted on October 12, 2022. The program has been characterized by rigorous adherence to ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and ICH Q5A through Q5E.

### 1.4.2. Initial Investigational New Drug (IND) Submission
The original IND (Sequence 0001) provided the foundational CMC, non-clinical, and clinical protocol data for the Phase 1 First-in-Human (FIH) study of Glucogen-XR.

#### 1.4.2.1. Initial CMC Data Package
The CMC section of the initial IND focused on the characterization of the **GHS-CHO-001 cell line** (a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative) and the preliminary manufacturing process (Process Version 1.0).

**Table 1.4.2-1: Initial IND Submission Components (Sequence 0001)**
| Module | Section | Title | Content Focus |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | 1.2 | Cover Letter | Request for Phase 1 initiation; Summary of Fast Track Designation request. |
| 2 | 2.3 | Quality Overall Summary | High-level summary of the recombinant peptide synthesis and ER formulation. |
| 3 | 3.2.S | Drug Substance | Description of the GS-knockout CHO expression system and Protein A purification. |
| 3 | 3.2.P | Drug Product | Formulation of 1.0 mg/mL Glucogen-XR in a PLGA-based microsphere matrix. |
| 4 | 4.2 | Non-clinical Study Reports | PK/PD profiles in cynomolgus monkeys and Sprague-Dawley rats. |

### 1.4.3. Chronological History of IND Amendments
Since the initial filing, Google Health Sciences has submitted a series of amendments to support manufacturing scale-up, process optimization, and the introduction of a new delivery device.

#### 1.4.3.1. CMC Amendments (Quality-Related)
The following table details the quality-related amendments submitted under IND #168,422.

**Table 1.4.3-1: Summary of CMC Amendments for Glucogen-XR**
| Seq # | Date | Category | Description of Change / Amendment | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 0005 | 15-JAN-2023 | Protocol | Introduction of Post-Approval Stability Protocol (PASP) for Batch GLUC-2023-001. | Acknowledged |
| 0012 | 22-MAY-2023 | Process | Scale-up of DS manufacture from 50L to 500L Single-Use Bioreactor (SUB). | Reviewed |
| 0018 | 10-SEP-2023 | Analytical | Implementation of a new RP-HPLC method for purity (Method Met-00452). | Approved |
| 0024 | 04-JAN-2024 | Facility | Site transfer of Fill/Finish to 3000 Innovation Drive, SSF, CA. | Inspected |
| 0031 | 12-MAR-2024 | Specification | Tightening of HCP (Host Cell Protein) limits from <100 ppm to <20 ppm. | Accepted |
| 0045 | 18-AUG-2024 | Formulation | Inclusion of a high-concentration (5.0 mg/mL) variant for Phase 3. | Active |

---

### 1.4.4. Detailed Review of Critical Amendments
#### 1.4.4.1. Amendment 0012: Scale-Up and Process Version 2.0
In May 2023, GHS submitted a major CMC amendment to transition from the clinical pilot scale (50L) to the pivotal clinical scale (500L). This transition involved the migration from a traditional stainless steel stirred-tank reactor to a **HyClone™ S.U.B.** platform.

**Step-by-Step Scale-Up Protocol (SOP-GHS-7782):**
1. **Inoculum Expansion:** Sequential expansion from WCB (Working Cell Bank) vial thaw to 10L Wave Bioreactor.
2. **Transfer Criteria:** VCD (Viable Cell Density) must reach $>8.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL with viability $>98\%$.
3. **Bioreactor Parameters:** 
   - pH: $7.0 \pm 0.1$ (controlled via $CO_2$ sparging and $NaCO_3$ addition).
   - Dissolved Oxygen (DO): 40% of air saturation.
   - Temperature: $36.5^{\circ}C$ shift to $33.0^{\circ}C$ on Day 5 to enhance protein folding.
4. **Harvest:** Continuous centrifugation at 5,000 x g followed by depth filtration (Millistak+® HC Pro).

**Data Comparison: 50L vs. 500L (Batch Comparison)**
| Parameter | Pilot Scale (GLUC-2023-008) | Pivotal Scale (GLUC-2024-001) | Specification |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Harvest Titer (g/L) | 3.2 | 3.5 | Report Result |
| Glycan Profile (G0F) | 78.2% | 79.1% | 75% - 85% |
| High Molecular Weight (HMW) | 0.8% | 1.1% | $\leq 2.0\%$ |
| Endotoxin (EU/mg) | <0.05 | <0.05 | $\leq 0.1$ |

#### 1.4.4.2. Amendment 0031: Analytical Method Validation and Specification Update
Following the "Pre-Phase 2" meeting with the FDA, GHS refined the analytical suite to include a more sensitive assay for **Glucapeptide-specific Aggregation Rates (GSAR)**.

**Table 1.4.4-2: Updated Specification Comparison (Post-Amendment 0031)**
| Quality Attribute | Original Limit (Seq 0001) | Amended Limit (Seq 0031) | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Purity by SE-HPLC | $\geq 95.0\%$ | $\geq 98.5\%$ | Alignment with ICH Q6B |
| Residual DNA | $\leq 100$ pg/mg | $\leq 10$ pg/mg | Improved purification efficiency |
| Potency (In vitro) | 80% - 120% | 90% - 110% | Process consistency data |

### 1.4.6. Regulatory Communications and Formal Meetings
Google Health Sciences has maintained active communication with the FDA to ensure the Glucogen-XR development program meets the rigorous standards for biological products.

#### 1.4.6.1. Pre-IND Meeting (PIND #155,200) - June 2022
*   **Topic:** Acceptability of the GS-knockout CHO-K1 cell line and the proposed viral clearance strategy.
*   **FDA Feedback:** The Agency agreed with the use of a 2-step orthogonal viral inactivation/removal process (Solvent/Detergent treatment and Nano-filtration).
*   **GHS Action:** Integrated a 20nm virus-retentive filter (Planova™ 20N) into the downstream process.

#### 1.4.6.2. Type B Meeting (End-of-Phase 2) - September 2024
*   **Topic:** Proposed Phase 3 manufacturing scale and validation of the extended-release microsphere technology.
*   **FDA Feedback:** Requested additional data on the leachables/extractables profile of the new 500L Single-Use Bioreactor bags.
*   **GHS Action:** Initiated study **GHS-RPT-2024-09** (Extractables Profile of Polyethylene Film in DS Manufacture).

---

### 1.4.7. Statistical Analysis of Process Consistency
To support the IND amendments, GHS utilized a **Process Capability Index ($C_{pk}$)** analysis for the primary potency assay across the 500L batches.

**Formula utilized:**
$$C_{pk} = \min \left( \frac{USL - \mu}{3\sigma}, \frac{\mu - LSL}{3\sigma} \right)$$

*Where:*
*   $USL = 110\%$ (Upper Specification Limit)
*   $LSL = 90\%$ (Lower Specification Limit)
*   $\mu = 99.8\%$ (Mean Potency across 5 batches)
*   $\sigma = 1.2\%$ (Standard Deviation)

**Result:** $C_{pk} = 2.72$, indicating a highly capable and controlled manufacturing process, exceeding the industry standard of $1.33$.

### 1.4.8. References to USP and ICH Guidelines
The following standards are referenced throughout the IND amendments:
1.  **USP <1043>:** Ancillary Materials for Cell, Gene, and Tissue-Engineered Products.
2.  **USP <129>:** Analytical Procedures for Recombinant Therapeutic Monoclonal Antibodies (adapted for Glucapeptides).
3.  **ICH Q5D:** Derivation and Characterization of Cell Substrates Used for Production of Biotechnological/Biological Products.
4.  **ICH Q11:** Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances (Chemical Entities and Biotechnological/Biological Entities).

---
*End of Subsection 1.4: Regulatory History*
*Document ID: GHS-GLUC-M3-DS-REG-2025*
*Confidential - Property of Google Health Sciences*

## FDA Feedback and Commitments

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE (GENERAL INFORMATION)
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.1.4: REGULATORY HISTORY – FDA FEEDBACK AND COMMITMENTS

---

#### 1.4.1 Executive Overview of Regulatory Interactions
This section provides a comprehensive chronological account of the formal interactions between **Google Health Sciences (GHS)**, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences, and the **U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA)** Center for Drug Evaluation and Research (CDER), specifically the Office of Tissues and Advanced Therapies (OTAT) and the Office of Biotechnology Products (OBP), regarding the development of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**.

Glucogen-XR is a recombinant human glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1) analogue produced in a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative cell line (**GHS-CHO-001**). Due to its unique extended-release profile achieved through a novel peptide-linker-polymer conjugation, the FDA requested specific focus on structural characterization, impurity profiling of the linker-polymer moiety, and the validation of the manufacturing process at the South San Francisco facility (3000 Innovation Drive).

---

#### 1.4.2 Chronology of Formal Regulatory Meetings

| Meeting Type | Date | Reference ID | Primary Objective |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Pre-IND Meeting** | 14-OCT-2022 | PIND-158922 | Discussion of CMC strategy and cell line development. |
| **Type B Meeting** | 22-MAY-2023 | IND-158922-M001 | End of Phase 1 (EOP1) feedback on impurity profile. |
| **Type B Meeting** | 18-JAN-2024 | IND-158922-M005 | End of Phase 2 (EOP2) manufacturing scale-up. |
| **Pre-BLA Meeting** | 12-FEB-2025 | BLA-761440-PRE | CMC readiness and validation data requirements. |

---

#### 1.4.3 Detailed FDA Feedback and GHS Commitments

##### 1.4.3.1 Cell Line Development and Genetic Stability (GHS-CHO-001)
During the Pre-IND meeting (PIND-158922), the FDA expressed concerns regarding the genetic stability of the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** cell line, specifically the impact of the GS (Glutamine Synthetase) knockout on long-term phenotype consistency.

*   **FDA Feedback (PIND-158922):** "The sponsor should provide comprehensive data demonstrating the genetic stability of the Master Cell Bank (MCB) and Working Cell Bank (WCB) up to and beyond the limit of in vitro cell age (LIVA) for the proposed commercial process."
*   **GHS Commitment:** GHS committed to performing Southern Blot analysis and Next-Generation Sequencing (NGS) to verify copy number stability and integration site integrity across 60 generations.

**Table 1.4.3.1-A: Genetic Stability Analysis Data (Batch GLUC-2025-MCB01)**
| Analysis Parameter | Methodology | Acceptance Criteria | Result (LIVA + 20 Gen) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Copy Number** | qPCR / Droplet Digital PCR | 15 ± 3 copies/cell | 14.8 copies/cell (Pass) |
| **mRNA Sequence** | Sanger Sequencing | 100% Homology to GLP-1 | 100% Match (Pass) |
| **Integration Site** | NGS (Illumina HiSeq) | No de novo insertions | Verified (Pass) |
| **Karyotype** | G-Banding | 2n = 20-24 (Modal 21) | Consistent (Pass) |

---

##### 1.4.3.2 Linker-Polymer Characterization and Impurity Profiling
A critical point of discussion during the EOP2 meeting (IND-158922-M005) involved the extended-release mechanism. Glucogen-XR utilizes a proprietary PEG-based high-molecular-weight linker.

*   **FDA Feedback:** "The agency requires a detailed impurity profile for the linker-polymer, including polydispersity indices (PDI) and the identification of degradation products resulting from the sterilization process of the polymer prior to conjugation."
*   **GHS Commitment:** GHS established a Multi-Angle Light Scattering (MALS) protocol integrated with Size-Exclusion Chromatography (SEC) to monitor PDI.

**Protocol GHS-QC-882: Polydispersity Index (PDI) Determination**
1. **Instrument Calibration:** Calibrate the SEC-MALS system using Bovine Serum Albumin (BSA) (NIST-traceable) to determine the instrument constant ($K$).
2. **Sample Preparation:** Dissolve Glucogen-XR intermediate (Batch GLUC-2025-LNK-01) in PBS (pH 7.4) at 2.0 mg/mL.
3. **Calculation:** Use the Zimm equation for light scattering:
   $$\frac{Kc}{R_{\theta}} = \frac{1}{M_w P(\theta)} + 2A_2 c$$
   Where $M_w$ is the weight-average molecular weight and $P(\theta)$ is the form factor.
4. **Data Acceptance:** PDI ($M_w/M_n$) must remain within $1.02 - 1.05$.

---

##### 1.4.3.3 Manufacturing Scale-Up and Validation (GLUC-2025-XXX Series)
In the Pre-BLA communication, the FDA emphasized the need for Process Performance Qualification (PPQ) across three consecutive batches at the commercial scale (2,000L).

*   **FDA Feedback (BLA-761440-PRE):** "Identify the Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs) that will be monitored during the PPQ runs and provide a statistical justification for the sampling plan."
*   **GHS Commitment:** GHS implemented a rigorous PPQ program using Batches **GLUC-2025-VAL01**, **GLUC-2025-VAL02**, and **GLUC-2025-VAL03**.

**Table 1.4.3.3-B: PPQ Batch Consistency Data**
| Attribute | Unit | GLUC-2025-VAL01 | GLUC-2025-VAL02 | GLUC-2025-VAL03 | Statistical P-Value |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Bioreactor Yield** | g/L | 4.82 | 4.91 | 4.85 | 0.94 (NS) |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | % | 99.4 | 99.5 | 99.3 | 0.88 (NS) |
| **HCP Content** | ppm | < 10 | < 10 | < 10 | N/A |
| **Endotoxin** | EU/mg | < 0.05 | < 0.05 | < 0.05 | N/A |
| **Aggregation** | % SEC | 0.22 | 0.19 | 0.25 | 0.91 (NS) |

*NS: Non-significant, indicating high process reproducibility.*

---

#### 1.4.4 Post-Marketing Commitments (PMC) and Post-Marketing Requirements (PMR)
GHS has agreed to the following commitments to be fulfilled post-approval, as discussed during the final CMC wrap-up meeting on 10-MAR-2025.

**1.4.4.1 PMC #1: Sub-visible Particulate Characterization**
*   **Description:** GHS will conduct a study to characterize sub-visible particles (SVP) in the size range of 2 µm to 10 µm using Flow Imaging Microscopy (MFI) for the first five commercial lots.
*   **Timeline:** Data submission by Q4 2026.

**1.4.4.2 PMC #2: Leachable/Extractable Assessment**
*   **Description:** GHS will perform an exhaustive 24-month extractable and leachable (E&L) study on the primary container closure system (pre-filled syringe, Equipment ID: GHS-PFS-77).
*   **Protocol Reference:** USP <1663> and USP <1664>.

---

#### 1.4.5 Technical Response to FDA Request for Information (RFI) - Case Study
On 15-JAN-2025, the FDA requested clarification on the "Glucapeptide-Linker Charge Variant Distribution" during accelerated stability testing (40°C/75% RH).

**GHS Response Summary:**
GHS demonstrated through Cation Exchange Chromatography (CEX-HPLC) that the acidic variants observed were the result of deamidation at the $Asn^{28}$ position of the glucapeptide. However, potency assays (In vitro cAMP activation) confirmed that deamidated Glucogen-XR retains 98% bioactivity compared to the reference standard.

**Statistical Analysis of Variant Potency:**
$$Potency_{Relative} = \frac{EC_{50, Standard}}{EC_{50, Sample}} \times 100$$
*   **Standard EC50:** 12.4 pM
*   **Deamidated Sample EC50:** 12.6 pM
*   **Result:** 98.4% Relative Potency (Within specification of 80-125%).

---

#### 1.4.6 Conclusion of Regulatory History
Google Health Sciences has addressed all FDA queries raised during the IND phase. All commitments regarding the **GLUC-2025-XXX** batch series and the **GHS-CHO-001** cell line have been integrated into the Master Production Record (MPR) version 4.0. The manufacturing process at 3000 Innovation Drive is deemed "In-Control" and "Validated" per ICH Q10 guidelines.

## Manufacturing Changes During Development

### 3.2.S.2.6 Manufacturing Process Development
#### Subsection: Manufacturing Changes During Development (Historical Evolution)

**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-M3-DS-2.6-CHG-001  
**Product:** Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)  
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080  
**Effective Date:** 24 October 2024  
**Regulatory Status:** IND 158,294 / BLA Submission Preparation  

---

### 1.0 OVERVIEW OF PROCESS EVOLUTION
The manufacturing process for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) has undergone significant evolution from the initial Discovery Phase through Phase 3 Pivotal Clinical Trials. The development strategy employed by Google Health Sciences (GHS) followed a "Quality by Design" (QbD) approach, utilizing High-Throughput Screening (HTS) and Google Cloud AI-driven predictive modeling to optimize protein folding and glycosylation patterns.

The process evolution is categorized into four primary generations (Gen 1.0 to Gen 4.0), transitioning from transient expression systems to the final commercial-scale GHS-CHO-001 GS-knockout stable cell line process.

---

### 2.0 TABULATED SUMMARY OF MANUFACTURING CHANGES
The following table (Table 2.6-1) summarizes the major process versions, the associated clinical phases, and the rationale for the modifications implemented.

#### Table 2.6-1: Summary of Manufacturing Process Changes for Glucogen-XR

| Process Version | Batch Series (Representative) | Clinical Phase | Site of Manufacture | Key Changes & Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Gen 1.0** (Discovery) | GLUC-2022-001 to 010 | Pre-clinical / Toxicology | GHS Lab Scale (SSF) | Initial transient HEK293 expression; Flask-based; Manual purification. |
| **Gen 2.0** (Phase 1) | GLUC-2023-101 to 105 | Phase 1 (SAD/MAD) | GHS Pilot Plant (SSF) | Transition to CHO-K1 GS-KO; 50L SUB; Introduction of Protein A capture. |
| **Gen 3.0** (Phase 2) | GLUC-2024-201 to 215 | Phase 2 Dose Finding | GHS Clinical Mfg (SSF) | Scale-up to 500L; Change in peptone-free media; Optimization of XR-Polymer conjugation. |
| **Gen 4.0** (Pivotal/Commercial) | GLUC-2025-401 to 410 | Phase 3 / PPQ | GHS Commercial Site | 2000L Stainless Steel; Automated UF/DF; Integration of Google AI Process Control (GAIPC). |

---

### 3.0 DETAILED CHRONOLOGY OF PROCESS MODIFICATIONS

#### 3.1 Generation 1.0 to 2.0 Transition: Cell Line Stabilization
**Change ID:** CHG-GLUC-001  
**Scope:** Cell Line and Expression System  
**Description:** The initial material was produced using transient transfection in HEK293 cells. For Phase 1, GHS developed the GHS-CHO-001 cell line (GS-knockout).  
**Rationale:** To ensure long-term genetic stability and scalability required for human dosing and commercial viability.

**Technical Specifications (Gen 2.0):**
*   **Vector:** pGHS-GLUC-Exp4.2
*   **Selection Marker:** Glutamine Synthetase (GS)
*   **Seeding Density:** $0.5 \times 10^6$ cells/mL
*   **Harvest Titer Target:** $> 3.5$ g/L

#### 3.2 Generation 2.0 to 3.0 Transition: Extended-Release (XR) Conjugation Optimization
**Change ID:** CHG-GLUC-008  
**Scope:** Downstream Processing / Polymer Conjugation  
**Description:** In Gen 2.0, the conjugation of the glucapeptide to the extended-release PEG-based polymer was performed using a batch-wise addition. Gen 3.0 introduced a microfluidic mixing protocol (GHS-MF-01).

**Step-by-Step Conjugation Protocol (Gen 3.0):**
1.  **Buffer Exchange:** DS intermediate equilibrated into 50 mM Sodium Phosphate, pH 7.2.
2.  **Concentration:** Adjust protein concentration to $12.5 \text{ mg/mL} \pm 0.5 \text{ mg/mL}$ using UF/DF (30kDa MWCO).
3.  **Mixing:** Utilizing the GHS-MF-01 Microfluidic Reactor, the activated polymer (20kDa Linear) is introduced at a molar ratio of 1.2:1 (Polymer:Protein).
4.  **Reaction Parameters:** Temperature $4^\circ\text{C} \pm 1^\circ\text{C}$; Residence time 120 seconds.
5.  **Quenching:** 1M Glycine addition to terminate the reaction.

---

### 4.0 COMPARABILITY ASSESSMENT DATA
To support the transition between Gen 3.0 (Phase 2) and Gen 4.0 (Phase 3/Commercial), a comprehensive comparability study was performed under Protocol **PRT-GLUC-400**.

#### 4.1 Analytical Comparability (Primary Structure & Purity)
Batch comparison data for representative batches GLUC-2024-210 (Gen 3.0) and GLUC-2025-401 (Gen 4.0).

#### Table 2.6-2: Comparison of Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs)

| Attribute | Method | Specification | GLUC-2024-210 (Phase 2) | GLUC-2025-401 (Phase 3) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Intact Mass** | LC-MS | $42,345 \pm 5 \text{ Da}$ | 42,346 Da | 42,345 Da |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SE-HPLC | $\geq 98.0\%$ | 99.2% | 99.4% |
| **Conjugation Site** | Peptide Map | Asp-23 (>95%) | 97.4% | 98.1% |
| **Host Cell Protein** | ELISA | $\leq 100 \text{ ppm}$ | 14 ppm | 8 ppm |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> | $\leq 0.5 \text{ EU/mg}$ | <0.05 EU/mg | <0.05 EU/mg |
| **In vitro Potency** | Cell-based | 80% - 125% | 102% | 105% |

#### 4.2 Statistical Analysis of Glycosylation Profiles
A critical change in Gen 4.0 involved the implementation of an automated glucose feeding strategy controlled by Google Cloud AI. The impact on N-glycan profiles (specifically G0F and G1F species) was analyzed using a T-test (alpha = 0.05).

**Calculated Values:**
*   **Mean G0F (Gen 3.0):** $42.3\% \pm 2.1\%$
*   **Mean G0F (Gen 4.0):** $41.8\% \pm 1.4\%$
*   **P-value:** 0.34 (No statistically significant difference)

---

### 5.0 DOWNSTREAM PROCESS (DSP) REFINEMENTS (GEN 3.0 TO 4.0)
Significant refinements were made to the purification train to improve viral clearance and reduce process-related impurities.

#### 5.1 Viral Clearance Protocol (Enhanced)
The viral filtration step was upgraded from the Planova 20N to the Pegasus Prime filter to accommodate higher flux rates at the 2000L scale.

**Validation Parameters (Study V-2025-GLUC):**
1.  **Spike Virus:** Xenotropic murine leukemia virus (XMuLV) and Minute virus of mice (MVM).
2.  **Load Ratio:** $200 \text{ L/m}^2$.
3.  **LRV Target:** $> 4.0 \log_{10}$ for XMuLV.
4.  **Actual Result (GLUC-2025-401):** $5.82 \log_{10}$ (XMuLV).

#### 5.2 Chromatography Resin Life-Cycle Studies
For Gen 4.0, Resin Life-Cycle studies (USP <1132>) were conducted to ensure the Protein A (MabSelect Sure LX) maintained binding capacity over 50 cycles.
*   **Static Binding Capacity (SBC):** 65 mg/mL (Initial) vs 62 mg/mL (Cycle 50).
*   **Yield Recovery:** 94% (Cycle 1) vs 92.5% (Cycle 50).

---

### 6.0 REGULATORY JUSTIFICATION FOR CHANGES
All manufacturing changes implemented during the development of Glucogen-XR were evaluated according to **ICH Q5E: Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products**.

1.  **Risk Assessment:** A Failure Mode and Effects Analysis (FMEA) was conducted for each change. All "High Risk" items (e.g., Change in XR-linkage chemistry) were mitigated through side-by-side analytical characterization and forced degradation studies.
2.  **Stability:** Stability data for Gen 4.0 batches (GLUC-2025-401 through 403) are currently at the 12-month time point under $5^\circ\text{C}$ storage, demonstrating equivalence to the Gen 3.0 clinical stability profile.
3.  **Bioequivalence:** For the Gen 3.0 to Gen 4.0 transition, a bridging PK study (GHS-GLUC-PK-102) in healthy volunteers was performed, confirming that the $C_{\max}$ and $AUC_{0-\infty}$ remained within the 80-125% equivalence interval.

---

### 7.0 APPENDICES AND REFERENCES
*   **Ref 1:** ICH Q11 Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances.
*   **Ref 2:** USP <121> Insulin Assays (modified for GLP-1 analogues).
*   **Ref 3:** Google Health Sciences Standard Operating Procedure SOP-PRO-0098: "Change Control for Biologics."
*   **Batch Record Location:** GHS-Cloud-Vault / Manufacturing / Glucogen-XR / BMR / 2025 / GLUC-2025-401.pdf

# Nomenclature and Regulatory Designations

## USAN and INN Applications

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S: DRUG SUBSTANCE (GLUCAPEPTIDE)
### 3.2.S.1 GENERAL INFORMATION
#### 3.2.S.1.1 NOMENCLATURE AND REGULATORY DESIGNATIONS

---

### SUBSECTION: USAN AND INN APPLICATIONS

#### 1.0 Executive Summary of Nomenclature Strategy
The nomenclature strategy for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** was initiated in the early stages of Phase 2 clinical development to ensure global harmonization of the nonproprietary name across key regulatory jurisdictions, specifically the United States (via the USAN Council) and the international community (via the World Health Organization [WHO] INN Programme). 

Google Health Sciences (GHS), a division of Google Cloud Life Sciences, has pursued a naming convention that accurately reflects the pharmacological class (GLP-1 receptor agonist), the structural modifications (site-specific pegylation and amino acid substitutions), and the extended-release profile of the drug substance.

#### 2.0 United States Adopted Name (USAN) Application
The USAN application for glucapeptide was submitted to the USAN Council (managed by the American Medical Association [AMA]) in accordance with the "USP Dictionary of USAN and International Drug Names" guidelines.

##### 2.1 Application Chronology and Submission Details
The following table summarizes the formal interactions with the USAN Council regarding the designation of "glucapeptide."

| Submission ID | Date of Submission | Document Type | Action/Status | Primary Contact |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| USAN-2023-GHS-01 | 14-JAN-2023 | Initial Application | Received | Dr. A. V. Thompson |
| USAN-2023-GHS-01-R1 | 22-MAR-2023 | Response to Query | Structural Clarification | Dr. A. V. Thompson |
| USAN-2023-GHS-02 | 15-JUN-2023 | Balloting Phase | Preliminary Approval | USAN Council |
| **USAN-FINAL-992** | **10-OCT-2023** | **Final Adoption** | **Adopted** | **Google Health Sciences** |

##### 2.2 USAN Structural Rationale and Criteria
The name "glucapeptide" was selected based on the following USAN Council Stem requirements:
1.  **Prefix:** "Gluca-" relates to the glucagon-like peptide origin.
2.  **Stem:** "-peptide" (Class: Synthetic peptides; non-vaccine).
3.  **Qualifier:** While "extended-release" is a dosage form descriptor, the USAN Council recognized the unique covalent 40kDa PEG-linkage as part of the molecular identity, necessitating a specific chemical description in the USAN Statement of Adoption.

##### 2.3 Detailed USAN Chemical Description
As per USAN Council requirements, the following chemical description was provided in the application (USAN File No. 23-104):
*   **Chemical Name (IUPAC):** $N^{6,26}-\{[(2RS)-2,3-bis(\text{polyoxyethylene})propyl]carbamoyl\}-L-lysyl^{26}, [Aib^8, Arg^{34}]GLP-1(7-37)$
*   **Molecular Formula:** $C_{172}H_{265}N_{43}O_{51} \cdot (C_2H_4O)_n$
*   **Molecular Weight:** ~4,100 Da (peptide core) + ~40,000 Da (PEG moiety) = ~44.1 kDa total.

#### 3.0 International Nonproprietary Name (INN) Application
The INN application was filed with the World Health Organization (WHO) in Geneva to ensure global consistency in prescribing and safety monitoring.

##### 3.1 WHO INN Programme Submission Data
The application followed the "Procedure for the Selection of Recommended International Nonproprietary Names for Pharmaceutical Substances."

| WHO Request No. | List Number | Publication Date | Status |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 112-P-2023 | Proposed INN List 129 | 15-AUG-2023 | Published for Comment |
| 112-R-2024 | Recommended INN List 91 | 20-FEB-2024 | Final Publication |

##### 3.2 Linguistic Analysis and Conflicts
As part of the INN application, GHS conducted a linguistic search in the six official WHO languages (Arabic, Chinese, English, French, Russian, and Spanish) to ensure the name "glucapeptide" did not have unintended meanings or phonetic similarities to existing drugs.

| Language | Potential Conflict | Search Result | GHS Disposition |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| Spanish | Glucagon | Distinct suffix | No Confusion |
| French | Glucide | Broad category | No Confusion |
| Russian | Глюкапептид | Phonetic match | Acceptable |

#### 4.0 Comparative Analysis of USAN and INN Requirements
The following table provides a side-by-side comparison of the data provided to the USAN and WHO committees for the characterization of Glucogen-XR.

| Feature | USAN Requirement | WHO INN Requirement |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Primary Identity** | 7-37 GLP-1 Analog | Glucagon-like peptide-1 agonist |
| **Structural Formula** | Required (Detailed) | Required (Graphic) |
| **CAS Registry No.** | Required (2841202-XX-X) | Required |
| **Pharmacology** | GLP-1 Receptor Agonist | Antidiabetic |
| **Salt Form** | Acetate (implied) | Base Name Only |

#### 5.0 Batch Correspondence and Traceability
The characterization data supporting the USAN/INN applications were derived from the following pivotal batches manufactured at the South San Francisco facility.

| Batch Number | Scale | Date of Manufacture | Purpose | USAN/INN Alignment |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| GLUC-2025-001 | 50L | 12-JAN-2025 | Proof of Concept | Pre-filing ID |
| GLUC-2025-002 | 200L | 15-FEB-2025 | Characterization | Structural Verification |
| GLUC-2025-003 | 500L | 10-MAR-2025 | GMP Clinical | Final Nomenclature Validation |

#### 6.0 Protocol for Maintenance of Nomenclature Records
GHS maintains a rigorous internal protocol (SOP-RA-NOM-001) for managing nonproprietary name records.

##### 6.1 Step-by-Step Procedure for Regulatory Updates
1.  **Trigger:** Any modification to the primary sequence or conjugation site of glucapeptide.
2.  **Assessment:** Regulatory Affairs evaluates if the change requires a "New USAN" or a "Modified USAN."
3.  **Calculation:** If PEG density changes by >10% ($\Delta MW > 4kDa$), a new CAS number and USAN addendum are required.
    *   *Formula:* $PD = \frac{MW_{total} - MW_{peptide}}{MW_{peptide}}$
    *   *Threshold:* $\Delta PD > 0.10$ triggers re-application.
4.  **Submission:** Filing of Form 1.1 to USAN Council within 30 days of manufacturing change approval.

#### 7.0 Conclusion
The designation of "glucapeptide" as the USAN and INN for the active ingredient in Glucogen-XR provides a robust framework for global regulatory consistency. All applications have been finalized, and the name is now utilized in all Module 1 (Administrative Information) and Module 2 (Summaries) documentation for the current NDA/BLA submission.

#### 8.0 References
1.  **USP Dictionary** of USAN and International Drug Names (2024 Edition).
2.  **WHO Technical Report Series**, No. 961, Annex 4 (INN Guidelines).
3.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
4.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Contents of a Complete Submission for the Evaluation of Proprietary Names.

---
**END OF SUBSECTION**
